401 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Cutter v. Classic Fire & Marine Ins. Co.


No. 49A05-0906-CV-315


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


926 N.E.2d 1067; 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 759



May 5, 2010, Decided 
May 5, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Louis Rosenberg, Judge. Cause No. 49C01-9712-CP-2827.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marion Circuit Court, Indiana, found that appellant claimants were not entitled to payment from respondent insurer's liquidation estate and dismissed the claim. The claimants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the claimants could not recover twice on the same judgments, and therefore it would reduce the amount of any award on the claim by the amount the claimants recovered on their Alaska judgments from the tortfeasor's bankruptcy estate. The appellate court noted that the claimants' claim against the tortfeasor and the tortfeasor's claim against the insurer were not based on the same cause of action. Because the claimants' claim was completely distinct from the tortfeasor's claim, a distribution from the insurer's liquidation estate on the disputed claim to the tortfeasor's assignee did not implicate the prohibition against double recovery. Based on cases from other jurisdictions and a plain reading of Ind. Code § 27-9-3-34(d), in the insurer's liquidation proceedings, the Alaska judgments were not conclusive evidence of liability or the measure of damages. The owner of the disputed claim had to prove both liability and the measure of damages in the insurer's liquidation proceedings. The Alaska judgments were not conclusive as to the value of the disputed claim in the insurer's liquidation proceedings and this did not render § 27-9-3-34(d) unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded as to the finding that the claimants' claim and tortfeasor's claim were the same; the judgment was affirmed in all other respects.


 

402 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Bellows v. Bd. of Comm'rs of Elkhart


No. 20A03-0909-CV-412


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


926 N.E.2d 96; 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 747



April 30, 2010, Decided 
April 30, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Terry C. Shewmaker, Judge. Cause No. 20C01-0810-PL-75.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment of the Elkhart Circuit Court (Indiana) dismissing their three-count petition for writ of certiorari under Ind. Code § 36-7-4-1003(a) and complaint for declaratory judgment against appellees, the Board of Commissioners of the County of Elkhart (Board) and the Plan Commission of Elkhart County (Commission). The owners took issue with a Board vote to approve a zoning map change (the ordinance).


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not err in determining that, as a stand-alone allegation, Count I failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, Ind. R. Trial P. 12(B)(6). Count I only set forth general allegations which were expressly incorporated by reference into Counts II and III. Count II sought a writ of certiorari for the trial court to review the ordinance. Count II was properly dismissed pursuant to Ind. R. Trial P. 12(B)(1) for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The plain language of § 36-7-4-1003(a) did not include either the Board or the Commission, the only two defendants named in the complaint. Thus, judicial review by writ of certiorari of a decision of the Board or a recommendation of the Commission was not cognizable. Count III sought a declaratory judgment on the question of whether the ordinance was illegal. The court agreed that the property owners lacked standing to seek declaratory relief. After appellees made a prima facie showing that no genuine issue of material fact existed on the question of the property owners' alleged pecuniary injuries, the owners did not meet their burden. They did not submit any evidence demonstrating a pecuniary loss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.


 

403 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Blakemore v. State


No. 49A02-0907-CR-614


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


925 N.E.2d 759; 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 633



April 16, 2010, Decided 
April 16, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Marie Kern, Commissioner. Cause No. 49F24-0711-FD-233526.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Marion Superior Court, Indiana, convicting him for failure to register as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: In 1999, defendant agreed to plead guilty to sexual misconduct with a minor as a Class C felony. The plea agreement provided defendant would comply with the statutory requirements of registering with local law enforcement as a sex offender. However, at that time there was no statutory registration requirement for persons who committed defendant's offense of sexual misconduct with a minor as a Class C felony. In 2001, Ind. Code § 11-8-8-4.5 added a registration requirement for persons convicted of defendant's underlying offense. After being discharged from probation, defendant was arrested for failure to register as a sex offender. That retroactive application of the sex offender registry requirement violated the Indiana constitutional prohibition of ex post facto laws. The Court of Appeals of Indiana declined the State's invitation to enlarge defendant's plea agreement by requiring him to predict changes in the law and to comply with such changes.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

404 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Wrigley


No. 33A04-0912-CV-727


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


925 N.E.2d 747; 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 624



April 14, 2010, Decided 
April 14, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Smith v. Wrigley, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 946 (Ind., Aug. 27, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HENRY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael D. Peyton, Judge. Cause No. 33D01-0911-PL-27.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a motion for waiver of fees required under Ind. Code § 34-10-1-3 to file a civil complaint against certain prison officials. The Henry Superior Court (Indiana) denied the motion and ordered the clerk not to process the inmate's cause until he paid the appropriate costs in full. The inmate's complaint was subsequently dismissed. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that Ind. Code § 34-10-1-3, prohibiting an inmate who has filed three or more frivolous lawsuits from filing in forma pauperis, violated the Privileges and Immunities clause of Indiana's Constitution, Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. He claimed the statute discriminated against incarcerated plaintiffs because it did not impose fees on non-incarcerated plaintiffs who have filed three or more frivolous complaints and that the disparate treatment was not reasonably related to inherent characteristics distinguishing the classes. The court of appeals disagreed. The court noted that incarcerated plaintiffs were inherently distinct because of the withdrawal or limitation of rights associated with incarceration. The court of appeals also noted the courts have been inundated with civil actions filed by incarcerated plaintiffs, many of which were frivolous and that the inmate had filed about 50 lawsuits, many of which were frivolous. The court of appeals found that the State had a legitimate interest in preserving judicial and administrative resources and that the filing fee statute did not deny the inmate access to court; it merely conditioned access on payment of a filing fee.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

405 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



L.D. v. Jo.D.


No. 49A02-0907-CV-671


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


921 N.E.2d 867; 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 277



February 25, 2010, Decided 
February 25, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by L.D. v. J.D., 929 N.E.2d 797, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 503 (Ind., 2010)
Superseded by, Remanded by L.D.A.B. v. Jo.D., 2010 Ind. LEXIS 799 (Ind., Dec. 16, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Cynthia J. Ayers, Judge. Cause No. 49D04-0708-AD-35277.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee paternal grandparents filed two petitions to adopt their grandchild. Their second adoption petition was granted. Appellants, the child's biological mother and the child's adoptive maternal grandmother, filed a motion to set aside the adoption decree pursuant to Ind. R. Trial P. 60(B)(4). The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied the motion. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother gave birth to the child while she was incarcerated. The mother's co-worker became the child's guardian and later adopted the mother as an adult, becoming the child's adoptive maternal grandparent. The paternal grandparents alleged that the mother's consent to the adoption was not necessary due to her abandonment of the child and averred that they could not locate her. Pursuant to Ind. Code § 31-19-4.5-2, they gave notice of the adoption petition to the mother by publication in a newspaper. No notice was given to the maternal grandmother. On appeal, the court held that it could not review the issue of the mother's consent because the propriety of the adoption decree was not before the court. Further, the mother failed to show that service of process by publication was inadequate. Finally, a grandparent did not have a liberty interest in visitation with her grandchild. Thus, the maternal grandmother did not show that her due process rights were violated by the adoption statute's failure to require that grandparents receive notice of the adoption proceeding. She also did not show that she was entitled to visitation after the adoption under the Grandparent Visitation Act.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the mother's appeal as to the issue of consent. The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the motion to set aside the adoption decree.

407 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Terry v. Stephens


No. 54A01-0908-CV-419


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


921 N.E.2d 516; 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 189



February 17, 2010, Decided 
February 17, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Terry v. Stephens, 929 N.E.2d 797, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 577 (Ind., 2010)
Transfer denied by Terry v. Stephens, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 753 (Ind., June 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MONTGOMERY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Peggy Q. Lohorn, Judge. Cause No. 54D02-0708-CT-129.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death action, plaintiffs, the children of a decedent, challenged summary judgment entered by the Montgomery Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of defendant nurse, arguing that the children of a parent who provided love, care, and affection but no financial or non-financial support should nevertheless be considered dependent children under the Wrongful Death Act, Ind. Code § 34-23-1-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Prior to his demise, the decedent was mentally ill to the extent that he could not support himself or anyone else. In the last six years of his life, he was homeless and had no contact with his children. While incarcerated in a county jail, he hanged himself and died of asphyxiation. His children filed suit against the nurse, alleging that his medical malpractice proximately resulted in the decedent's death by suicide. On review of summary judgment entered in favor of the nurse, the court held that, to prevail under the Wrongful Death Act, Ind. Code § 34-23-1-1 et seq., decedent's children were required to prove that they needed his support and actually received it. They failed to do so because the evidence established that the decedent was never capable of providing financial support or nonpecuniary services to his children. While he may have provided emotional support--a difficult task, given that he was prohibited from having contact with them--emotional support alone was insufficient to establish dependency. The touchstone of the Wrongful Death Act was pecuniary loss, and the children failed to establish any.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of the nurse was affirmed.


 

408 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Morris v. State


No. 02A03-0905-CR-210


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


921 N.E.2d 40; 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 161



February 9, 2010, Decided 
February 9, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Morris v. State, 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 696 (Ind. Ct. App., Apr. 14, 2010)
Transfer denied by Morris v. State, 929 N.E.2d 797, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 511 (Ind., 2010)
Transfer denied by Morris v. State, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 745 (Ind., June 24, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Dismissed without prejudice by Morris v. Superintendent, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 98448 (N.D. Ind., Sept. 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth R. Scheibenberger, Judge. Cause No. 02D04-0901-FD-23.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Indiana charged defendant with class D felony theft in violation of Ind. Code § 35-43-4-2 and filed an information alleging that he was a habitual offender. At his jury trial, defendant requested an instruction describing criminal conversion under Ind. Code § 35-43-4-3 as a lesser included offense of theft. The Allen Superior Court (Indiana) denied the request. The jury found defendant guilty as charged. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A loss prevention supervisor at a department store saw defendant stuff numerous clothing items into a large black plastic trash bag on her surveillance video screen. Defendant had been apprehended for shoplifting from the same store 14 months earlier when he stuffed jeans into a trash bag and exited the store. This time, he dropped the bag when he saw the supervisor approaching him and exited without the clothing. On appeal, the court held that it was reversible error to refuse to give defendant's requested instruction describing criminal conversion as a lesser included offense of theft. If criminal conversion as a class A misdemeanor and theft as a class D felony were indeed two different crimes as outlined by Indiana's Legislature, then the trial court abused its discretion by failing to instruct the jury as to the lesser-included offense of conversion. If the elements of conversion and theft had no practical difference, then the rule of lenity and/or the Proportionality Clause contained in Ind. Const. art. 1, § 16 entitled defendant to have the jury instructed on both crimes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

409 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Bishop v. Hous. Auth. of S. Bend


No. 71A03-0906-CV-273


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


920 N.E.2d 772; 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 94



February 1, 2010, Decided 
February 1, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Bishop v. Hous. Auth. of S. Bend, 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 524 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 24, 2010)
Transfer denied by Bishop v. Hous. Auth. of S. Bend, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 1007 (Ind., July 30, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bishop v. Hous. Auth., 131 S. Ct. 1022, 178 L. Ed. 2d 846, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 865 (U.S., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Margot F. Reagan, Judge. Cause No. 71D04-0811-PL-282.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenant appealed the judgment of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) that granted appellee, the Housing Authority of South Bend (HASB), prejudgment possession of the apartment unit the tenant had leased from HASB.


OVERVIEW: The tenant argued, inter alia, that the trial court committed reversible error when it refused to order that the son be transported from prison to testify at the immediate possession hearing. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court heard testimony "that at the time of the robbery in July 2008, the son maintained a separate household with his pregnant girlfriend." However, even if the son had moved from the tenant's unit in late February of 2008, the terms of the lease clearly provided that until the tenant provided written notice to HASB of that fact, he was considered to be a resident of the unit. Hence, evidence at the hearing of the son's absence was not relevant to controverting the claim that the tenant had breached the terms of her lease. As to any involvement by the tenant and the son's siblings in his July 2008 crime, neither the lease nor any regulation to which the tenant pointed provide that their non-involvement was the dispositive issue as to whether she should remain a tenant. Moreover, the trial court had evidence of admissions by the son that directly connected his presence in the tenant's unit with the crime he committed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

410 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


No. 02A03-0908-CR-363


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


924 N.E.2d 121; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 3055



December 31, 2009, Decided 
December 31, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published February 24, 2010.
Transfer denied by Williams v. State, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 611 (Ind., Sept. 20, 2010)
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Motion to strike granted by, in part, Motion to strike denied by, in part, Summary judgment granted by, Summary judgment denied by, Judgment entered by Williams v. York, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 106934 (N.D. Ind., Oct. 4, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John F. Surbeck, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 02D04-0804-FD-288.
Williams v. State, 919 N.E.2d 618, 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 2998 (Ind. Ct. App., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Allen Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of strangulation in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-2-9(b), and battery in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1(a)(2)(M), each as Class D felonies. The jury also found that defendant was an habitual offender. The trial court denied defendant's motion to correct error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with the victim and her two children, and the couple engaged in sexual intercourse. The victim called 9-1-1 twice after defendant refused to leave her home and then angrily choked her and beat her at length. Her children observed part of the attack. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not deprive defendant of his right to counsel in determining that he knowingly, willingly, and voluntarily exercised his right to self-representation. Defendant was clearly warned of the dangers of representing himself and the advantages of having an attorney. Further, it was harmless error to deny defendant's motion for separation of witnesses under Ind. R. Evid. 615 because there was no prejudice. In addition, Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1(a)(2)(M) was not void for vagueness as applied to defendant. The definition of a "family or household member" under Ind. Code § 35-41-1-10.6(a) as one who "is or was engaged in a sexual relationship with the other person" was sufficiently definite to inform ordinary people of the prohibited conduct and to avoid arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement of the statute. Finally, there was sufficient evidence supporting the battery conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

411 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



City of Indianapolis v. Armour


No. 49A02-0901-CV-84


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


918 N.E.2d 401; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 2669



December 18, 2009, Decided 
December 18, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by City of Indianapolis v. Armour, 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 244 (Ind. Ct. App., Feb. 17, 2010)
Transfer granted by, Vacated by City of Indianapolis v. Armour, 940 N.E.2d 821, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 873 (Ind., 2010)
Superseded by City of Indianapolis v. Armour, 2011 Ind. LEXIS 350 (Ind., May 10, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John F. Hanley, Judge. Cause No. 49D11-0706-CT-26050.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, 45 homeowners in a neighborhood, sued appellants, a city and its board of public works, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging in part that the board's resolution violated the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Constitution as applied to the homeowners. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granted the homeowners' request for summary judgment and denied the city's motion for summary judgment. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city assessed each property owner in the neighborhood for a sewer project under the Barrett Law. The 45 homeowners paid the full assessment, while 142 others paid in installments. The next year, the city passed an ordinance abandoning Barrett Law assessments, and the board passed a resolution forgiving future installment payments. The court held that the city's refusal to grant the homeowners' request for a partial refund of their assessments violated the Equal Protection Clause. It was the city's burden to demonstrate a plausible policy reason for its disparate treatment of the homeowners, but it failed to demonstrate a rational basis for the differential treatment. The city only offered attenuated justifications for its failure to treat the similarly situated homeowners with rough equality. It could not lawfully confer privileges upon property owners who paid in installments and, at the same time, impose liabilities upon those within the same class who paid in full. The resolution's only stated policy justification, which was to alleviate financial hardship on middle to lower-income property owners, bore no rational relation to the homeowners' equal protection claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment for the homeowners on their Equal Protection claim, and it affirmed the trial court's denial of the city's motion for summary judgment. The court also affirmed the money judgment entered by the trial court for the homeowners. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to determine the appropriate amount of prejudgment interest to which each homeowner was entitled.


 

412 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Greer v. Buss


No. 49A02-0903-CV-243


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


918 N.E.2d 607; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 2666



December 17, 2009, Decided 
December 17, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Patrick L. McCarty, Judge. Cause No. 49D03-0801-PL-2278.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two former registered sex offenders (registrants), filed a proposed class action lawsuit against defendants, state and local government officials and entities, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief with respect to the sex offender registration policy of the Indiana Department of Correction (DOC). The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) dismissed the action, granted summary judgment to the DOC, and denied class action certification.


OVERVIEW: Each registrant was required to register as a sex offender and received a letter informing him that the ten-year registration had expired. Based on the DOC's interpretation of Ind. Code § 11-8-8-19(a) in effect prior to July 1, 2008, each registrant was required to register again as a sex offender for a second ten-year period for his subsequent DUI offense. The court overturned the summary judgment for defendants. First, the registrants could seek declaratory relief because the burdens imposed by the Indiana Sex Offender Registration Act were such that a possible defense in response to criminal prosecution was not a full and complete remedy. Second, the DOC's interpretation of the statute violated the prohibition on ex post facto laws contained in Ind. Const. art. 1, § 24. It would impose burdens that had the effect of adding punishment beyond that which could have been imposed when their crimes were committed. Third, application of a residency restriction pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-42-4-11 likewise violated Indiana's constitutional prohibition on ex post facto laws. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied class action certification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendants on the registrants' claims that they were not required to register as sex offenders for a second ten-year period and on one registrant's claim that the residency restriction statute as applied violated his ex post facto rights under the Indiana Constitution. The court affirmed, however, as to the trial court's denial of class action certification.


 

413 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Rice v. State


No. 55A04-0902-CR-99


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


916 N.E.2d 296; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 2438



November 13, 2009, Decided 
November 13, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Rice v. State, 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 169 (Ind. Ct. App., Feb. 3, 2010)
Transfer denied by Rice v. State, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 329 (Ind., Apr. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MORGAN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Christopher Burnham, Judge. Cause No. 55D02-0807-FD-261.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an interlocutory order of the Morgan Superior Court (Indiana) that denied her motion to suppress evidence, arguing that the trial court abused its discretion in applying the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule and denying her motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested pursuant to a warrant on a charge of receiving stolen property. Her purse was searched incident to that arrest, and the police discovered drugs. Defendant was then charged with drug possession. After the receiving stolen property charge was dismissed on motion of the State, defendant moved to suppress the drug evidence, arguing that, because there was no probable cause to support the issuance of the arrest warrant, the drugs, as fruits of an illegal arrest, should be suppressed. On review, the court held that the trial court erred in denying defendant's suppression motion because the warrant for defendant's arrest was based upon an affidavit so lacking in indicia of probable cause as to render official believe in its existence entirely unreasonable. Therefore, the police conduct therefore fell outside of Indiana's good faith exception to the exclusionary rule under Ind. Code § 35-37-4-5, and evidence obtained as a result of the search incident to defendant's arrest had to be suppressed.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized as a result of her arrest was reversed.

 

414 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Lindsey v. State


No. 29A02-0902-CR-196


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


916 N.E.2d 230; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 2404



November 9, 2009, Decided 
November 9, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Lindsey v. State, 929 N.E.2d 783, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 71 (Ind., 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at Lindsey v. State, 2012 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1000 (Ind. Ct. App., Aug. 14, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Daniel J. Pfleging, Judge. Cause No. 29D03-0803-FB-35.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted him of robbery, theft, criminal confinement, and resisting law enforcement, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV and Ind. Const. art. 1, § 11.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant run into a store, brandish a weapon, and then run out of the store shortly thereafter. During pursuit, the officer assumed a position next to a vehicle; as defendant ran toward the vehicle, the officer emerged, identified himself, and ordered defendant to stop. Defendant turned ran. Because defendant had been running in the direction of the car, the driver's side door was open approximately six inches, and the windows were blacked out, the officer, concerned for his safety, opened the door wider to see if an accomplice was inside. On review, the court held that, under the circumstances, it was not unreasonable for the officer to believe that the car was defendant's getaway car and that an accomplice, possibly also armed, might be inside. Further, the officer's search ceased as soon as the exigency concern had dissipated, and nothing in the car was seized until a search warrant was obtained. As such, the exigent circumstance of officer safety justified the warrantless search, and defendant's suppression motion was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Howard v. Daugherty

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The LaPorte Superior Court, Indiana, dismissed appellant inmate's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 complaint for failure to pay filing fees. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued he paid the statutory filing fee, Ind. Code § 33-37-3-3, which was 22 cents, because he sent the court a 42-cent postage stamp. The appellate court found that the trial court was not obliged to accept the stamp as payment for the filing fee. United States coin and currency were legal tender for all debts, public charges, taxes, and dues, 31 U.S.C.S. § 5103.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

416 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Donovan v. Grand Vict. Casino & Resort, L.P.


No. 49A02-0903-CV-259


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


915 N.E.2d 1001; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 2332



October 30, 2009, Decided 
October 30, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Donovan v. Grand Victoria Casino & Resort, L.P., 929 N.E.2d 786, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 132 (Ind., 2010)
Affirmed in part and superseded in part by Donovan v. Grand Victoria Casino & Resort, L.P., 2010 Ind. LEXIS 559 (Ind., Sept. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robyn L. Moberly, Judge. Cause No. 49D05-0709-MI-39223.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff casino patron filed a breach of contract claim against defendant casino, and requested a declaratory judgment providing that he could not be excluded from blackjack for counting cards. The Marion Superior Court, Indiana, granted summary judgment to the casino on both counts. The patron appealed.


OVERVIEW: The casino patron taught himself to count cards. He and the blackjack pit boss for a casino had ostensibly agreed that he could play blackjack at the casino if he wagered no more than $ 25 per hand. When the patron was barred from the blackjack tables, he filed a complaint for breach of contract and sought declaratory relief. The trial court granted summary judgment to the casino. The Court of Appeals of Indiana held that the casino could not take refuge in the common law right of exclusion, because gambling was subject to strict regulation under Ind. Code § 4-33-1-2(2). The State Lottery Commission did not enact a prohibition against card counting, and the casino did not seek a prohibition by rule amendment. Therefore, the casino patron was entitled to summary judgment on his request for a declaratory judgment that the casino could not exclude him from blackjack because he counted cards. Summary judgment was properly granted for the casino on the patron's contract claim. The designated materials revealed a lack of mutuality of obligation.


OUTCOME: The portion of the trial court's order granting summary judgment to the casino on the patron's breach of contract claim was affirmed; the portion of the order denying the patron's motion for summary judgment on the claim for declaratory relief was reversed.

 

417 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Liberty Landowners Ass'n v. Porter County Comm'rs


No. 64A03-0905-CV-213


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


913 N.E.2d 1245; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 2038



September 29, 2009, Decided 
September 29, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Liberty Landowners Assoc. v. Porter City Comm'rs, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 49 (Ind., Jan. 14, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable A. James Sarkisian, Judge Pro Tem. Cause No. 64D05-0803-PL-2433.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Porter Superior Court, Indiana, dismissed appellant landowner associations's (association) complaint for declaratory judgment that it filed against appellees, Porter County Commissioners (Commissioners) regarding the decision to rezone certain real property in Porter County, which permitted appellee health care company to construct a hospital on the property. The association appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association argued that the trial court erred in concluding that it lacked standing to proceed with the action. The appellate court noted that it had consistently held that landowner associations lacked standing to challenge zoning decisions. It was apparent that the association sought to have the trial court reverse established precedent that landowner associations owning no real estate were without standing to challenge zoning decisions. Thus, the association had waived the issue. The association had no legal right--personal or pecuniary--that had been put in jeopardy by the Commissioners' decision. The association has not alleged any direct harm and had not been denied any rights. As a result, the association's claims failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

418 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



League of Women Voters of Ind., Inc. v. Rokita


No. 49A02-0901-CV-40


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


915 N.E.2d 151; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1628



September 17, 2009, Decided 
September 17, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by League of Women Voters v. Rokita, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 85 (Ind., Jan. 25, 2010)
Superseded by League of Women Voters of Ind., Inc. v. Rokita, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 412 (Ind., June 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM 13. The Honorable S.K. Reid, Judge. Cause No. 49D13-0806-PL-27627.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the League of Women Voters of Indiana and the League of Women Voters of Indianapolis, challenged the dismissal of their declaratory judgment action by the Marion Superior Court, Civil Division (Indiana), in which they sought a judicial declaration that the Indian Voter I.D. Law violated the Indiana Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana Legislature passed Ind. Code §§ 3-10-1-7.2(e), 3-11-8-25.1, and 3-11-10-1.2, which required citizens voting in person to present government-issued photo identification but excepted from the identification requirement persons voting via absentee ballot or those residing at a state licensed care facility where a precinct polling place was located. On review of the superior court ruling, the court held that the Voter I.D. Law violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23, through its disparate treatment between mail-in absentee voters and in-person voters because it was irrational for the legislature to require identification of in-person voters but not to require an affidavit affirming the identity of mail-in voters. Further, the class created by Ind. Code §§ 3-10-1-7.2 and 3-11-8-25.1 was based in part upon an arbitrary characteristic that granted an unequal privilege to residents of state licensed care facilities that also happened to be polling places. The privilege granted was unnecessary when those persons already had an opportunity to vote absentee without showing identification. Therefore, Ind. Code §§ 3-10-1-7.2 and 3-11-8-25.1 violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court was reversed, and the case was remanded with instructions to the superior court to declare the Voter I.D. law void.

Slone v. State


No. 57A03-0904-CR-162


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


912 N.E.2d 875; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1480



September 9, 2009, Decided 
September 9, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Slone v. State, 919 N.E.2d 559, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1606 (Ind., Dec. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NOBLE SUPERIOR COURT, DIVISION 2. The Honorable Michael J. Kramer, Judge. Cause Nos. 57D03-0709-CM-961 & 57D02-0803-CM-329.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Noble Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted her of purchasing drugs containing more than three grams of ephedrine, pseudoephedrine, or both within one week in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-14.7(d) and (i), arguing that the evidence was insufficient to show that she knowingly or intentionally purchased contraband.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the evidence presented by the State was insufficient to establish that defendant knowingly or intentionally purchased drugs containing three grams or more of ephedrine, pseudoephedrine, or both. The evidence proved only that defendant bought two 20-count packages of pseudoephedrine within one week during cold season and presented no evidence to prove that defendant was aware of the high probability that two packages of drugs contained more than three grams of pseudoephedrine. Further, the State did not enter into evidence either of the packages of drugs that defendant purchased, so the court was unable to review what information regarding the contents of those drugs was contained on the packaging. While the trial court took judicial notice of Food and Drug Administration regulations providing that active ingredients be listed per dosage units and gave examples in metric units, the State failed to prove establish that defendant was capable of converting the metric dosages into grams. As such, the State failed to meet its burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed.

 

420 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Tooley v. State


No. 49A04-0902-CR-62


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


911 N.E.2d 721; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1223



August 21, 2009, Decided 
August 21, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Tooley v. State, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1425 (Ind., Nov. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William J. Nelson, Judge. Cause No. 49F07-0806-CM-147543.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted him of cruelty to an animal in violation of Ind. Code § 35-46-3-12(b), arguing that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the statue was not void for vagueness. One "beat" an animal when he unnecessarily or cruelly struck an animal and caused the animal to suffer severe pain or injury. Unnecessarily meant needlessly, and cruelly meant to cause suffering. These straightforward definitions were sufficient to inform a person of ordinary intelligent of the proscribed conduct. As such, the statute was not vague on its face or applied to defendant, who kicked a cat. Further, the court rejected the argument that the evidence was insufficient because the cat was not examined by anyone qualified to determine if he was in pain or injured. The record reflected that defendant, while wearing steel-toed boots, drop kicked the cat with such force that the cat was sent flying, the cat made unhappy sounds, and the cat did not want to be picked up by the people who came to his rescue. The cat did not have to be examined by a veterinarian; the factfinder could infer from the evidence that the cat suffered severe pain.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

421 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Price v. State


No. 49A04-0812-CR-698


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


911 N.E.2d 716; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1225



August 21, 2009, Decided 
August 21, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Price v. State, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1445 (Ind., Nov. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William J. Nelson, Judge. Cause No. 49F07-0807-CM-178427.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted him of cruelty to an animal in violation of Ind. Code § 35-46-3-12(b), arguing that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The evidence, including defendant's admission, established that defendant grabbed his dog by the back of the neck to immobilize him and then repeatedly struck the dog with a belt in the face and stomach as the dog cowered in the corner. Each time defendant struck the dog, his screams could be heard outside. Under these circumstances, the court concluded that a person of ordinary intelligence would be aware that these actions violated Ind. Code § 35-46-3-12(b), which prohibited beating a vertebrate animal. Furthermore, a person of ordinary intelligence would know that such actions were not reasonable acts of discipline or training, which were exempt from the purview of the statue. As such, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. Further, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of cruelty to an animal because he grabbed his dog by the back of the neck and struck him multiple times with a belt and with enough force to make the dog scream loudly every time he was struck.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

422 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Collins v. State


No. 35A02-0902-CR-162


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


911 N.E.2d 700; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1231



August 21, 2009, Decided 
August 21, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Collins v. State, 919 N.E.2d 559, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1618 (Ind., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HUNTINGTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas M. Hakes, Judge. Cause No. 35C01-9906-CF-27.
Collins v. State, 740 N.E.2d 143, 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2037 (Ind. Ct. App., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Huntington Circuit Court (Indiana) that altered the terms of his probation, arguing that the trial court abused its discretion in altering the conditions of his probation and that the new conditions were impermissibly vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to raping a 17-year-old girl and was given terms of incarceration and probation. Shortly before his release from prison, the State moved to add sex offender conditions to defendant's probation. On review of the trial court order, the court held that, under Ind. Code § 35-38-2-1, the trial court had discretion to alter the terms of defendant's probation at any time, even though defendant was not accused of violating the terms of his probation. However, certain conditions were impermissibly vague. The requirement that defendant notify his probation officer of any "dating" relationship was impermissibly vague because it failed to define the conduct that constituted dating. Likewise, the requirement that defendant refrain from engaging in activities that could be construed as enticing children was impermissibly vague because prohibited conduct could include innocuous activities. In addition, requiring defendant to report to his probation officer any incidental contact with persons under the age of 18 was impermissibly vague considering that any number of slight encounters in public could trigger the reporting requirement.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed in part, but the case was remanded with instructions to clarify the sex offender conditions of probation with greater specificity.

 

423 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. State


No. 49A02-0808-CR-757


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


911 N.E.2d 76; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1059



August 12, 2009, Decided 
August 12, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Lewis v. State, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1586 (Ind., Oct. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Barbara Collins, Judge. Cause Nos. 49F08-0712-FD-280888, 49F08-0610-FD-207800, 49F08-0702-FD-023947, 49F08-0705-FD-095186.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate actions, defendants challenged, on due process and equal protection grounds, the State's refusal to waive a jury trial. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied defendants' petitions to transfer their cases; defendants' interlocutory appeals from this decision were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: In Marion County, Class D felony cases involving persons who, like defendants, had mental health problems were often transferred to Court 8. The State's refusal to waive jury trials in defendants' cases precluded such transfers. The appellate court held the State's alleged policy did not violate defendants' right to effective assistance of counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI. The negative public perception of mental illness did not mean defendants could not receive a fair trial by jury. As there was no showing that the State's policy related to defendants' mental illness, and as this policy was rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose--to seek their convictions--there was no violation of the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. As there was a reasonable relationship between their offense and court assignment and the State's policy (they were charged with serious crimes in a court where the State lacked success in obtaining convictions in bench trials), and as the policy applied to all defendants accused of Class D felonies in Court 8, their was no violation of the Privileges and Immunities Clause, Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Moore


No. 29A02-0811-CR-1039


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


909 N.E.2d 1053; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 978



July 22, 2009, Decided 
July 22, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Moore, 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 5 (Ind. Ct. App., Jan. 5, 2010)
Transfer denied by State v. Moore, 2010 Ind. LEXIS 324 (Ind., Apr. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Judith S. Proffitt, Judge. Cause No. 29C01-0506-FA-112.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee inmate filed a motion for restoration of credit time classification and Department of Correction (DOC) privileges. Appellant DOC challenged a judgment of the Hamilton Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted the motion and ordered it to restore defendant's classification. The inmate challenged the trial court's decision to grant DOC's motion to correct error after the forty-five days required by Ind. R. Trial P. 53.3.


OVERVIEW: DOC argued that the trial court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to review and rule on the inmate's motion because such review required it to pass judgment on the propriety of DOC's disciplinary actions. The court of appeals held that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction to review the deprivation of the inmate's credit time after such deprivation occurred pursuant to his claim of his Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination. The gravamen of the inmate's claim was based on the constitutionality of certain requirements of DOC's Sex Offender Management and Monitory Treatment Plan program. DOC could violate a prisoner's constitutional right against self-incrimination. DOC could appeal from the trial court's belated grant of its motion to correct error. However, because the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction, it erroneously granted DOC's motion, which was premised on the trial court's alleged lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Therefore, the trial court's original order granting the inmate's motion had to stand. DOC was not denied due process. It received notice in sufficient time to intervene and be heard.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals remanded the case with directions that the trial court vacate its grant of the motion to correct error and reinstate its original order in favor of the inmate.

Stoffel v. Daniels


No. 35A05-0902-CV-87


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


908 N.E.2d 1260; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 955



July 13, 2009, Decided 
July 13, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HUNTINGTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable James R. Heuer, Special Judge. Cause No. 35C01-0806-PL-349.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a township assessor, individually and on behalf of a class of township assessors, appealed the judgment of the Huntington Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed her complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants, the Indiana Governor, the State Commissioner, the Indiana Department of Local Government and Finance, and a county.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's suit sought a declaration that various public acts that directed county assessors to take over the duties of the township assessors were unconstitutional. Plaintiff also asserted a claim for contractual tortious interference and sought a preliminary injunction. The court held that since the office of a township assessor was provided for in Ind. Const. art. 6, § 3, its existence necessarily entailed statutory action by the Indiana Legislature. Therefore, the Indiana General Assembly had the authority to curtail the duties, powers, and obligations of an elected township assessor, even during the middle of his or her elected term, and transfer those duties, powers, and obligations to the county assessor. The court likewise upheld the dismissal of plaintiff's tortious interference claims since with regard to a public office, there was no contractual relationship or obligation that could be interfered with since the duties of a public officer are statutorily prescribed. The court did find that standing on the part of defendants existed and that plaintiff had properly brought initiated the declaratory judgment action against them.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court with regard to its decision that plaintiff improperly brought a declaratory judgment action against defendants but, otherwise, affirmed the judgment.

In re Adoption Of: J.L.S.


No. 45A03-0811-CV-572


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


908 N.E.2d 1245; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 954



July 13, 2009, Decided 
July 13, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Mary Beth Bonaventura, Senior Judge. The Honorable Katherine Garza, Referee. Cause No. 45D06-0804-AD-000111.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prospective parents petitioned to adopt a child. Appellant guardian ad litem (GAL) reported that the adoption was in the child's best interests. The Lake Superior Court (Indiana) found, however, that one of the prospective parents had been convicted in Illinois of aggravated battery, and, pursuant to Ind. Code § 31-19-11-1(c), denied the petition. The GAL appealed.


OVERVIEW: The GAL argued that § 31-19-11-1(c) was unconstitutional as applied to the child. The appellate court found, however, that the entries from the Illinois case at issue did not reflect that judgment of conviction was entered or sentence was imposed for the counts charging aggravated battery or armed violence. Although the jury found the prospective parent guilty to aggravated battery, the Illinois trial court "merged" that into attempted murder. Pursuant to Illinois law, because this offense was merged into a greater offense, the offense was vacated. Because the record showed that there were no judgments of conviction entered against the prospective parent except for attempted murder and he was only sentenced for that charge, he was only "convicted" of attempted murder. Attempted murder was not one of the offenses listed in § 31-19-11-1(c). The crime of attempted murder did not appear to impede the adoption petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for the trial court to determine whether adoption was still in the best interests of the child and whether the prospective parents were of sufficient ability to rear the child and furnish suitable support and education.

Ben-Yisrayl v. State


No. 49A02-0806-CR-512


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


908 N.E.2d 1223; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 949



July 10, 2009, Decided 
July 10, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Davis v. State, 919 N.E.2d 554, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1334 (Ind., 2009)
Appeal after remand at Ben-Yisrayl v. State, 2010 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1744 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 14, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Sheila A. Carlisle, Judge. Cause No. CR84-076E/84-005165.
State v. Ben-Yisrayl, 809 N.E.2d 309, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 478 (Ind., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) of murder, rape, burglary, and criminal confinement. The court imposed the death penalty for the murder conviction and, alternatively, imprisonment if the death penalty was set aside. The court also imposed consecutive imprisonment terms for the other convictions. The postconviction court set aside the death sentence but upheld the remainder of the sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred upon remand when it adopted, without a sentencing hearing, the alternative sentence of imprisonment originally imposed by the trial court. He further alleged that his alternative sentence was an illegal sentence. On appeal, the court found that the postconviction court granted relief only as to the death penalty. To the extent that defendant's sentence of imprisonment reflected the aggregate sentence imposed for the separate convictions of burglary, criminal confinement, and rape, his claim was waived. In addition, res judicata did not bar his sentencing challenges on their merits. Thus, the original trial court exceeded its statutory authority in imposing defendant's alternative consecutive sentence for murder. The trial court upon remand was to conduct a full sentencing hearing for the murder conviction. Any term in excess of the presumptive sentence under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-3 was to be determined on the basis of aggravating circumstances pursuant to the Sixth Amendment right to jury trial. Finally, defendant waived his challenge to the denial of hiss motion to transfer based upon an allegedly improper change of judge.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part as to the sentences for the convictions of burglary, criminal confinement, and rape, and reversed in part as to the sentence for the conviction of murder. The cause was remanded for a new sentencing hearing on the murder conviction only.

K.M.K. v. A.K.


No. 34A02-0812-CV-1079


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


908 N.E.2d 658; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 931



June 30, 2009, Decided 
June 30, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by K.M.K. v. A.K., 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1638 (Ind. Ct. App., Sept. 14, 2009)
Transfer denied by K.M.K. v. A.K., 919 N.E.2d 560, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1546 (Ind., 2009)
Decision reached on appeal by Price v. K.M.K., 2011 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 276 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas R. Lett, Special Judge. Cause No. 34D02-0710-CT-1178.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother filed suit against appellee father's attorney alleging 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and civil conspiracy claims and seeking treble damages. The attorney counterclaimed for attorney's fees. The mother appealed an order entered by the Howard Superior Court (Indiana), which granted the attorney's motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court rejected the mother's claim that the attorney was engaged in a conspiracy with the trial court in obtaining an ex parte custody order as the attorney did not act under the color of state law, and was not engaged in a joint action, a concerted effort, or a conspiracy with the trial court. The § 1983 and civil conspiracy claims were properly dismissed. The mother did not show that the alleged ex parte communication between the attorney and the custody court constituted a joint action, a concerted effort, or a conspiracy. Further, a conspiracy to violate § 1983 was not a violation of a state statute independent of a § 1983 violation. The trial court granted a hearing on the attorney's request for attorney's fees. The dismissal order did not implicitly deny the attorney's request. The request was not barred by collateral estoppel as a prior request for attorney's fees was related to a prior matter. Ind. Code § 34-52-1-1(b) (2007) indicated that attorney's fees could be awarded to the prevailing party in any civil action if the trial court deemed them necessary or proper. There was no basis for barring the attorney from requesting attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

429 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Wrigley


No. 33A05-0903-CV-156


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


908 N.E.2d 354; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 918



June 25, 2009, Decided 
June 25, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HENRY SUPERIOR COURT I. The Honorable Michael D. Peyton, Judge. Cause No. 33D01-0902-PL-2.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged an order of the Henry Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against appellees, the superintendent of a correctional facility and the grievance executive assistant at the facility. The trial court dismissed the complaint as frivolous under the Indiana Frivolous Claim Law, Ind. Code § 34-58-1-2.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that defendant deprived him of his rights under the Eighth Amended to the United States Constitution. Because the Indiana Frivolous Claim Law tracked 28 U.S.C.S. § 1915 and the Prison Litigation Reform Act, 28 U.S.C.S. § 1915A, as well as the United States Supreme Court's interpretation of "frivolous" in those statutes, the court of appeals adopted that interpretation. It held that the trial court erred by dismissing the inmate's complaint as frivolous under § 34-58-1-2. The inmate claimed that defendants had control over the temperature of the water in the prison showers and had made it scolding hot. He also alleged that he broke his ankle during recreation time and that the shackles that he was forced to wear when taken out of his cell caused him severe pain. The inmate contended that those actions violated his Eighth Amendment right to be free from cruel and unusual punishment. That was a valid legal theory and conclusion, even if it was eventually determined that the facts alleged were false. The inmate's claims did not meet the United States Supreme Court's standard for factual frivolousness. His complaint did not lack an arguable basis in law or in fact.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals reversed the order.

 

430 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


B.L.H. v. G.L.H. (In re Visitation of C.L.H.)


No. 32A01-0812-CV-597


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


908 N.E.2d 320; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 907



June 23, 2009, Decided 
June 23, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at Heckler v. Heckler, 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 1776 (Ind. Ct. App., Sept. 23, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Karen M. Love, Judge. Cause No. 32D03-0804-DR-54.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee grandparents filed a petition against appellant mother in the Hendricks Superior Court (Indiana), for visitation under the Indiana Grandparent's Visitation Act, Ind. Code § 31-17-5. Following a hearing, the trial court awarded the grandparents extensive visitation with the mother's child. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents were primarily responsible for caring for the mother's child, who was born out of wedlock, until the child was five years old. When the mother entered into a relationship with another woman, a serious level of discord developed between the mother and the grandparents as the grandparents did not approve of the relationship or the other woman. On appeal, the court noted that the mother's parental rights were a liberty interest protected by the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court found that the trial court's visitation order was not supported by the findings or the undisputed evidence. The evidence showed that the mother was a reasonable person and had a rational basis for the decision, which she did not come to easily. Further, the presumption was that the mother, who was an undisputed fit parent, had made a decision that was in her child's best interests, and that decision deserved special weight under the law. However, the trial court's findings did not support the conclusion that visitation was in the child's best interests. Accordingly, the grandparents failed to meet their burden and to rebut the presumption accorded to the mother.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order awarding visitation to the grandparents was reversed.

Dowdell v. City of Jeffersonville


No. 10A04-0811-CV-676


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


907 N.E.2d 559; 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 888



June 9, 2009, Decided 
June 9, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Dowdell v. City of Jeffersonville, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1658 (Ind., Sept. 11, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE CLARK SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Vicki L. Carmichael, Judge. Cause No. 10D01-0708-PL-143.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant filed a complaint against appellee city in the Clark Superior Court (Indiana), for injunctive and declaratory relief in a challenge to the constitutionality of a city ordinance. The trial court found that the ordinance, which prohibited all sex offenders from ever having unrestricted access to the city's parks and recreation areas, was constitutional and granted summary judgment in favor of the city. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A city ordinance prohibited convicted sex offenders from entering public parks in the city. Though offenders could seek very limited exemptions, the exemption procedure was extraordinarily burdensome and virtually illusory. The claimant was charged, convicted, served the sentence for his crime of sexual battery, and completed his registration requirement before the ordinance was enacted. He argued that the trial court erred by concluding that the city's ordinance prohibiting all sex offenders from ever having unrestricted access to the city's parks and recreation areas was constitutional. Specifically, he argued that the ordinance was facially unconstitutional pursuant to Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 12, and 24 and that it was unconstitutional as applied to him pursuant to the same constitutional provisions because he was no longer required to register as a sex offender. On appeal, the court found that, as applied to the claimant, the ordinance violated the prohibition on ex post facto laws contained in the Indiana Constitution because it imposed burdens that had the effect of adding punishment beyond that which could have been imposed when the crime was committed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.


 

432 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Donahue
