Suggs v. State


No. 32A01-0710-CR-477


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


883 N.E.2d 1188; 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 711



April 10, 2008, Decided 
April 10, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jeffrey V. Boles, Judge. Cause No. 32C01-0704-FD-37.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hendricks Circuit Court (Indiana) of attempted theft as a class D felony under Ind. Code §§ 35-43-4-2 and 35-41-5-1 (2004). The jury found defendant to be a habitual offender under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8 (Supp. 2005). The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent prison sentences with one sentence enhanced due to defendant's status as an habitual offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two women were accused of attempted theft from the electronics department of a store. Defendant argued that the trial court committed fundamental error by failing to instruct the jury regarding accomplice liability under Ind. Code § 35-41-2-4 for the attempted theft charge. He also contended that the court committed fundamental error by admitting copies of certified court documents in the habitual offender proceedings. On appeal, the court found that the State of Indiana appeared not to have argued that defendant aided, induced, or caused the two women to commit the offense of attempted theft, but rather to have argued that he was a principal in the offense. Moreover, defendant could not establish substantial harm or substantial potential for harm due to the lack of accomplice liability instructions because the evidence was sufficient to convict him as a principal. Finally, although the certifications of defendant's prior offenses were copies rather than originals, in violation of Ind. R. Evid. 902(1), this did not deprive defendant of a fair trial and did not result in fundamental error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and his status as an habitual offender were affirmed.

Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner sought pro se review of a grant of summary judgment by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of defendants, the Indiana Department of Corrections (DOC) and a control unit, in the prisoner's action seeking injunctive and declaratory relief regarding his treatment in segregated confinement in the unit and alleging violations of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights (UDHR).

Manigault v. State


No. 49A02-0707-CR-565


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


881 N.E.2d 679; 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 307



February 22, 2008, Decided 
February 22, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Patrick Murphy, Commissioner. Cause No. 49G23-0701-FB-1265.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with possessing cocaine within one thousand feet of a family housing complex, a class B felony, Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) conducted a bench trial; denied his motion to dismiss, which challenged the constitutionality of § 35-48-4-6; and convicted him of possession of cocaine, a class B felony. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A trooper observed defendant outside of a hotel, loitering near a car belonging to an individual with an outstanding arrest warrant. The hotel was a family housing complex under Ind. Code § 35-41-1-10.5. Defendant lied about his identity and tried to evade the trooper by walking into the lobby. Upon confirmation that the identity information was false, defendant was arrested and transported to a processing center where cocaine base was found in his pocket during an inventory search. The appellate court found that there was no abuse of discretion in admitting the cocaine because there was no violation of the Fourth Amendment or Ind. Const. art. 1, § 11. The trooper's approach and initial contact with defendant near the car did not amount to a seizure, as defendant was free to leave. The encounter evolved into a detention for investigatory purposes. Defendant's false identity information and other facts created a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity. The detention was reasonable given the totality of the circumstances. Denial of defendant's motion to dismiss was not error because the language of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6 was clear and unambiguous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

Zitlaw v. State


No. 29A05-0701-CR-35


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


880 N.E.2d 724; 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 249



February 14, 2008, Decided 
February 14, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Zitlaw v. State, 891 N.E.2d 45, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 1585 (Ind., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Steven R. Nation, Judge. Cause No. 29D01-0606-FD-112.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with performance harmful to minors as a class D felony in violation of Ind. Code § 35-49-3-3(a)(5) (2004), public indecency, and public nudity. The Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charge for performance harmful to minors. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The probable cause affidavit alleged that while in a public park, defendant exposed his penis and fondled it front of an undercover officer to attempt to get the officer to engage in oral sex. The court held that § 35-49-3-3(a)(5), which forbade certain conduct in an area to which minors had access, did not require that a minor actually be present. Furthermore, unaccompanied minors were usually allowed in a public park. Thus, it was unnecessary for the State to name specific minor victims or to include the phrase "unless each minor is accompanied by the minor's parent or guardian" in the information. Next, as § 35-49-3-3(a)(5) and Ind. Code § 35-49-2-2(2) and (3) did not require minors' actual presence, there was no merit to the argument that there was no performance harmful to minors under § 35-49-2-2. Finally, Ind. Code §§ 35-49-3-3 and 35-49-2-2 were not unconstitutionally vague. Individuals of ordinary intelligence would comprehend the statutes adequately enough to inform them of the proscribed conduct. Further, defendant's alleged conduct of exposing himself in a public park for the purpose of engaging in oral sex clearly fell within the conduct proscribed by the statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the motion to dismiss.

Johnson v. State


No. 49A02-0704-CR-314


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


879 N.E.2d 649; 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 70



January 25, 2008, Decided 
January 25, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Rebecca Pierson-Treacy, Judge. Cause No. 49F19-0602-CM-20922.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), defendant was convicted of operating a vehicle while intoxicated, as a class A misdemeanor; and operating a vehicle with an alcohol concentration equivalent to at least.08 grams of alcohol per 210 liters of her breath, as a class C misdemeanor. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's argument that the presumption created by Ind. Code § 9-30-6-15(b) violated the United States Constitution. Under Indiana law, there was no fundamental right to drive a motor vehicle. By enjoying the privilege of driving on Indiana's roadways, defendant had consented to be subject to the legislation that governed their use. Furthermore, the presumption was a legislative creation, and it was within the legislature's prerogative to determine its applicability. Finally, defendant had not rebutted the presumption; reasonably, 45 minutes elapsed between the time defendant consumed her last alcoholic beverage at a restaurant and her undertaking the chemical breath test. Next, it was not error to admit under Ind. Code § 9-30-6-5(b) the certificate of compliance for the breath test machine issued by the Indiana Department of Toxicology. The court had previously held that admission of such certifications did not violate the Confrontation Clause of the Sixth Amendment. Furthermore, the statement in the certification indicating that the machine was in good working order was not bolstering language that exceeded the scope of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

478 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. City of Hammond


No. 45A03-0708-CV-372


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


879 N.E.2d 644; 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 490



January 25, 2008, Decided 
January 25, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Allen v. City of Hammond, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 473 (Ind., May 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable E. Duane Daugherty, Judge Pro Tem. Cause No. 45D05-0507-PL-122.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant city in which plaintiff challenged defendant's ordinance imposing a $100 business license fee. The Lake Superior Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment for the city and denied plaintiff's summary judgment motion. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected plaintiff's argument that under Ind. Code § 36-1-3-8, the fee was greater than that reasonably related to the cost of exercising a regulatory power. The fact that the city did not have documentary evidence of specific calculations one year after the enactment of the ordinance did not itself establish that the cost did not exist or that the fee was not reasonably related to the regulatory purpose. Furthermore, the fact that before the ordinance was enacted, the city had no visible regulatory presence at plaintiff's office except for occasional fire inspections did not establish a lack of regulatory costs. The fact that the fees were deposited into the city's general fund and then distributed to municipal departments did not show that the fee was imposed with any other purpose than to defray the administrative costs of regulating business operations. The ordinance was not an unconstitutional attempt to license attorneys under Ind. Const. art. VII, § 4 or an attempt under Ind. Code § 36-1-3-8 to regulate conduct that was regulated by a state agency. It did not regulate who was licensed as an attorney or place any professional requirements on attorneys.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

479 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Cole v. State


No. 49A05-0704-CR-208


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


878 N.E.2d 882; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2998



December 31, 2007, Decided 
December 31, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Amy Barbar, Magistrate. Cause No. 49G02-0608-FC-155946.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of carrying a handgun without a license as a Class C felony, resisting law enforcement as a Class A misdemeanor (by resisting), and resisting law enforcement as a Class A misdemeanor (by fleeing). The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to two years for the handgun charge and one year each for the resisting charges, all to be served concurrently on home detention. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the officer did not have reasonable suspicion to stop him and therefore the handgun later found on his person should have been suppressed pursuant to the exclusionary rule. Even assuming the officer did not have reasonable suspicion to order defendant back into the car, by fleeing from and forcibly resisting the officer, defendant committed two new criminal offenses. These actions purged the taint from the unconstitutional investigatory stop, making the exclusionary rule inapplicable. The appellate court noted that defendant had no right to flee from and forcibly resist the officer. Even though the officer may not have had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant, the officer did have probable cause to believe that defendant violated the resisting law enforcement statute by fleeing after being ordered to stop and by forcibly resisting the officer. Because the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant for those crimes, it followed that the handgun was seized incident to a lawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

480 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Marlett v. State


No. 18A04-0703-CR-131


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


878 N.E.2d 860; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2953



December 28, 2007, Decided 
December 28, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Marlett v. State, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 300 (Ind., Mar. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Peter Haviza, Special Judge. Cause No. 18C02-0509-JD-208. 18C03-0605-FA-7.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty but mentally ill to Class B felony criminal confinement. The Delaware Circuit Court (Indiana) imposed a 20-year sentence. It found that defendant was a sexually violent predator and required that he register as a sexual or violent offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Reviewing the sentence under Ind. R. App. P. 7(B), the court stated that although defendant had Asperger's syndrome, there was conflicting evidence as to the extent it limited his overall functioning and no clear evidence of a direct nexus between it and the crime. Although defendant's attack on a classmate was egregious, the period of confinement was brief; thus, the offense could not be said to be in the worst class. Defendant's mental health, guilty plea, and lack of an official criminal history weighed in his favor. Thus, his sentence would be reduced to 15 years executed, plus two years suspended and served on probation. Next, including criminal confinement of a minor as a crime requiring defendant to register with the Sex and Violent Offender Registry under Ind. Code § 11-8-8-5 did not violate substantive due process. Other courts had held that such inclusion bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest. Finally, the trial court was to determine sexually violent predator status under the new procedures prescribed by Ind. Code § 35-38-1-7.5(e), which addressed defendant's concerns regarding the conclusory nature of reports and experts' failure to testify.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's sentence and directed that it be revised to a term of 17 years, with two years suspended to supervised probation. It affirmed the requirement that defendant be placed on the Registry after his release from prison. It remanded for the trial court to reconsider defendant's sexually violent predator status after conducting a hearing on the matter that complied with the current version of § 35-38-1-7.5(e).


 

481 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Douglas v. State


No. 48A02-0701-CR-33


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


878 N.E.2d 873; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 3052



December 28, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Dennis D. Carroll, Judge. Cause No. 48D01-0406-FD-215.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence of 30 months by the Madison Superior Court (Indiana) and sentence of 30 months after pleading guilty to failing to register as a sex offender. Defendant argued the sex offender registry statute was an ex post facto law and his sentence was inappropriate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was released from prison after serving his sentence for three counts of sexual misconduct with a minor. Pursuant to the then-existing version of the sex offender statute, he was required to register as a sex offender for the following 10 years. Defendant moved and failed to register. The appellate court noted a plea agreement was not used. Additionally, conducting a trial would have been fruitless. Thus, defendant did not waive the ex post facto issue. The overall legislative intent in enacting the sex offender registry was civil and regulatory in nature. The registration did not restrain the offender's movement, and the information required to register was not burdensome. The consequence of violating the registration requirement was not retrospective because the amended version of the statute was in effect when defendant failed to register. However, the appellate court agreed that his criminal history's lack of gravity, dissimilarity, and proximity to the current offense did not warrant an enhanced sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed as to the conviction. The sentence imposed was inappropriate and it was remanded for the trial court to impose the presumptive sentence of eighteen months.

Plaza Group Props., LLC v. Spencer County Plan Comm'n


No. 74A01-0703-CV-145


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


877 N.E.2d 877; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2744



December 13, 2007, Decided 
December 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Plaza Group Props. LLC v. Spencer County Plan Comm'n, 891 N.E.2d 47, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 382 (Ind., 2008)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Plaza Group Props., LLC v. Spencer County Plan Comm'n, 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1229 (Ind. Ct. App., Aug. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SPENCER CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Wayne A. Roell, Judge. Cause No. 74C01-0512-MI-0482.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged the judgment of the Spencer Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted partial summary judgment to appellees, a county plan commission and its board of commissioners (the county). The county filed a complaint for an injunction against the landowner, alleging that the landowner violated its building and zoning ordinances. The landowner counterclaimed alleging that the ordinances at issue were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The landowner had purchased a truck stop, which consisted of a main building, a motel, and a convenience store. After the landowner commenced renovations without a permit, the county issued a stop-work order and filed suit seeking to prevent the landowner from operating a sexually oriented business on the property. The trial court subsequently issued a permanent injunction in favor of the county enjoining the landowner from operating such a business. The court held that there was no genuine issue of material fact that the landowner made more than $ 5,000 of renovations to the property without receiving a building permit and, therefore, it was not entitled to lawful nonconforming use status on the property. The court further held that the portions of the sexually oriented business ordinances at issue did not unconstitutionally burden protected speech and, therefore, the court rejected the landowner's argument that the challenged ordinances were unconstitutional. The court also determined that the permanent injunction was properly narrowed to enjoining the operation of a sexually oriented business only and did not prevent the operation of any compliant commercial business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting partial summary judgment in favor of the county.


 

483 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Lindsey v. State


No. 59A01-0703-CR-107


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


877 N.E.2d 190; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2725



December 3, 2007, Decided 
December 3, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Lindsey v. State, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 194 (Ind., Feb. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ORANGE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Kenneth L. Lopp, Special Judge. Cause No. 59C01-0608-FB-54.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of operating a vehicle with an alcohol concentration equivalent of .15 or more, a misdemeanor, and was found to be a Habitual Substance Offender (HSO) under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-50-2-10. The Orange Circuit Court (Indiana) enhanced defendant's one-year sentence by seven years for the HSO determination, resulting in an eight-year sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first rejected defendant's argument that he was denied due process because the State had not disclosed evidence relating to the HSO allegation in a timely manner. The failure appeared to be inadvertent; thus, exclusion was not an appropriate remedy. Furthermore, the evidence produced by the State as part of discovery at least put defendant on notice of the prior convictions on which the State intended to rely. Next, the seven-year enhancement was not disproportionate under Ind. Const. art. I, § 16, given the fact that the current offense was defendant's fifth OWI violation. Next, other than defendant's bare assertions, nothing substantiated his claim that his incarceration in the county jail instead of a state facility was cruel and unusual punishment under § 16. The trial court did not err in not treating defendant's guilty plea to the HSO allegation as a significant mitigating circumstance. Defendant's guilty plea was a pragmatic decision that had not saved the State time or money. Finally, the eight-year sentence was not inappropriate under Ind. R. App. P. 7(B), given defendant's significant history of OWI convictions and an additional conviction involving alcohol.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Hamilton County Plan Comm'n v. Nieten


No. 29A05-0612-CV-736


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


876 N.E.2d 355; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2571



November 14, 2007, Decided 
November 14, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hamilton Co. Plan Comm'n v. Nieten, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 75 (Ind. Ct. App., Jan. 18, 2008)
Transfer denied by Hamilton County Plan Comm'n v. Nieten, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 444 (Ind., May 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Steven R. Nation, Judge. Cause No. 29D01-0508-MI-691.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of zoning appeals (BZA) sought review of the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) which reversed the determination by the BZA that a building maintained on property owned by appellee property owners constituted a violation of the Hamilton County, Ind., Zoning Ordinance art. 2, § 1, as it was not a principal building for residential purposes. The issue was whether the existence of a building used as a guesthouse was prohibited.


OVERVIEW: The property owners moved into a newly constructed home. They built a support building which included a small kitchen, a toilet and shower. The property owners informed the plan commission that they would not use the building for residential purposes, and that it would only be infrequently used as a guesthouse for occasional visitors. The plan commission alleged that the property owners violated Hamilton County, Ind. Zoning Ordinance art. 18C, § 1(a). The property owners filed an application for a variance from the ordinance to "allow" their "outbuilding" to be used as a guest house. The application specified that the guest house would only be for occasional visitor use, not as a residence. Their request for a variance was denied. The property owners alleged that the ordinance did not forbid their use of an accessory building to temporarily house a visiting guest. The appellate court found that no application to vary the zoning ordinance was necessary as the accessory building was one to provide housing for less than 30 days and it was both incident to and related to their use of their main building. Thus, the guesthouse did not violate the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Smith & Wesson Corp. v. City of Gary


No. 45A05-0612-CV-754


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


875 N.E.2d 422; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2381



October 29, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Smith & Wesson Corp. v. City of Gary, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 8 (Ind. Ct. App., Jan. 9, 2008)
Transfer denied by Smith & Wesson v. City of Gary, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 12 (Ind., Jan. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert A. Pete, Judge. Cause No. 45D05-0005-CT-243.
City of Gary v. Smith & Wesson, 801 N.E.2d 1222, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 1096 (Ind., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant gun manufacturers brought an interlocutory appeal from denial of their motion to dismiss or, in the alternative, judgment on the pleadings by the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) in an action brought by plaintiff city. The manufacturers argued, inter alia, that the Protection of Lawful Commerce in Arms Act (PLCAA), 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 7901-7903, barred the city's nuisance claims.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the enactment of the PLCAA, the manufacturers moved to dismiss the city's nuisance complaint. The appellate court held that the case turned on the interpretation of the word "applicable" in the predicate exception, 15 U.S.C.S. § 7903(5)(A)(iii). Even assuming that the PLCAA required an underlying violation of a statute directly applicable to the sale or marketing of a firearm, the city alleged such violations in their complaint. The specific context did not create an ambiguous meaning of the predicate exception with regard to the particular dispute at issue. Indiana's public nuisance statute, Ind. Code § 32-30-6-6, was a legislative enactment, which the Indiana Supreme Court interpreted as applying to the city's claim. Thus, the city's claim was not an attempt to expand the common law and it was not an attempt to circumvent the legislative branch of government. Because the city's complaint and the Indiana Supreme Court's opinion indicated that the city alleged that the manufacturers violated a state or federal statute applicable to the sale or marketing of the product, the city's action fell under the predicate exception and was not barred by the PLCAA.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Vega v. Allen County Dep't of Family & Children Servs. (In re J.V.)


No. 02A03-0702-JV-69


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


875 N.E.2d 395; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2379



October 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Vega v. Allen County Dep't of Children Servs. (In re J.V.), 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 76 (Ind. Ct. App., Jan. 24, 2008)
Transfer denied by In re J.V. v. Allen Co. Dep't of Family & Children Servs., 2008 Ind. LEXIS 374 (Ind., Apr. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Lori K. Morgan, Magistrate. The Honorable Charles F. Pratt, Judge. Cause No. 02D07-8710-JC-137.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Allen county Department of Family and Children Services filed a petition alleging the subject children to be children in need of services (CHINS). Respondent parents filed a motion to suppress. The motion was denied. The Allen Superior Court (Indiana) found the children to be CHINS. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police arrived at the parents' home in response to a 911 call and the mother allowed them to enter. The father told the police that the parents had been engaged in "kinky sex" on the living room couch. The police discovered a digital camera which contained nude pictures of the mother, some of which included the children, and pictures of the parents engaged in sex acts. The appellate court, which assumed, without deciding, that evidence was obtained in violation of the Fourth Amendment and Ind. Const. art. 1, § 11, determined that the exclusionary rule did not apply to CHINS proceedings and thus, the trial court did not err in denying the parents' motion to suppress. The appellate court further concluded that the best evidence rule did not preclude the admission of evidence relating to pictures the officers had seen on the camera as police made a diligent search for the photos and memory card. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's findings of fact, as, inter alia, the children could have seen the parents engaging in sexual relations and there were pictures of the mother naked while a child touched her vaginal area.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Belvedere v. State


No. 48A05-0611-CR-669


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


875 N.E.2d 352; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2360



October 23, 2007, Decided 
October 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by Belvedere v. State, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 519 (Ind., June 27, 2008)
Superseded by Belvedere v. State, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 489 (Ind., June 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas Newman, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 48D03-0406-FC-00303.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Madison Superior Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion to suppress and entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of Possession of Marijuana with Intent to Deal and Maintaining a Common Nuisance. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police detective was contacted by a "source" regarding a white male at two addresses on a single piece of property, and indicated that the source had seen marijuana at the addresses. The detective retrieved trash sitting in an alley that included mail addressed to defendant, as well as stems, seeds, and a small amount of marijuana. The detective made some inquiries and confirmed defendant's identity. The detective then obtained a search warrant for the addresses. The search warrant was executed, marijuana was located, and defendant was arrested. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress and defendant was convicted based on the evidence found. After the search was conducted, but before defendant's convictions became final, the state supreme court announced in Litchfield a new constitutional rule that trash searches required Terry-like "articulable individualized suspicion." The appellate court found that the new rule applied retroactively to defendant's case, that the source's tip lacked any indicia of reliability, and that the lack of reliability could not be excused by the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule recognized in Leon or in Ind. Code § 35-37-4-5.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments of conviction were reversed.

 

488 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Wiley v. McShane


No. 64A05-0702-CV-109


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


875 N.E.2d 273; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2363



October 22, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Wiley v. McShane, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 73 (Ind. Ct. App., Jan. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William E. Alexa, Judge. Cause No. 64D02-0510-EU-8839.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant daughter sought review of a decision of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which required her to file a bond, pursuant to Ind. Code § 29-1-7-19, after she filed a complaint challenging the validity of her deceased mother's last will and testament. When the daughter failed to file the bond, the trial court had dismissed the complaint, entering judgment in favor of appellees, the estate, its personal representative, and others.


OVERVIEW: There was no dispute that the daughter was required to file a bond. The contested issue was whether the $ 75,000 bond ordered by the trial court was unreasonable and an abuse of discretion. The appellate court reversed. The only evidence before the trial court when it set the bond was appellees' demonstrative exhibit that listed estimated costs to be incurred by the estate as a result of and during the will contest totaling $ 279,850. However, the estimated costs included, inter alia, costs for depositions, the production of medical records, and attorney fees. Those were litigation expenses that were not recoverable under § 29-1-7-19 and they should not have been considered when the bond was set. The bond was to be set at an amount to compensate for due prosecution of the will contest proceedings and the payment of all costs should the daughter not prevail in the will contest.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for a cost determination consistent with the appellate court's opinion for purposes of setting the bond at an amount to compensate for due prosecution of the will contest proceedings and for payment of all costs if the daughter did not prevail.

State v. Washington


No. 02A03-0703-CR-124


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


875 N.E.2d 278; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2370



October 22, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Washington, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 74 (Ind. Ct. App., Jan. 24, 2008)
Transfer granted by State v. Washington, 891 N.E.2d 45, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 355 (Ind., 2008)
Superseded by State v. Washington, 898 N.E.2d 1200, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 1284 (Ind., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert E. Ross, Magistrate. Cause No. 02D04-0607-CM-5058.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with misdemeanor possession of marijuana. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the marijuana seized from his pocket during a traffic stop. The Allen Superior Court (Indiana) granted the motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped after an officer observed defendant riding a moped without goggles and a helmet, as required for riders under 18 years of age, and swerving and crossing what the officer perceived to be the center point of the road. The issue on appeal was whether the officer violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 11 against unreasonable searches and seizures when the officer asked defendant if he was in possession of drugs. The appellate court noted that the officer was entitled to detain defendant for a time sufficient to complete the purpose of the traffic stop. However, the appellate concluded that, under the totality of the circumstances, the officer's inquiry that asked whether defendant had any drugs on him or with him was unreasonable under § 11. In the context of the afternoon traffic stop of defendant's moped for a traffic infraction, which presented no indications of drugs or other criminal activity, the officer's inquiry that asked defendant whether he possessed drugs was not related either to the purpose of the stop or to officer safety. While the officer's inquiry was minimal in terms of duration, it nevertheless extended the duration of the stop.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Crist v. South-West Lake Maxinkuckee Conservancy Dist. (In re Creation of South-West Lake Maxinkuckee Conservancy Dist.)


No. 50A04-0612-CV-694


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


875 N.E.2d 222; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2372



October 22, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Crist v. South-West Lake Maxinkuckee Conservancy Dist., 2008 Ind. LEXIS 208 (Ind., Feb. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARSHALL CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Michael D. Cook, Judge. Cause No. 50C01-0309-MI-91.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant-intervenor remonstrator, on behalf of all remonstrators in the action, challenged the judgment of the Marshall Circuit Court (Indiana), which ordered the creation of a conservancy district of a portion of a lake, pursuant to Ind. Code § 14-33-2-16. Petitioner freeholders had filed a petition for the creation of the district and the remonstrators filed petitions opposing its creation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held a hearing to determine the validity of the signatures on both petitions and thereafter issued an order creating the conservancy district and dividing it into seven districts. The court held that the trial court erred as a matter of law by striking 10 signatures from the remonstrators' petition after they filed an untimely request to withdraw their signatures. However, the trial court properly struck four signatures from the remonstrators' petition because those individuals were not freeholders when the remonstrators filed their petition. As a result, the remonstrators' petition contained 50.9 percent of the freeholders' signatures, which was less than the 51 percent that was required to dismiss the petition, pursuant to Ind. Code § 14-33-2-15. The court also agreed with the trial court's finding that the conservancy district was contiguous within the meaning of Ind. Code § 14-33-3-1 and held that the trial court adequately defined the conservancy district areas. The court also held that the trial court's finding that the conservancy district would serve the public health was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court found no error and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Carter v. Carolina Tobacco Co.


No. 49A04-0503-CV-151


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


873 N.E.2d 611; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2123



September 17, 2007, Decided 
September 17, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Theodore M. Sosin, Judge. Cause No. 49C01-0308-PL-2403.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee tobacco company filed a complaint against appellant, the Office of the Attorney General of the State of Indiana (OAG), in the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), for injunctive relief and a declaratory judgment. The court found that the tobacco company was entitled to an injunction prohibiting the OAG from excluding the tobacco company from a directory, and to a declaration that it was a manufacturer of tobacco products. The OAG appealed.


OVERVIEW: The OAG contended that the tobacco company's brand of cigarettes was not to be listed in the OAG's Directory of Cigarettes Approved for Stamping and Sale in Indiana because the tobacco company was not a tobacco product manufacturer under Ind. Code § 24-3-3-10. In essence, if the tobacco company was not the manufacturer of cigarettes, the tobacco company could not sell its brand of cigarettes in Indiana. While the tobacco company did not physically produce its brand of cigarettes, it controlled the manufacturing process for its cigarettes. On appeal, the court found that the OAG's decision to equate "manufacture" with "fabricate" for purposes of considering the tobacco company's request for inclusion in the Directory was arbitrary and, therefore, unreasonable. Therefore, the trial court's determination that the tobacco company was the manufacturer of its brand of cigarettes was proper. Moreover, the injunction prohibiting the OAG from basing its decision to exclude the tobacco company from the Directory upon the OAG's determination that the tobacco company was not the manufacturer of its brand of cigarettes was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Keeney v. State


No. 21A01-0611-CR-495


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


873 N.E.2d 187; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2080



September 13, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Daniel Lee Pflum, Judge. Cause No. 21C01-0210-FB-214.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pleaded guilty to forgery, a felony, the Fayette Circuit Court (Indiana) ordered him to provide a deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) sample to the State under Ind. Code § 10-13-6-10. Defendant appealed. arguing that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that it had previously held that the compulsory collection of DNA samples under the DNA Database, Ind. Code §§ 10-13-6-1 to 10-13-6-22, did not violate the Fourth Amendment. It served a special need, assisting in future criminal investigations and for use in research and other administrative purposes, beyond the normal need for law enforcement and crime detection. Although the United States Supreme Court had recently used a general balancing test to determine whether a suspicionless search of a parolee was permissible, the special needs test was a more stringent analysis. Defendant presented no cogent reasoning to explain why the court, having upheld the statutes under the special needs analysis, should find the statutes unconstitutional under the less stringent general balancing test. Thus, his argument was waived under Ind. R. App. P. 46(A)(8)(a). Moreover, defendant had presented no argument as to why the court's balancing of the salient interests in the previous case was either in error or otherwise inapplicable; thus, that error was waived too. Next, the court admonished defense counsel, whose brief contained uncited material in violation of Rule 46(A)(8)(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order. It admonished defendant's appellate counsel as to uncited material in her brief.

 

493 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


DAP, Inc. v. Akaiwa


No. 49A02-0608-CV-670


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


872 N.E.2d 1098; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2003



August 31, 2007, Decided 
August 31, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9801-MI-0001-291.
Asbestos Corp., Ltd. v. Akaiwa, 872 N.E.2d 1095, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2001 (Ind. Ct. App., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A decedent brought an action against defendant manufacturer based on exposure to asbestos fibers. Later, plaintiff executor was substituted for the decedent. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion for summary judgment. It held that the 10-year statute of repose of Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 did not apply to plaintiff's cause of action. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Through 1977, defendant manufactured an asphalt sealant that contained asbestos fibers. At some point from around 1980 to 1982, the decedent used a sealant made by defendant. He first developed symptoms consistent with asbestos exposure in June 2004. The next month, he was diagnosed with mesothelioma resulting from asbestos exposure. He filed his complaint in 2005. The court noted that the Indiana Supreme Court had held that Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 did not apply to non-miner defendants. Accordingly, as defendant was not a miner, plaintiff's action was barred by Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1. Although the supreme court had held that § 34-20-3-1 could be unconstitutional if a plaintiff could have been diagnosed with an asbestos-related disease during the 10-year repose period, it was undisputed that the decedent had not developed symptoms until about 22 years after his last possible exposure to asbestos. Finally, the court would not reach the issue of whether Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. Plaintiff lacked a cognizable harm from which to challenge any constitutional defect, and defendant as a non-miner lacked standing to challenge the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision.

 

494 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


TH Agric. & Nutrition, LLC v. Akaiwa


No. 49A05-0608-CV-441


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


872 N.E.2d 1104; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2005



August 31, 2007, Decided 
August 31, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9801-MI-0001-291.
Asbestos Corp., Ltd. v. Akaiwa, 872 N.E.2d 1095, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2001 (Ind. Ct. App., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executor brought an action against defendant distributor in which plaintiff alleged that the decedent had been exposed to asbestos. The Marion Superior Court denied defendant's motion for summary judgment. It held that the 10-year statute of repose of Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 did not apply to the action. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and its predecessor in interest distributed asbestos fibers on behalf of a mining company that later went bankrupt. Sometime between 1976 and 1982, the decedent was exposed to raw asbestos fibers. In 2004, he was diagnosed with mesothelioma resulting from asbestos exposure. The court stated that because defendant was not a miner, Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 did not apply to it; therefore, the statute of repose of Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 applied. It rejected plaintiff's argument that Ind. Code Ann. § 34-20-2-4 (2004), providing for jurisdiction over a principal distributor when a court could not hold jurisdiction over a manufacturer, required treating defendant as if it were a miner. Section 34-20-2-4 applied only to Ind. Code ch. 34-20-2. Furthermore, the Indiana Supreme Court had read Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 to apply only to actual miners of asbestos. Thus, plaintiff's suit was barred by the statute of repose. As for the argument that the supreme court's analysis of Ind. Code § 34-20-3-2 violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, plaintiff lacked a cognizable harm from which to challenge any constitutional defect, and defendant, as a non-miner, lacked standing to challenge the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision.

 

495 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Dempsey v. Auditor of Marion County


No. 49A02-0612-CV-1074


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


871 N.E.2d 1031; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1916



August 17, 2007, Decided 
August 17, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Dempsey v. Auditor of Marion County, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2581 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 17, 2007)
Transfer denied by Dempsey v. Auditor of Marion County, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 417 (Ind., May 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Theodore M. Sosin, Judge. Cause No. 49C01-0207-MI-1978.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer filed a motion to dismiss and/or for relief under Ind. R. Trial P. 60, seeking to set aside a tax deed to appellee county and a subsequent quitclaim deed to a third party. The Marion Circuit Court (Indiana) denied the motion; the taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer did not record his deed to the parcel. After the taxpayer filed a Chapter 13 bankruptcy petition, the county auditor sent notice of a tax sale and redemption rights to the former owner, but not to the taxpayer. No one bought the parcel; the county then received a tax certificate for the parcel. After the redemption period expired, it successfully petitioned the trial court for the issuance of a tax deed for the parcel; it then sold the parcel to a third party. Later, the bankruptcy court dismissed the taxpayer's bankruptcy case. The taxpayer argued that the county's petition for a tax deed was void because it was filed while the bankruptcy was pending, which violated the automatic stay imposed by 11 U.S.C.S. § 362. The appellate court agreed. Petitioning for the issuance of a tax deed was an affirmative act to obtain possession of property of the estate, in violation of § 362(a)(3). That the county was ignorant of the bankruptcy filing was irrelevant when considering whether it violated the stay, and the dismissal of the bankruptcy case did not retroactively lift the stay. As the tax deed was void, the sale to the third party was also void.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the denial of the taxpayer's motion to set aside the issuance of the tax deed.


 

496 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Johnson v. Patriotic Fireworks, Inc.


No. 49A02-0608-CV-632


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


871 N.E.2d 989; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1864



August 14, 2007, Decided 
August 14, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Patrick L. McCarty, Judge. Cause No. 49D03-9709-CP-1334.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fireworks wholesalers filed an action against defendant Indiana State Fire Marshall in which plaintiffs challenged a requirement that wholesalers with multiple sales locations obtain separate certificates of compliance for each location in which they operated. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion to dismiss the case for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Under Ind. Code § 22-11-14-5, wholesalers of restricted fireworks had to pay a $1,000 annual fee to operate in Indiana. Defendant interpreted this provision to mean that wholesalers had to pay the fee for each wholesale location that they operated. Defendant argued that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because plaintiffs had not exhausted their administrative remedies before filing the complaint. Defendant argued that there was no opportunity for administrative review. The court stated that the Indiana Supreme Court had categorically held that the question of whether § 22-11-14-5 required fireworks wholesalers to obtain separate certificates of compliance for each of their locations was a question of fact that could be resolved through the administrative process. The supreme court had rejected the assertion that review would be futile because there was no formal mechanism in place for the review of defendant's policies of general applicability. The mere fact that an administrative agency might refuse to provide the relief requested did not amount to futility. Accordingly, plaintiffs were required to pursue administrative review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's ruling with instructions that the complaint be dismissed.


 

497 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Christopher R. Brown, DDS, Inc. v. Decatur County Mem. Hosp.


No. 93A02-0703-EX-236


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


873 N.E.2d 69; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1809



August 9, 2007, Decided 
August 9, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by Christopher R. Brown, DDS, Inc. v. Decatur County Mem. Hosp., 2007 Ind. LEXIS 1069 (Ind., Nov. 29, 2007)
Superseded by Christopher R. Brown, D.D.S., Inc. v. Decatur County Mem. Hosp., 2008 Ind. LEXIS 771 (Ind., Aug. 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE WORKER'S COMPENSATION BOARD OF INDIANA. The Honorable G. Terence Coriden, Chairman. Cause No. C-159326.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dental office treated an employee of defendant hospital for work-related injuries. A single member of the Indiana Worker's Compensation Board awarded plaintiff prejudgment interest after plaintiff was belatedly paid the amount owed on its claim. Defendant appealed to the full Board, which reversed the single member's decision and denied plaintiff prejudgment interest. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff argued that a contract was created when it was requested by defendant's insurer to provide medical care to the employee. Therefore, it argued, the case should be treated as any other civil contract action addressing prejudgment interest. The court stated that a proceeding for worker's compensation was purely statutory in origin and procedure. Therefore, the rights and obligations of the parties had to be determined by reference to the Worker's Compensation Act. The legislature had amended the Act numerous times, but had never seen fit to add a provision for prejudgment interest for balances owed to health care providers for services rendered to employees in worker's compensation cases. Plaintiff was seeking prejudgment interest pursuant to a worker's compensation claim, and the court had no authority to read into a statute a provision the legislature had purposely omitted. As the court had determined that plaintiff was not entitled to prejudgment interest in that there was no provision for such within the Act, it would not address plaintiff's argument under the Indiana Constitution's Equal Privileges Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Roberts v. ACandS, Inc.


No. 93A02-0702-EX-180


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


873 N.E.2d 1055; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2135



August 8, 2007, Decided 
August 8, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered published by Roberts v. ACandS, Inc., 873 N.E.2d 1055, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2136 (Ind. Ct. App., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA WORKER'S COMPENSATION BOARD. Application No. O-159799.
Roberts v. ACandS, Inc., 872 N.E.2d 217, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1857 (Ind. Ct. App., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A worker who had been exposed to asbestos-containing insulation products sought worker's compensation benefits under the Occupational Diseases Act (ODA) from appellee employer. After the worker died, appellant estate was substituted as plaintiff. The full Worker's Compensation Board of Indiana dismissed the claim under Ind. Code § 22-3-7-36(b). The estate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board held that because the worker had recovered against third parties, the employer had no further liability to compensate him for his occupational disease. The court rejected the estate's argument that dismissal of the application was premature. The third-party lawsuit was final, the verdict defendant had paid its portion of the judgment in full, and the estate had received in excess of $4 million, well in excess of the potential amount recoverable under the ODA. The dismissal would not impair the estate's pursuit of claims against bankrupt defendants. Next, § 22-3-7-36(b) as applied to the estate did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, the Privileges and Immunities Clause, by denying the estate a complete remedy. The sum of the estate's recovery exceeded the total damages found by the jury. Furthermore, the humanitarian purpose of the ODA was to provide workers with an expeditious and adequate remedy, not a complete remedy. Finally, the statute as applied here did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 12, the Open Courts Clause. The estate had not been denied access to the courts, but had chosen to pursue third parties, forgoing the statutory remedy against the employer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

Sapen v. State


No. 20A03-0609-CR-424


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


869 N.E.2d 1273; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1590



July 20, 2007, Decided 
July 20, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Sapen v. State, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 937 (Ind., Oct. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable David C. Bonfiglio, Judge. Cause No. 20D06-0410-FD-971.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, defendant was convicted for resisting law enforcement, as a Class D felony, and operating while intoxicated, as a Class A misdemeanor. The Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to jail time, with most suspended to probation, suspended defendant's driver's license for 90 days, and required defendant to pay fines and make a written apology to the arresting officer. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erroneously admitted evidence obtained during a warrantless entry of defendant's home in violation of the Fourth Amendment and deprived defendant of the opportunity to present his defense when it, inter alia, refused to exclude the evidence or give instructions on reasonable resistance. The appellate court agreed, finding that exigent circumstances sufficient to overcome the warrant requirement of the Fourth Amendment did not exist. The officer did not order defendant to stop and was not in "hot pursuit" at the time defendant entered his garage. The officer could have obtained a telephonic warrant pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-33-5-8(a)(2), prior to entry into defendant's home. The appellate court went on to conclude that, even without the improperly obtained evidence, there was sufficient evidence to permit a factfinder to conclude defendant committed the offense of driving while intoxicated and thus, retrial on that charge would be permitted. However, because there was not sufficient evidence to establish that defendant forcibly resisted the officer by strong, violent, or powerful means, defendant could not be retried on the resisting charge.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were reversed and the case was remanded for retrial on the operating while intoxicated.

 

500 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Brenwick Assocs., LLC v. Boone County Redevelopment Comm'n


No. 06A04-0611-CV-682


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


870 N.E.2d 474; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1588



July 20, 2007, Decided 
July 20, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by Brenwick Assoc. v. Boone County Redevelopment Comm'n, 878 N.E.2d 220, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 1071 (Ind., 2007)
Superseded by Brenwick Assocs., LLC v. Boone County Redevelopment Comm'n, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 498 (Ind., June 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE BOONE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas K. Milligan, Special Judge. Cause No. 06D01-0610-PL-365.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Remonstrators, a town and a limited liability company, brought an action against defendants, a county redevelopment commission and a county board of commissioners, after defendants created an economic development area (EDA). The Boone Superior Court (Indiana) upheld the creation of the EDA. Remonstrators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first held that remonstrators were "aggrieved" under Ind. Code § 36-7-14-18(a). Whenever an action caused someone to lose control over the development of his own property, he was sufficiently aggrieved to challenge that action. Thus, any person who owned property in a proposed EDA was "aggrieved" for purposes of § 36-7-14-18. Next, 1425 acres of the area in question had previously been annexed by the town. Under case law, the authority that first undertook to exercise jurisdiction acquired exclusive jurisdiction. Here, the town had exercised jurisdiction when it adopted the annexation ordinance. Thus, the county was prohibited from establishing an EDA over those 1425 acres. With regard to the additional 2500 acres at issue, the procedure followed in creating the EDA, being legislative in nature, did not violate remonstrators' federal due process rights or Ind. Code § 36-7-14-17. Finally, in asking the court to find that the county had established the EDA as a power grab rather than in an effort to promote the best interests of the county, remonstrators were simply requesting that the court judge the credibility of witnesses and reweigh the evidence, which it would not do.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conclusion that remonstrators were not aggrieved. It also reversed the trial court's approval of the EDA as to 1425 acres in an annexation ordinance. It affirmed the trial court's approval of the EDA area as to an additional 2500 acres.

Nagy v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Sch. Corp.


No. 82A05-0609-CV-488


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


870 N.E.2d 12; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1501



July 13, 2007, Decided 
July 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Nagy v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Sch. Corp., 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2128 (Ind. Ct. App., Sept. 11, 2007)
Transfer denied by Nagy v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Sch. Corp., 2008 Ind. LEXIS 64 (Ind., Jan. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable J. Douglas Knight, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-0210-PL-4388.
Nagy v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Sch. Corp., 844 N.E.2d 481, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 271 (Ind., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents brought a suit against appellee school corporation in which the parents challenged a school activity fee. The Indiana Supreme Court held that the fee violated the Indiana Constitution, but did not rule on the parents' federal due process claim. On remand to the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), the parents filed a motion for attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The trial court denied the motion. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first stated that a plaintiff could be considered to be a prevailing party even when the merits of a federal constitutional claim had not been addressed, as long as the plaintiff's claims arose out of a common nucleus of operative fact and the federal claim was substantial. It then rejected the trial court's determination that because the parents had not succeeded on their claim that no activity fee at all could be charged, the parents had not been the prevailing party. The supreme court had explicitly held that the fee violated Ind. Const. art. 8, § 1. Thus, the parents had succeeded on a significant issue in the litigation that achieved some of the benefit they sought. The state and federal claims arose out of the same facts, the practice of charging an activity fee. Furthermore, the federal claim was substantial. It had been accepted by the trial court in an initial summary judgment ruling and by at least one judge on the present court. Next, it was not until the second set of parents were added to the suit that a federal claim was brought. Thus, only the second set of parents could recover attorney fees for work done upon both the state and federal claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision. It remanded the case for a calculation of reasonable attorney fees.

Manley v. State


No. 53A01-0701-PC-43


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


868 N.E.2d 1175; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1415



July 3, 2007, Decided 
July 3, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Manley v. State, 878 N.E.2d 210, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 749 (Ind., Sept. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Marc R. Kellams, Judge. Cause No. 53C02-9702-CF-74.
Manley v. State, 708 N.E.2d 928, 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 265 (Ind. Ct. App., Feb. 18, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of his petition for modification of sentence by the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana). Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court should have conducted a hearing and the trial court had authority to modify his sentence when the request was submitted more than one year after defendant began serving his sentence and the request for modification was not approved by the prosecuting attorney.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was convicted of child molesting, received a 55-year executed sentence. Defendant's motion to modify his sentence by reducing the term of years was denied. Defendant offered no support for his contention that Ind. Code § 35-38-1-17(b) ran afoul of the Indiana Constitution because it permitted a court to deny a petition for modification without first conducting a hearing. The appellate court held there was nothing vindictive about requiring defendant to serve his entire sentence. The appellate court declined his invitation to create a requirement that a hearing must be held before a trial court could rule upon a request for sentence modification under § 35-38-1-17(b) where a prosecutor refused to approve the request. There was nothing sinister or vindictive about the Department of Correction's allocation of resources. As defendant submitted his request for modification long after the statutory 365-day period had lapsed, and there was no evidence that the prosecutor approved his petition for modification, the trial court had no authority to grant his request.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Blackman v. State


No. 49A02-0610-CR-893


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


868 N.E.2d 579; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1323



June 26, 2007, Decided 
June 26, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Blackman v. State, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 719 (Ind., Sept. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kaisa Schafer, Judge Pro Tempore. Cause No. 49F10-0605-CM-91568.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marion Superior Court, Indiana, convicted defendant after a bench trial of disorderly conduct, as a class B misdemeanor, under Ind. Code § 35-45-1-3. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the noise generated by her outbursts was not unreasonable under the circumstances, and therefore the evidence was insufficient to support a finding of disorderly conduct. The sheer volume of defendant's outbursts disrupted the officers' investigation and attracted unwanted attention. The officers repeatedly asked defendant to lower her voice and to leave the scene of their investigation. Defendant defiantly ignored their requests and shouted even louder. The instant court found that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct because she produced decibels of sound that were too loud for the circumstances. Defendant's speech was ultimately ambiguous as to whether she was commenting on her own conduct or that of the officers. Accordingly, defendant's expression was not political. The State could have rationally concluded that where defendant obstructed and interfered with the officers' attempts to function as law enforcement officers, her conduct constituted an abuse of the right to speak and fell within the State's police power. Thus, defendant's arrest for disorderly conduct did not violate Ind. Const. art. 1, § 9.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

504 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Hanninen v. Koch


No. 36A01-0611-CV-503


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


868 N.E.2d 1137; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1312



June 22, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE JACKSON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable William E. Vance, Judge. Cause No. 36C01-0205-CT-9.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sued appellee estate administrator, asserting tort claims. Appellant rejected the administrator's qualified settlement offer (QSO). A jury returned a verdict in favor of the administrator. The administrator moved for attorney's fees, costs, and expenses pursuant to the QSO statute, Ind. Code § 34-50-1-6. The Jackson Circuit Court (Indiana) granted attorney's fees, costs, and expenses to the estate. Appellant filed an appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court determined that the trial court properly awarded the administrator $ 1,000 in attorney's fees, costs, and expenses. Regarding appellant's argument that the QSO statute chilled tort litigants' rights to access Indiana courts in violation of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 12, the court determined that the QSO statute did not violate § 12 because the possibility of paying up to $ 1,000 in attorney's fees after rejecting a more favorable offer than what was awarded at trial was not an impediment to a party's access to courts. The QSO statute also did not violate Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23 based upon the argument that tort litigants were treated differently from other civil litigants, because the preferential treatment, i.e. receipt of attorney's fees, was equally available to any offeror when a QSO was rejected and the offeree received a less favorable final judgment. The QSO statute permitted the award of fees to an attorney hired by the administrator's insurance company because the administrator incurred an obligation to pay her attorney's fees even if her insurance company ultimately paid them on her behalf, and payment to a nonparty was permitted.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.
