Green Tree Servicing, LLC v. Auditor & Treasurer


No. 34A02-0608-CV-679


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


868 N.E.2d 1; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1208



June 6, 2007, Decided  
June 6, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Lynn Murray, Judge. Cause No. 34C01-0504-PL-353.
Green Tree Servicing, LLC v. Random Antics, LLC, 869 N.E.2d 464, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1205 (Ind. Ct. App., June 6, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagee brought suit against defendants, a county treasurer and a county auditor, in which plaintiff argued that defendants were negligent in not notifying it of tax sale surplus funds before disbursing them and that plaintiff's due process rights had been violated. The Howard Circuit Court (Indiana) granted defendants' motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff argued that Ind. Code § 6-1.1-24-7(b) was unconstitutional because it did not designate mortgagees as claimants. The court stated that as it had held in a related case, plaintiff had received the notices provided for in Ind. Code §§ 6-1.1-25-4.5 and 6-1.1-25-4.6, but had taken no action to protect its interest in the property after it received the notices. Plaintiff could have learned additional information about the property by contacting the county, but had failed to do so. The tax sale statutes were not designed to protect those who received actual notice of a tax sale, but then did nothing else to protect their interest in the property. Thus, the court rejected the argument that Ind. Code § 6-1.1-24-7(b) was unconstitutional. Furthermore, defendants had followed the relevant statutory procedures in distributing the surplus funds. Thus, they were not negligent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.


 

506 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Green Tree Servicing, LLC v. Random Antics, LLC


No. 18A05-0605-CV-233


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


869 N.E.2d 464; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1205



June 6, 2007, Decided  
June 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Green Tree Servicing, LLC v. Auditor & Treasurer, 868 N.E.2d 1, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1208 (Ind. Ct. App., June 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Wayne J. Lennington, Judge. Cause No. 18C05-0203-PL-0025.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a quiet title action filed by the predecessor of appellee limited liability company (LLC), appellant mortgagee filed a counterclaim and third-party complaint against appellees, a county auditor and a treasurer. The Delaware Circuit Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment to the LLC with regard to possession of a mobile home. It granted summary judgment to the auditor and the treasurer with regard to tax sale proceeds. The mortgagee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagee lent the mortgagors funds to purchase a mobile home and a lot. The lot was later sold to the LLC's predecessor at a tax sale. The sale produced a surplus, of which the mortgagee was not notified. The surplus was paid to the mortgagors. The court first held that the mobile home was personal property under Ind. Code § 6-1.1-1-11(a)(4). Furthermore, because the mobile home could be removed from the real estate without material damage to the real estate, it was not a "building or fixture situated on the land" under Ind. Code § 6-1.1-1-15. Thus, it had not passed to the LLC through the tax deed, and the mortgagee was entitled to possession of the mobile home through its recorded lien on the certificate of title. Next, the court rejected the mortgagee's argument that it had been denied due process because it had not been given notice of the surplus. The mortgagee had been given the notices required by Ind. Code §§ 6-1.1-25-4.5 and 6-1.1-25-4.6 and had done nothing to protect its interest in the land after receiving the notices. As the auditor and the treasurer had followed the required statutory procedures in distributing the surplus, they were not negligent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for the LLC with regard to the possession of the mobile home. It affirmed the entry of summary judgment as to the notice regarding the distribution of the tax sale proceeds.


 

507 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



GPI at Danville Crossing, L.P. v. W. Cent. Conservancy Dist.


No. 32A01-0609-CV-395


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


867 N.E.2d 645; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1206



June 6, 2007, Decided  
June 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by GPI at Danville Crossing LP v. W. Cent. Conservancy Dist., 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1713 (Ind. Ct. App., July 23, 2007)
Transfer denied by GPI at Danville Crossing, L.P. v. W. Cent. Conservancy Dist., 2007 Ind. LEXIS 1012 (Ind., Nov. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jeffrey V. Boles, Judge. Cause No. 32C01-0305-PL-27.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the owner of an apartment complex, brought an action for injunctive relief against defendant conservancy district. Defendant filed an answer and counterclaim for unpaid sewer fees and attorney's fees. The Hendricks Circuit Court (Indiana) entered summary judgment in favor of defendant. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the time defendant adopted a resolution establishing higher rates for its sewer customers, plaintiff had been classified as a commercial customer. It continued to be billed as such until six months later, when it began to be billed as a residential customer. Defendant first argued that plaintiff had failed to exhaust its administrative remedies. The court stated that a user who objected to ratemaking normally had to follow the procedures set out in Ind. Code § 36-9-23-26.1. The statute, however, did not provide a means to challenge a classification that occurred well after a rate ordinance had been adopted. Thus, judicial review was not precluded here. Next, the classification of plaintiff as a residential user was not arbitrary or capricious. The resolution defined a residential user as including "all dwelling units." This term could only pertain to an apartment building. Furthermore, defendant had classified all apartment buildings as residential users. Finally, Ind. Code § 36-9-23-31 was clear and unambiguous. It did not provide for compounding penalties, but for a single penalty of 10 percent. As such, defendant was not authorized to compound the statutory penalty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment on the issue of the amount of fees and the total penalty plaintiff owed to defendant. It remanded for a hearing to determine the amount of delinquent fees owed, plus a 10 percent penalty on that total amount and reasonable attorney's fees. It affirmed the remainder of the trial court's decision.


 

508 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Bowles v. State


No. 49A04-0605-CR-238


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


867 N.E.2d 242; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1150



May 31, 2007, Decided  
May 31, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by Bowles v. State, 878 N.E.2d 207, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 654 (Ind., 2007)
Superseded by Bowles v. State, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 490 (Ind., June 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael Jensen, Commissioner. Cause No. 49G20-0303-FA-35854.
Bowles v. State, 820 N.E.2d 739, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 29 (Ind. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), defendant was convicted of Class A felony dealing in cocaine, Class C felony possession of cocaine, Class D felony possession of a controlled substance, and Class A misdemeanor possession of marijuana. The trial court had previously denied defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant told an officer that he bought cocaine from defendant. Police never made a controlled buy from defendant. An officer conducted surveillance of defendant's residence but did not note any evidence consistent with drug dealing. Eight months after receiving the tip, the officer collected trash that had been set out for delivery outside defendant's home. The trash contained marijuana seeds and stems and about 25 plastic bags with cocaine residue. The officer then obtained a search warrant for the home, which contained drugs and over $3,000 in cash. The court stated that the tip had not been corroborated and was stale, and there was no previous history of tips from the informant. Under these circumstances, any weight given to the tip as a declaration against penal interest was insufficient to provide the reasonable suspicion required for the "trash pull." The good faith exception to the exclusionary rule, however, applied. There was no evidence that the officer had acted with intentional, reckless, or even negligent disregard of defendant's rights under the United States or Indiana constitutions when he searched the garbage, then obtained a search warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

509 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Herron v. Anigbo


No. 45A03-0608-CV-378


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


866 N.E.2d 842; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1080



May 23, 2007, Decided  
May 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by Herron v. Anigbo, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 1057 (Ind., Nov. 13, 2008)
Superseded by Herron v. Anigbo, 897 N.E.2d 444, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 1051 (Ind., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Lorenzo Arredondo, Judge. The Honorable Christina J. Miller, Magistrate. Cause No. 45C01-0503-CT-400.
Herron v. Anigbo, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2744 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 19, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a medical malpractice action against defendant doctor. The doctor moved for summary judgment alleging that the complaint was not timely within Indiana's medical malpractice statute of limitations. The Lake Circuit Court (Indiana) granted the motion. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient, a quadriplegic, contended that summary judgment was inappropriate because Indiana's medical malpractice "occurrence-based" statute was unconstitutional as applied to the patient. The appellate court concluded that it was unconstitutional to apply the "occurrence-based" nature of Indiana's medical malpractice statute of limitations to the patient. It was not until another doctor informed the patient of the doctor's possible malpractice that the patient had sufficient knowledge to discover the malpractice. A previous diagnosis which included a complicated postsurgical list of problem was not sufficient to put the patient on notice that the patient had been the victim of medical malpractice. The appellate court further noted that the patient did not have a meaningful opportunity to bring his action between the discovery date and the running of the statute of limitations because of the extensive corrective procedures required and the fact that the patient was on oxygen and unable to be transported by car for a period of time following the procedures.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded to proceed with the patient's action.


 

510 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Foreman v. State


No. 49A02-0606-CR-470


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


865 N.E.2d 652; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 861



April 30, 2007, Decided  
April 30, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Foreman v. State, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1304 (Ind. Ct. App., June 14, 2007)
Transfer denied by Foreman v. State, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 679 (Ind., Aug. 23, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violating Ind. Code Ann. § 4-30-14-4 (2002), which made disclosure of confidential information relating to the lottery a class A felony. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion to dismiss. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal in which he argued that the penalty violated the proportionality clause, Ind. Const. art. I, § 16.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who worked for the lottery, was accused of disclosing confidential information to two lottery customers, who subsequently brought a winning ticket. At the time of the alleged acts, Ind. Code Ann. § 35-50-2-4 (2004) provided that the penalty for a Class A felony was a presumptive sentence of 30 years, with a minimum of 20 years and a maximum of 50 years. The court held that Ind. Code Ann. § 4-30-14-4 was not disproportionate. The crime was not merely an economic one, but involved the disclosure of confidential information, most likely by an employee of the lottery commission, which was statutorily charged with maintaining the integrity and dignity of the lottery and of the State. It had the potential to affect many citizens of Indiana. The state lottery served an important revenue-generating function that, in turn, benefitted the public welfare. Finally, because of the difficulty in detecting the crime of disclosing confidential information relating to the lottery, the crime justified a stricter penalty for the sake of deterrence. Moreover, a court was not allowed to set aside a legislative determination as to an appropriate penalty merely because it seemed too severe.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

511 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Meister v. State


No. 68A04-0604-CV-196


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


864 N.E.2d 1137; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 852



April 27, 2007, Decided  
April 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Meister v. State, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1318 (Ind. Ct. App., June 19, 2007)
Transfer denied by Meister v. State, 878 N.E.2d 214, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 905 (Ind., 2007)
Vacated by, Remanded by Meister v. Indiana, 129 S. Ct. 2155, 173 L. Ed. 2d 1152, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3393 (U.S., 2009)
Substituted opinion at, On reconsideration by Meister v. State, 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1245 (Ind. Ct. App., Aug. 31, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the State of Indiana and the City of Union City, brought a forfeiture action against defendant mother under Ind. Code Ann. § 34-24-1-4(a) (2003). Methamphetamine had been found in defendant's truck after her son was arrested in October 2003 for driving it on a suspended license. The Randolph Superior Court (Indiana) ordered the forfeiture of the truck. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first rejected defendant's argument the search of the truck was illegal. It was a search incident to a lawful custodial arrest and did not violate the Fourth Amendment. As for Ind. Const. art. I, § 11, the interior search of the truck was reasonable under the circumstances. Before searching the truck, an officer had found a hollowed-out pen that contained a powdery looking residue; the degree of intrusion upon defendant was minimal, as she was not present and the search took place in the evening; and the needs of law enforcement were a factor, as there was a possible concern with preserving any potential evidence relating to the discovery of the pen and the crime of possession of paraphernalia. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to support the forfeiture order. The son had a reputation for being involved with drugs; the son had been arrested three times for drug offenses in 2003 before his October 2003 arrest; the son lived with or on the same lot as defendant at the time of his arrests: defendant had posted bond for him once and said that she "might have known" of the other arrests; and the son was driving the car with defendant's permission in October 2003.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.


 

512 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Higgason v. Ind. Dep't of Corr.


No. 46A03-0610-CV-474


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


864 N.E.2d 1133; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 854



April 27, 2007, Decided  
April 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer dismissed by Higgason v. Ind. Dep't of Corr., 2007 Ind. LEXIS 1157 (Ind., Dec. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Paul J. Baldoni, Judge. Cause No. 46D03-0608-MI-275.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sued appellee department, alleging that the department's employees impeded the inmate's access to the courts. The LaPorte Superior Court (Indiana) dismissed the case pursuant to Ind. Code § 34-58-2-1. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In essence, the complaint asserted that alleged actions by certain of the department's officials, including the use of physical force, were in retaliation for the inmate's prolific amount of litigation. The inmate argued that the trial court erred in dismissing his complaint pursuant to Ind. Code § 34-58-2-1 because that code section was unconstitutional. The appellate court disagreed. Ind. Code § 34-58-2-1 did not infringe upon a fundamental right to seek redress in court, but instead placed conditions on a prisoner's ability to file a claim. Ind. Code § 34-58-2-1 did not unreasonably deny offenders the right of access to the courts, but offered a balance between an offender's right to bring a civil action and the heavy burden that those claims placed on the judicial system. The State had an interest in preserving valuable judicial and administrative resources. The inmate had filed more than 100 complaints in his 30-plus years of incarceration. Nothing in the record substantiated the inmate's claim that he was in immediate danger of serious bodily injury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jackson


No. 29A02-0610-CR-867


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


864 N.E.2d 431; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 771



April 20, 2007, Decided  
April 20, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Jackson, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1655 (Ind. Ct. App., July 17, 2007)
Transfer granted by, Vacated by State v. Jackson, 878 N.E.2d 214, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 885 (Ind., 2007)
Superseded by State v. Jackson, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 364 (Ind., May 13, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable J. Richard Campbell, Judge. Cause No. 29D04-0501-FD-434.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) with operating a vehicle after being adjudged an habitual traffic violator (OWHTV), in violation of Ind. Code § 9-30-10-16, a Class D felony. The State of Indiana appealed from the trial court's judgment of acquittal in favor defendant.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles (BMV) mailed a notice of its determination that defendant was a habitual traffic violator, under Ind. Code § 9-30-10-4, to the last address defendant gave the BMV. A police officer later arrested defendant for driving with a suspended license. Defendant admitted that he knew his license was suspended, but argued that he did not know it was suspended under Ind. Code § 9-30-10-5 for his status as a habitual traffic violator (HTV). He stated that he never received the notice from the BMV, and introduced evidence that when the BMV mailed the notice, he was living at a different location. Additionally, he never informed the BMV that his address had changed as required by Ind. Code § 9-24-13-4. On appeal, the court found that the OWHTV statute required that defendant have actual knowledge that his license was suspended because he was determined to be a HTV. The trial court also did not abuse its discretion in finding that defendant rebutted the presumption under Ind. Code § 9-30-10-16(b)(1) that he had knowledge of his HTV status, notwithstanding the fact that he failed to comply with the requirement that he notify the BMV of a change in address.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

514 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Broadhacker v. City of Indianapolis


No. 49A02-0511-CV-1084


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


864 N.E.2d 372; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 759



April 17, 2007, Decided  
April 17, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael D. Keele, Judge. Cause No. 49F12-0310-PL-3348.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a city and a development commission, brought an action against defendants, a club and its owners, to enjoin the club's operation under a city nuisance ordinance and to fine the owners. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs on four counts. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Undercover police officers visited the club and stated that they were interested in joining it. After completing a membership application and being given membership cards, the officers were given a tour of the club. During the tour, the officers saw various adults performing sex acts. Plaintiffs then brought the present action. Defendants argued that the club was a private club and therefore not subject to the city's nuisance ordinance. The court held that there was an issue of material fact as to whether the club was private. The club had no signage on its building or grounds to indicate to the public the nature of the activities that took place inside; it did not advertise in local newspapers or other local media; and it did not in any manner direct the general public to the club or invite the public inside. Its membership agreement was explicit in stating that the general public could not use the premises. There was no evidence that persons were able to enter the club without obtaining membership or that the club accepted every applicant. It was not necessary for a club to be owned by members who were directly involved in its operation for it to be private as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case.


 

515 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Kazmier v. State


No. 29A02-0605-CR-380


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


863 N.E.2d 912; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 647



April 4, 2007, Decided  
April 4, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable David Najjar, Magistrate. Cause No. 29D03-0507-CM-287.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for battery resulting in bodily injury by the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana). Specifically, defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction as the trial court did not believe the victim's account of events, and the trial court's domestic violence determination constituted judicial factfinding in violation of Blakely.


OVERVIEW: The victim told defendant, her husband of 23 years, that she wanted a divorce. A confrontation ensued at their home. During the argument, The victim stated that defendant forcibly poked her with his finger, climbed on top of her, placed his knee against her chest, and covered her mouth with his hand. The victim freed herself and fled. She suffered bruising on her body and a scratch on her face. While the trial court opined that the confrontation might have been mutual, it clearly stated that the victim's guilt was not for it to determine. The appellate court held the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of class A misdemeanor battery. Even though defendant was not convicted of domestic battery, the trial court still made a domestic violence determination because Ind. Code § 35-38-1-7.7 required it to do so if defendant committed a crime of domestic violence based upon the evidence introduced at trial. As defendant testified that the victim was his wife, for Blakely purposes, that testimony constituted an admission. Thus, the domestic violence determination did not implicate Blakely.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

516 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Smith v. Lake County


No. 45A03-0609-CV-430


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


863 N.E.2d 464; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 643



April 3, 2007, Decided  
April 3, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Smith v. Lake County, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1153 (Ind. Ct. App., May 30, 2007)
Transfer denied by Smith v. Lake County, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 701 (Ind., Aug. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jeffery Dywan, Special Judge. Cause No. 45D11-0208-PL-94.
Smith v. Lake County, 807 N.E.2d 53, 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 745 (Ind. Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bondsman brought an action against appellees, a county and a court clerk, in which appellant challenged the constitutionality of Indiana's bail scheme. Appellee county bar association was allowed to intervene as a defendant. The Lake Superior Court (Indiana) entered summary judgment in favor of the county and the clerk on the basis of res judicata. Appellant challenged the trial court's decision. Appellees sought sanctions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had brought a previous action challenging the constitutionality of the bail scheme in 1999. He argued that his claim involving Ind. Code § 35-33-8.5-4 had not been litigated in the prior action. The court stated that it was clear that appellant had alleged at some point in the former proceedings that appellees were not enforcing the statute and that he had litigated that matter in the context of his constitutional claims. The fact that the matter was not actually determined by the Indiana Supreme Court was inconsequential for res judicata purposes. Next, appellant argued that res judicata was inapplicable because the bar association had not been an intervenor in the prior case. The trial court, however, had entered summary judgment only as to the county and the clerk, both of whom were parties in the previous case. Thus, res judicata applied to them. Next, appellant had a well documented history of piecemeal attacks on Indiana's bail scheme. Viewed in that context, the appeal here could be characterized as harassing and vexatious under Ind. R. App. P. 66(E). Thus, the court would remand the case for a calculation of damages under Rule 66(E).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of summary judgment. It remanded the case for a calculation of damages to which appellees might be entitled under Ind. R. App. P. 66(E).

McVey v. State


No. 73A04-0610-CR-561


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


863 N.E.2d 434; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 575



March 30, 2007, Decided  
March 30, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by McVey v. State, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1135 (Ind. Ct. App., May 24, 2007)
Transfer denied by McVey v. State, 878 N.E.2d 206, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 610 (Ind., 2007)
Related proceeding at McVey v. State, 2016 Ind. App. LEXIS 217 (Ind. Ct. App., July 1, 2016)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of child molesting as a Class B felony, child molesting as a Class A felony, child molesting as a Class C felony, and incest. The trial court merged the incest count with the Class C molestation count and imposed concurrent sentences, and imposed twenty separate special probation conditions for adult sex offenders. The Shelby Circuit Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting statements made during a polygraph examination. The appellate court disagreed, holding that statements made during a polygraph test were not excludable per se as evidence. The appellate court also concluded that defendant voluntarily made the subject statements, noting that defendant was not in custody, signed a polygraph waiver, and was not coerced into making the statements. Defendant also asserted that the trial court improperly prohibited the introduction of the victim's prior sexual history. The appellate court disagreed, noting that the evidence defendant sought to introduce related to an incident that occurred after the alleged sexual abuse by defendant and thus occurred after the victim's medical examination in which a doctor found evidence consistent with sexual assault. The appellate court also found that the special probation conditions prohibiting defendant from possessing or viewing pornographic or sexually explicit materials, requiring defendant to report dating activity, and requiring defendant to report incidental contacts with persons under 18 were not stated with sufficient specificity.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for the trial court to clarify certain conditions of probation with greater specificity, specifically the conditions prohibiting defendant from possession or viewing pornographic or sexually explicit materials, requiring defendant to report dating activity, and requiring defendant to report incidental contacts with persons under the age of 18. The judgment of the trial court was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Foy


No. 68A05-0605-CR-235


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


862 N.E.2d 1219; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 520



March 19, 2007, Decided  
March 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by State v. Foy, 878 N.E.2d 204, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 563 (Ind., 2007)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Foy v. State, 2010 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 124 (Ind. Ct. App., Feb. 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE RANDOLPH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jay L. Toney, Judge. Cause No. 68C01-0404-MR-20.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Randolph Circuit Court (Indiana) granted defendant's motion to suppress where defendant was charged with the murder of his wife, police executed a search warrant in conducting their investigation of that murder, and the trial court granted the State's belated motion to file an interlocutory appeal. The State appealed the granting of the motion to suppress; defendant cross-appealed the issuance of the warrant and the belated motion rulings.


OVERVIEW: A woman placed a call to 911 and informed the operator that the victim, who appeared to be deceased, was in the residence. Defendant, the victim's husband, said that the victim had recently left the residence and that defendant soon found her floating face down in a nearby pond. Defendant then told the woman that he carried the victim into the residence and placed her on a couch. The woman told the 911 operator that the victim appeared to have bruises. A sheriff's investigator filed a probable cause affidavit in support of a search warrant. Based on the affidavit, a search warrant was issued that described places to be searched and included a search for "any and all trace evidence" in those locations. Thereafter, defendant was charged with the victim's murder. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress upon concluding that the search warrant was not sufficiently particular. It then granted the State's belated motion to file an interlocutory appeal. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court had good cause for granting the belated appeal, the warrant was supported by probable cause, and that the warrant was as particular as the circumstances would allow.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling granting the motion to suppress was reversed, the issuance of the search warrant was affirmed, and the ruling granting the State's belated motion to file an interlocutory appeal was affirmed. Too, the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr.


No. 49A02-0602-CV-99


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


861 N.E.2d 1271; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 354



February 28, 2007, Decided  
February 28, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr., 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 855 (Ind. Ct. App., Apr. 24, 2007)
Related proceeding at Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr., 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 2160 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Cynthia J. Ayers, Judge. Cause No. 49D04-0508-PL-31239.
Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr., 853 N.E.2d 127, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1672 (Ind. Ct. App., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sued defendant Indiana Department of Correction (IDOC), alleging the conditions in the punitive disciplinary segregation unit in which he was confined violated his rights under the Indiana Constitution. He filed a motion for a preliminary injunction, seeking transfer to a general housing unit. The Marion Superior Court denied the motion, as well as his subsequent motion to reconsider. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was placed in the disciplinary segregation unit due to numerous disciplinary violations, 25 of which he admitted committing. He alleged the conditions of his confinement in the unit violated his rights under Ind. Const. art. 1, §§ 11 and 23, because he was forced to remain in his cell 23 hours per day, was not allowed to possess hardback books or compact disc players, and was denied access to someone trained in the law. The appellate court noted that to the extent the inmate sought reassignment to the general population, it was without jurisdiction to consider that matter. The trial court was entitled to disbelieve his unsubstantiated claim that he was the victim of abusive treatment at the hands of IDOC personnel. He was not entitled to a preliminary injunction because he had an adequate legal remedy -- filing the instant lawsuit. IDOC's policies obviously did not impede his legal endeavors, as he had filed at least 14 appeals in less than two years. Placing him in the segregation unit did not violate Ind. Const. art. 1, §§ 11 and 23, because his confinement was not arbitrary, but was attributable to his numerous disciplinary violations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

520 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Doe v. Town of Plainfield


No. 32A01-0605-CV-188


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


860 N.E.2d 1204; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 231



February 6, 2007, Decided  
February 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Doe v. Town of Plainfield, 869 N.E.2d 456, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 321 (Ind., 2007)
Subsequent appeal at Doe v. Town of Plainfield, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 2102 (Ind. Ct. App., Sept. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert W. Freese, Judge. Cause No. 32D01-0602-PL-8.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a registered sex offender, filed an action against defendant town in which he challenged the constitutionality of an ordinance that prevented sexual offenders from using town parks. The Hendricks Superior Court (Indiana) granted the town's motion to reconsider its order allowing plaintiff to proceed anonymously. It certified its order for interlocutory appeal, of which the present court accepted jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The court first stated that Ind. Admin. R. 9(A), governing court records, and the corresponding commentary suggested a balancing approach instead of a strict interpretation of Ind. R. Trial P. 10 and 17, governing captions and the prosecution of a suit by a real party in interest. The court concluded that plaintiff's need for anonymity outweighed the presumption of openness in judicial proceedings. Plaintiff was challenging government action, a situation in which a plaintiff's interest in proceeding anonymously was considered particularly strong. Both plaintiff and his son had been subjected to threats and acts of violence. Defendant would not suffer prejudice because plaintiff had disclosed his real name to its counsel. Plaintiff's use of a fictitious name would not interfere with the public's right or ability to follow the proceedings. Finally, although plaintiff had previously written a letter to defendant's chief of police threatening legal action, nothing in this letter connected plaintiff to the present case except for what defendant's counsel knew. Thus, plaintiff had not waived his right to claim a need for anonymity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of defendant's motion to reconsider. It remanded the case for proceedings consistent with its opinion.


 

521 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



C.D.H. v. State


No. 71A04-0503-JV-125


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


860 N.E.2d 608; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 105



January 24, 2007, Decided  
January 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by C.D.H. v. State, 869 N.E.2d 455, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 232 (Ind., 2007)
Subsequent civil proceeding at CH v. Dvorak, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15702 (N.D. Ind., Feb. 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH PROBATE COURT. The Honorable Barbara Johnston, Magistrate. Cause No. 71J01-0407-JD-600.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile was adjudicated a juvenile delinquent based upon a finding by the St. Joseph Probate Court (Indiana) that defendant committed an act that if committed by an adult would be the criminal offense of child molesting, as a Class C felony. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 10-year-old boy, lived next door to the victim, a 10-year-old girl. The victim's stepfather was babysitting defendant and found defendant on top of the victim in her bed. The stepfather observed that defendant's underwear was in its normal place, but that defendant's jeans were pulled down around his knees. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had the requisite intent because both defendant and the victim were 10 years old when the act took place. The appellate court concluded that the record contained insufficient evidence to support a finding that defendant was older than the victim, a requirement of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3(b). The appellate court declined to find that testimony by the victim or the victim's stepfather that defendant was 11 years old established that defendant was older than the victim, particularly in light of the trial court's references to defendant as a 10 year old. The appellate court further concluded that the fact that the State alleged that the victim had the mental capacity of a five to six-year-old was irrelevant for purposes of the child molestation statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.


 

522 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Blake v. State


No. 49A02-0605-CR-369


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


860 N.E.2d 625; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 103



January 24, 2007, Decided  
January 24, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Tanya Walton Pratt, Judge. The Honorable Heather A. Welch, Commissioner. Cause No. 49G01-9105-CF-56103.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of robbery in 1992. In 2005, he received a gubernatorial pardon. Defendant then filed a motion to expunge the criminal records related to his conviction. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied his request. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court stated that it had previously held that in carrying out the executive mandate of a pardon, a trial court was required to clear a defendant's name by expunging the record of his conviction. Therefore, as the State conceded, the trial court had erred in not expunging the record of conviction. Defendant also sought, however, to have his arrest records expunged. Ind. Code § 35-38-5-1 applied to expunging arrest records either when no criminal charges had ever been filed or when the charges had been dropped. Accordingly, as defendant had been convicted, the statute did not apply. No Indiana statute set out the procedure for expunging records after a gubernatorial pardon. The majority of states, however, held that a pardon did not entitle a defendant to expunction of all criminal records related to the conviction. Moreover, it had also been held that where a pardon was conditional, there could not be expunction of all criminal records related thereto. Here, the pardon showed no conditions per se, but there was nothing indicating that it was intended to be unconditional. Accordingly, defendant was not entitled to have his arrest records expunged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's request to have his arrest records expunged. It reversed the denial of defendant's request to have his record of conviction expunged. It remanded the case to the trial court with directions to it to expunge defendant's record of conviction.

 

523 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Shuger v. State


No. 64A03-0509-CR-456


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


859 N.E.2d 1226; 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 23



January 17, 2007, Decided  
January 17, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Shuger v. State, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 233 (Ind., Apr. 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Julia M. Jent, Judge. Cause No. 64D03-0202-CM-1120 & 64D03-0202-CM-1121.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a trial in the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), defendants, who were opposed to hunting, were convicted of violating Ind. Code § 14-22-37-2(b) (1998), part of the Hunter Harassment Act. Defendants appealed. They argued that the Act violated the First Amendment and that the evidence was insufficient to support their conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court first held that the Act was content neutral. The Act was not a regulation of speech, but a regulation of the place and the manner where some speech could occur. Speech was limited only in that it could not interfere with a lawful hunt on lands designated for bow hunting. The Act had not been adopted because of disagreement with the content of speech but to maintain safe hunts and to help control overpopulation of deer. The State's interests in protecting hunters' and protestors' safety and in facilitating the taking of game for ecological reasons were unrelated to the content of protestors' speech. The Act was narrowly tailored to prevent speech only in hunting areas that was intended to disturb game and impede the lawful taking of such game. Next, the Act was not overbroad; it merely regulated the time, place, and manner in which communications could occur. Any purported vagueness was ameliorated by its scienter requirement. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions. From defendants' statements at public meetings and to others, there was overwhelming circumstantial evidence that they had the intent to scare deer away on the date in question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions.

Howell v. State


No. 82A01-0606-CR-241


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


859 N.E.2d 677; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2635



December 27, 2006, Decided  
December 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Howell v. State, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 181 (Ind., Mar. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert J. Pigman, Judge. Cause No. 82D02-0504-FA-281.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for neglect of a dependent as a class A felony and reckless homicide as a class C felony. Defendant pleaded guilty to reckless homicide as a class C felony, and the State dismissed the remaining charge. The Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to the maximum sentence of eight years in the Indiana Department of Correction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that each of the three aggravators used to enhance her sentence violated Blakely. The appellate court first concluded that the use of defendant's prior convictions did not violate Blakely. The use of the victim's age, while obviously clear to the trial court and the parties, was erroneous, however, because it was not proven and defendant did not admit that the child, who was seven weeks old, was less than 12 years of age. The fact that defendant, the victim's mother, was in a position of trust was proven though defendant's admission that the presentence investigation report was accurate, as it included language that defendant stated she fell asleep with her son, thereby proving she was the child's mother. The appellate court also found no error in the trial court's use of a prior traffic stop to disprove defendant's rehabilitation as a mitigating factor. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion by using defendant's criminal history as an aggravating factor because the prior misdemeanor convictions were not sufficiently weighty or similar to the current offense to justify enhancing defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

Windhorst v. State


No. 49A04-0605-CR-260


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


858 N.E.2d 676; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2632



December 22, 2006, Decided  
December 22, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Windhorst v. State, 869 N.E.2d 447, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 56 (Ind., 2007)
Affirmed in part and superseded in part by Windhorst v. State, 868 N.E.2d 504, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 489 (Ind., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with one count of felony child solicitation and two counts of felony dissemination of material harmful to minors. Defendant pleaded guilty to the child solicitation count in exchange for dismissal of the other counts, with a cap of two years on the executed portion of his sentence. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) imposed a sentence of four years, with two executed and two suspended to probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentence imposed was inappropriate in light of the nature of the offense and defendant's character. The appellate court disagreed with defendant's suggestion that the particulars of his offense were unremarkable and did not go beyond the inherent nature of the crime charged. Defendant also admitted his intention to bring an alcoholic beverage to his planned rendezvous with a person he believed to be a 14-year-old girl. The appellate court concluded that those facts went beyond the mere solicitation of a purported child by using a computer network. Moreover, those facts reflected unfavorably on defendant's character and significantly diminished the luster of his lack of prior convictions, employment history, military service, and cooperation with the police. In addition, defendant provided no independent evidence to support his claim of severe depression or to establish that his depression affected his ability to differentiate between right and wrong.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Cadle Co. II, Inc. v. Overton


No. 32A01-0601-CV-21


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


857 N.E.2d 433; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2459



November 30, 2006, Decided  
November 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Cadle Co. II v. Overton, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 267 (Ind., Apr. 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable David H. Coleman, Judge. Cause No. 32D02-0505-CC-66.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company filed an action in the Hendricks Superior Court (Indiana) against appellee car buyer seeking to collect the amount owed under a retail installment contract and security agreement that the buyer executed in Indiana in connection with the purchase of the car. The company appealed after the superior court granted the buyer's summary judgment motion and dismissed its suit with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The buyer returned the car shortly after he purchased it and refused to make any further payments under the contract. The company acquired the contract a year later. It filed its suit seven years after the buyer left Indiana. The buyer successfully argued in the superior court that the suit was time-barred. The company contended that the statute of limitations was tolled under Ind. Code § 34-11-4-1, due to the buyer's absence from the state. It also asserted that Ind. R. Trial P. 4.10, the procedural provision for providing service through the Indiana Secretary of State, was unconstitutional as applied because it allowed the buyer to receive constructive, rather than actual notice, of the suit. It The court noted that R. 4.10 was presumed to be constitutional. The company could not show that R. 4.10 was unconstitutional as applied because the buyer had not been served in the suit. Ind. Code § 34-11-4-1 did not apply because under Ind. R. Trial P. 4.4(B), the Secretary was deemed to be the buyer's agent for service of process. The suit was time-barred because the company had not attempted to serve either the buyer or the Secretary before the limitations period had expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

Brinkman v. Bueter


No. 29A02-0510-CV-980


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


856 N.E.2d 1231; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2377



November 20, 2006, Decided  
November 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by Brinkman v. Bueter, 869 N.E.2d 455, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 215 (Ind., 2007)
Superseded by Brinkman v. Bueter, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 42 (Ind., Jan. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Steven David, Special Judge. Cause No. 29D01-0410-CT-872.
Bueter v. Brinkman, 776 N.E.2d 910, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1695 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a husband and wife, sued appellees, physicians and a partnership, alleging, inter alia, negligence in failing to identify and treat the wife's preeclampsia and eclampsia. The Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) granted the physicians summary judgment on all but the claim that one physician and the partnership negligently counseled appellants as to the risk of eclampsia in future pregnancies. The parties cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court erred in granting the physicians summary judgment based on Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b) because appellants' ability to discover information supporting a malpractice claim with respective to preeclampsia prior to meeting with another physician in January 2000 was impracticable. Specifically, there was no evidence that a treating physician discussed preeclampsia with appellants during post-delivery or during visits after the wife was treated in the hospital for eclampsia. Thus, pursuant to Ind. Const. art. 1, §§ 12 and 23, the occurrence-based statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to appellants. The trial court also erred in granting summary judgment as to all claims pertaining to one physician where, following the medical review panel's decision, appellants submitted an expert affidavit that provided sufficient evidence to refute the medical review panel's opinion. However, the trial court did not err in denying summary judgment on the negligent counseling claim as appellants lacked sufficient information prior to their January 2000 discussions with another physician to know that they had been ill-advised as to the dangers of future pregnancies.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the denial of summary judgment on the negligent counseling claim but was otherwise reversed. The case was remanded.

Brown v. State


No. 49A05-0506-CR-321


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


856 N.E.2d 739; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2332



November 13, 2006, Decided  
November 13, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Mark Stoner, Judge. Cause No. 49F09-0407-FD-137884.
Brown v. State, 848 N.E.2d 699, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1067 (Ind. Ct. App., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which vacated defendant's convictions for identity deception based on double jeopardy and denied defendant's proportionality claim. The trial court entered judgment on three counts of criminal confinement. The court reversed the convictions for criminal confinement and for a judgment of conviction to be entered for identity deception verdicts. Defendant sought a rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a rehearing solely on the court's decision not to address his constitutional proportionality claim. The court agreed and granted a rehearing to respond to defendant's argument that the penalty for identity deception under Ind. Code § 35-43-5-3.5 was unconstitutionally disproportionate under Ind. Const. art. 1, § 16 as compared with the penalty for impersonation of a public servant under Ind. Code § 35-44-2-3. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's proportionality claim. Identity deception required that a person knowingly or intentionally obtained, possessed, transferred, or used the identifying information of another, and impersonating a public servant had no such requirement. Additionally, the two crimes might result in exactly the same penalty. The fact that no person was harmed or defrauded was not a defense in a prosecution for identity deception. The court concluded that the penalty was not so severe or entirely out of proportion so as to shock public sentiment and was not unconstitutionally disproportionate as compared with the penalty for impersonation of a public servant.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion for rehearing, affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's proportionality claim, and affirmed its previous opinion in all other respects. .

W.C.B. v. State


No. 49A02-0509-JV-871


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


855 N.E.2d 1057; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2219



November 1, 2006, Decided  
November 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by In re W.C.B., 2007 Ind. LEXIS 40 (Ind., Jan. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] INTERLOCUTORY APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Marilyn Moores, Judge. Cause No. 49D09-0502-JD-681.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent took an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied respondent's motion to dismiss a delinquency petition alleging that he had committed acts of child molesting that would have violated Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3 had they been committed by an adult.


OVERVIEW: Respondent contended that § 35-42-4-3 was inherently and unconstitutionally contradictory, was unconstitutionally vague, and violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. On review, the court affirmed, finding that the statute was constitutional as written and as applied to respondent. Under Ind. Code §§ 35-42-4-3, 35-42-4-9, the mere fact that respondent fell within the protected class of the statute did not protect him from being charged with child molesting of a younger child. The provisions did not prescribe a minimum age for the perpetrator of the offense. The court found that Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3 was not unconstitutionally vague under the First and Fourteenth Amendments because the language of the statute made it clear that it applied to a person who committed the requisite act. The statute did not encourage arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement because the provisions were satisfied if a person with the requisite intent engaged in defined sexual acts with a child under 14 years old. Finally, the court found that the statute did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause of Ind. Const. art. I., § 23, in that it applied equally to all persons, regardless of age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the motion to dismiss.

Planned Parenthood v. Carter


No. 49A02-0505-CV-469


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


854 N.E.2d 853; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1947



September 22, 2006, Decided  
September 22, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-0503-PL-9631.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Planned Parenthood of Indiana (PPI), challenged the order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied PPI's motion for a preliminary injunction against appellees, the Attorney General of the State of Indiana and the director of the Indiana Medicaid Fraud Control Unit (IMFCU), for the purpose of denying IMFCU unlimited access to the medical records of PPI's minor patients.


OVERVIEW: The IMFCU was investigating a complaint that PPI neglected 73 of its minor patients by allegedly failing to report child sexual abuse as required by Indiana law. The court held that enjoining IMFCU's investigation would not violate the separation of powers doctrine and that IMFCU was authorized by statute to conduct its investigation but that PPI had standing to raise a Fourteenth Amendment informational privacy claim on behalf of its minor patients. The court held that those patients had a limited constitutional right to privacy in their medical records and that the court was required to balance that right against IMFCU's interest in investigating complaints of patient neglect. The result of that inquiry resulted in the court concluding that PPI had demonstrated a reasonable likelihood of proving at trial that granting IMFCU's demand for unlimited access to the medical records of PPI's minor patients would violate the patients' constitutional privacy rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying PPI's motion for preliminary injunction and remanded the case to the trial court for it to immediately enter a preliminary injunction in favor of PPI against IMFCU's demand for unlimited access to the medical records. IMFCU was directed to immediately deliver any medical records in its possession to the trial court under seal, pending resolution of the trial on the merits of PPI's informational privacy claim.

Poling v. State


No. 27A02-0601-CR-32


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


853 N.E.2d 1270; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1938



September 20, 2006, Decided  
September 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Poling v. State, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2571 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 5, 2006)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Claim dismissed by Poling v. Martin, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 65993 (N.D. Ind., Sept. 4, 2007)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Poling v. State, 2007 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 892 (Ind. Ct. App., Nov. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE GRANT SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jeffrey D. Todd, Judge. Cause No. 27D01-0504-FC-65.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Grant Superior Court (Indiana), defendant was convicted of three counts of neglect of a dependent as a class C felony under Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4, three counts of neglect of a dependent as a class D felony, and intimidation as a class A misdemeanor. He appealed, arguing in part that § 35-46-1-4 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The court stated that the constitutional challenge would be more appropriately framed as an argument that the statute violated the Proportionality Clause, Ind. Const. art. I, § 16. It stated that under the statute, if a jury found a defendant guilty of cruel confinement of a dependent, the jury could characterize the crime as either a class C felony or a class D felony. Thus, one defendant could receive a harsher sentence than another for the same crime, and the statute was unconstitutional. Accordingly, defendant's class C felony convictions were to be reduced to class D convictions. Next, defendant argued that the trial court had violated the double jeopardy provision of Ind. Const. art. I, § 14 by convicting him of two counts of neglect as to each of three victims. The court stated that there was evidence that defendant hog-tied three victims with duct tape on at least one occasion, thus confining them pursuant to the first three counts, and that he locked each of them in a closet for an extended time on another, thus knowingly endangering their life or health pursuant to the last three counts. Thus, there was no double jeopardy violation under the "essential elements" test.


OUTCOME: The court reduced defendant's three class C felony convictions to class D felony convictions and remanded the case with instructions to the trial court to resentence defendant accordingly. It affirmed the remainder of the trial court's decision.

Battema v. Booth


No. 49A02-0512-CV-1185


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


853 N.E.2d 1014; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1860



September 13, 2006, Decided  
September 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Battema v. Booth, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 79 (Ind., Jan. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable S.K. Reid, Judge. Cause No. 49D13-0512-CT-6285.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured patient appealed the grant of a petition for preliminary determination of law by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of appellee doctors. The issue was whether the doctors' failure to file a copy of the proposed complaint cited in their petition was fatal to the trial court's judgment and whether the trial court erred in finding that the medical malpractice claim was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The treating doctor joined the dermatology practice of her father. Her mother worked as a nurse for the practice. The treating doctor performed a pulse laser procedure on the patient to remove a birthmark. The procedure left the patient with scarring and darkened pigmentation over an 80-square-inch area. Unbeknownst to the patient, the doctor was a narcotics addict. No one at the doctor's office ever informed the patient that the doctor had a history of addiction or that her license was suspended. The patient eventually discovered that the doctor's father and mother knew about her addiction issues. The doctors informed the trial court of the proposed complaint's filing date which was confirmed by the patient. The appellate court held the fact that the actual document was not before the trial court was not fatal to the doctors' petition. Also, it could not be concluded that the patient possessed enough information within two years after her laser procedure to lead a reasonably diligent person to conclude that malpractice had occurred. The patient presented enough evidence to at least raise a question of fact as to whether the doctrine of fraudulent concealment applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The matter was remanded.

Hecht v. State


No. 49A02-0511-CV-1104


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


853 N.E.2d 1007; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1805



September 8, 2006, Decided  
September 8, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hecht v. State, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2430 (Ind. Ct. App., Nov. 8, 2006)
Transfer denied by Hecht v. State, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 151 (Ind., Mar. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robyn Moberly, Judge. Cause No. 49D12-0506-PL-24005.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed a class action suit against defendants, the State of Indiana, the Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles (BMV), and its Commissioner, seeking to recover allegedly excessive excise taxes imposed by the BMV under Ind. Code § 6-6-5-6. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) ordered the case transferred to the tax court. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The BMV changed its policy and split vehicle registrations to expire either in the middle or at the end of the applicable registration month, depending on the alphabetical order of the vehicle owner's name. The taxpayer argued he was required to pay 16 more days' excise tax than other taxpayers, simply by virtue of the spelling of his last name. The appellate court held that motor vehicle excise taxes were "listed taxes" under Ind. Code § 6-8.1-1-1 and that, pursuant to Ind. Code § 6-6-5-2(b), they were subject to Ind. Code § 6-8.1. To exhaust his administrative remedies, a tax protester had to either pay the tax and request a refund under Ind. Code § 6-8.1-9-1, or protest the tax at the assessment level and receive a letter of findings denying the protest. Instead, the taxpayer sought a refund under Ind. Code § 6-6-5-7.7, which, pursuant to Ind. Code § 6-6-5-7.4, was applicable to only to vehicles registered in and taxed by another state. Therefore, he failed to exhaust his administrative remedies, thereby depriving the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions to the trial court to dismiss the taxpayer's case.

Jones v. Womacks


No. 49A02-0509-CV-853


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


852 N.E.2d 1035; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1679



August 24, 2006, Decided  
August 24, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jones v. Womack, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2625 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 8, 2006)
Transfer granted by, Vacated by, Appeal dismissed by Jones v. Womacks, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 771 (Ind., May 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM 11. The Honorable John Hanley, Judge. Cause No. 49D11-0412-PL-2358.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged the decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, a county auditor. The citizen brought a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief seeking to have Ind. Code § 6-1.1-20-3.2 declared unconstitutional. The case involved a petition/remonstrance proceeding wherein the citizen was precluded from joining in since he was a renter, not a property owner.


OVERVIEW: A plan was developed to renovate existing school facilities, funded by the school district incurring property tax-backed debt. Because the school district was planning to incur debt, notice was sent pursuant to § 6-1.1-20-3.2. Owners of real property in the school district timely filed the sufficient number of signatures pursuant to § 6-1.1-20-3.2 to initiate a petition and remonstrance process. The citizen claimed that § 6-1.1-20-3.2 violated the Equal Protection Clause in that it restricted the right to participate in the petition/remonstrance process to owners of real property living within the political subdivision. The court agreed with the county auditor that the case was moot but addressed the constitutionality claim raised by the citizen since it fit within the public interest exception. The court concluded that § 6-1.1-20-3.2 called for what amounted to a de facto election and that the State was not permitted to limit the right to participate to only those who own real property within the political subdivision without the showing of a compelling state interest, with such showing not having been made in the case.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court was in error to grant summary judgment in favor of the county auditor and that the statute at issue was unconstitutional. The court stayed the effectiveness of its holding until such time as the Indiana General Assembly was provided an opportunity to redraft the statute. If the General Assembly did not take action by the time it adjourned, the holding applied to every petition/remonstrance procedure.

 

535 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr.


No. 49A02-0601-CV-58


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA


853 N.E.2d 127; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1672



August 23, 2006, Decided  
August 23, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr., 861 N.E.2d 1271, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 354 (Ind. Ct. App., 2007)
Transfer granted by, Vacated by Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr., 2008 Ind. LEXIS 318 (Ind., Apr. 9, 2008)
Superseded by, Remanded by Smith v. Ind. Dep't of Corr., 883 N.E.2d 802, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 316 (Ind., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Cale J. Bradford, Judge. Cause No. 49D01-0511-CT-43581.
Smith v. Huckins, 850 N.E.2d 480, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1344 (Ind. Ct. App., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a pro se action against defendants, the Indiana Department of Correction and its employees. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) dismissed the complaint under Ind. Code § 34-58-2-1 as the inmate had filed at least three previous civil actions that had been dismissed. The inmate appealed. He argued that the statute violated Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 12 and 23, the Open Courts Clause, and the Privileges and Immunities Clause.


OVERVIEW: The inmate set up a makeshift hammock and refused to come down until defendants made some copies for him. He was forced down with chemical spray and pepper balls, after which he filed his complaint. The court first held that the statute did not facially violate the Open Courts Clause. Like a statute of limitations, Ind. Code § 34-58-2-1 limited the substantive right that gave rise to a claim. It did not infringe upon a fundamental right to seek redress in court and did not prevent the prosecution of any claim as long its conditions had been met. Furthermore, given the gravamen of the inmate's complaint, that he was injured after refusing to come down from his hammock, the statute was constitutional as applied to him. Next, § 34-58-2-1 did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause, given the State's interest in conserving judicial and administrative resources and the fact that offenders had been abusing these resources. Finally, the trial court was not required to find that the inmate was an abuser of litigation. The proper inquiry was whether three claims had been dismissed and whether the inmate was in immediate danger of serious bodily injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the complaint.

Membres v. State


No. 49A02-0511-CR-1065


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


851 N.E.2d 990; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1465



July 31, 2006, Decided  
July 31, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Membres v. State, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2104 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 13, 2006)
Transfer granted by, Vacated by Membres v. State, 869 N.E.2d 447, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 55 (Ind., 2007)
Superseded by Membres v. State, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 492 (Ind., June 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael S. Jensen, Magistrate. Cause No. 49G20-0510-MC-185560.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied appellant's motion to suppress granted the motion by appellee State for a turnover order pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-33-5-5(j), which would authorize the transfer of $57,000 in cash, jewelry, and the firearms, recovered during a search of appellant's home, to federal authorities.


OVERVIEW: The county deputy received information from a confidential informant who was "pretty sure" that defendant was selling marijuana from his home. The deputy stated that he had used this same informant 40 to 50 times in the past, although he could not recall more than three or four convictions arising from the informant's tips. The deputy searched defendant's garbage that was left out on the curb for pick up. After finding evidence of marijuana use in the garbage, the State obtained a search warrant for appellant's residence. During the search, the police found marijuana, cash, jewelry, and firearms. In the turnover proceeding, the lower court denied appellant's motion to suppress. Reversing, the court held that the deputy had not established a reasonable suspicion to search appellant's trash, as required by Ind. Const. art. I, § 11. The search was based upon non-specific information that did not set forth an impending crime. The information was not sufficient to support the articulable, individualized suspicion required to conduct a search of the trash. The good faith exception did not apply because of the inherent unreliability of the information.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court and remanded the matter.

 

537 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Twp. Bd. v. Elgin


No. 45A03-0510-CV-526


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


850 N.E.2d 1020; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1389



July 21, 2006, Decided  
July 21, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John R. Pera, Judge. Cause No. 45D10-0403-PL-36.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township board members appealed an order by the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) that denied their motion to correct error, which challenged the grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiff township trustee and denied summary judgment to them.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the township trustee began her term of office, the township board adopted two resolutions that, inter alia, required the trustee to obtain the board's approval for certain acquisitions by the trustee. The trustee entered into contracts for professional services without board approval and then filed a declaratory judgment action to determine the validity of the resolutions and her actions. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the Home Rule Act, Ind. Code § 36-1-3-1 et seq., did not confer upon the board the statutory authority to pre-approve the trustee's contracts and purchases. Pursuant to Ind. Code §§ 36-6-4-3, 36-1-4-7, the trustee had the power to receive and pay out township funds and to enter into contracts. The board could not unilaterally declare itself a "governmental unit" within the scope of the Act. Aside from encroaching upon the statutory role of the trustee, the resolutions would not promote efficiency. Consequently, the board did not demonstrate its entitlement to summary judgment, nor establish that the trial court erred by granting summary judgment to the trustee.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


 

538 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Green v. State


No. 15A01-0508-CR-373


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


850 N.E.2d 977; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1386



July 20, 2006, Decided  
July 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Green v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 1037 (Ind., Nov. 15, 2006)
Affirmed by Green v. State, 856 N.E.2d 703, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 1022 (Ind., 2006)
Decision reached on appeal by Green v. State, 876 N.E.2d 390, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2670 (Ind. Ct. App., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DEARBORN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable G. Michael Witte, Judge. Cause No. 15D01-0208-FA-004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Dearborn Superior Court (Indiana) to attempted robbery, conspiracy to commit robbery, burglary, and conspiracy to commit burglary. He was sentenced to an aggregate sentence of 150 years with forty-five years suspended. He appealed his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplice burglarized and assaulted two victims. The appellate court held an attempted robbery was part of a burglary conspiracy, so defendant's sentence could not exceed the maximum sentences for burglary and the episode comprised of attempted robbery and burglary conspiracy. He could not be convicted of conspiracy and attempt to commit one robbery. The victims' ages were a proper sentencing aggravator, as he admitted them. To the extent serious bodily injury was an attempted robbery element, it could not be a sentencing aggravator. It was not an element of burglary or conspiracy to commit burglary. His criminal history was not reliable. Lack of remorse could not be an aggravator, but the credibility of remorse could be observed in comment on the proceedings. Defendant's hearsay "admissions" to an officer were not aggravators. Facts the trial court stated about the crimes were not admissions, nor did a jury find them, but, on remand, the charging informations' facts, to which defendant admitted, could be considered to find if they were an aggravator. The trial court could find he took no responsibility and did not have to give his youth mitigating weight.


OUTCOME: Defendant's robbery conspiracy conviction was reversed, as was his sentence. His convictions for burglary, conspiracy to commit burglary, and attempted robbery were affirmed, and the matter was remanded to vacate the robbery conspiracy conviction and for resentencing. Aggravators and mitigators had to be properly considered upon resentencing, and the new sentence could not exceed an aggregate of 105 years.
