Ponciano v. State


No. 49A02-0507-CR-657


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


851 N.E.2d 305; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1347



July 13, 2006, Decided  
July 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corected July 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jane Magnus-Stinson, Judge. Cause No. 49G06-0407-FC-136377.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) convicting defendant of, inter alia, criminal recklessness, a Class C felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Ind. Code § 35-42-2-2(c)(3) violated the Proportionality Clause of Ind. Const. art. I, § 16, because it more severely punished the criminally reckless act of shooting from a vehicle than the criminally reckless discharge of a gun by a person who did not occupy a vehicle. The appellate court disagreed, noting that Ind. Code § 35-42-2-2 provided graduation of the criminal penalties on the basis that additional elements regarding the manner in which a person committed the offense steadily increased the chance that serious injury might arise. Defendant also argued that § 35-42-2-2 was unconstitutionally vague because it would allow a shooter to be charged with a Class C felony for shooting into an empty field because an empty field was conceivably a place where "people are likely to gather." The appellate court found no merit in defendant's argument as applied to the instant action, concluding that the victim's home, where defendant shot, was both a dwelling and a residence, and resort to the challenged language of § 35-42-2-2 was not necessary.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

540 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Hubbard v. State


No. 20A03-0509-CR-409


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


849 N.E.2d 1165; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1262



June 29, 2006, Decided  
June 29, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 07, 2006.
Transfer denied by Hubbard v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 765 (Ind., Aug. 31, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable David C. Bonfiglio, Judge. Cause No. 20D06-0403-FD-273.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her convictions from the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana) for two counts of Sexual Misconduct by a Service Provider, Class D felonies under Ind. Code § 35-44-1-5, the Sexual Misconduct Statute. The court addressed the issues of whether defendant's conduct violated the statute and whether the statute violated her right to due process under the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a civilian employee of a work release center, and while off-duty, she and an inmate had consensual sexual relations in a motel while the inmate was out of the facility on an 8-hour pass. Defendant contended that she was not a "service provider," that the inmate was not in "custody," and that the statute violated her due process and privacy protections. The court observed that while criminal statutes were to be construed narrowly, the statute was clear in its language that it covered defendant and the inmate, because even while out on a pass, he was subject to lawful detention. Therefore defendant was subject to the prohibitions of the statute. As to defendant's due process and privacy constitutional claims, the court held that the statute was presumed to be constitutional, and that because there was a legitimate State interest in not allowing favoritism or retaliation of inmates and in the orderly operation of institutions, the statute as applied to defendant was not unconstitutional. As to defendant's privacy interest claim, the court observed that only unreasonable intrusions on privacy were unconstitutional, and that the statute was not such an intrusion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

541 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Willard Library v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Pub. Library


No. 82A01-0510-CV-479


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


848 N.E.2d 1162; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1119



June 16, 2006, Decided  
June 16, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Carl Heldt, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-0509-PL-718.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant library challenged a judgment of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted appellee library's motion to dismiss. Appellant contended that the circuit court had erred in interpreting Ind. Code § 36-12-7-8 to allow appellee to calculate the amount of tax necessary to support appellant's budget, and that the levy was arbitrary, capricious, unreasonable, and contrary to law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a private donation library and appellee was a publicly funded library, and therefore a political subdivision. Appellant submitted a budget to appellee and appellee published a notice of a public meeting regarding budgeting. As a result of the meeting, appellee adopted a budget that was less than that sought by appellant and appellant filed its action, contending that appellee was required to pass the levy as submitted by appellant. On appeal, the court held that the rules of statutory construction prohibited interpretation of a statute that was not ambiguous, and that the constitutionality of the statute was to be presumed. The Private Donation Library Statute provided that the taxing authority must levy the tax, which, in turn, meant that it must "fix" the budget, tax rate, and tax levy. To hold otherwise would have allowed a private entity to levy a tax, which would have been unconstitutional. The court therefore reasoned that the legislature did not intend the tax levy to be a purely ministerial function and appellee had not acted improperly by reducing the proposed levy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wells v. Ind., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3817 (U.S., Apr. 2, 2007)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's pretrial motion to disqualify the jury panel was denied. A jury in the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana) found defendant guilty of Class C misdemeanor operating a vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) and Class B misdemeanor disorderly conduct. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the jury venire did not represent a fair cross-section of the community because it did not include any students attending the university, whose students defendant claimed comprised almost one-third of the county's population. The appellate court found no error, concluding that defendant failed to meet his burden of demonstrating that the university students constituted a distinctive group within the community for purposes of cross-section analysis. Const. art. 1, § 9, as it was not based on any political speech.

Richardson v. State


No. 24A04-0507-CR-378


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


848 N.E.2d 1097; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1099



June 12, 2006, Decided  
June 12, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Richardson v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 785 (Ind., Aug. 31, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable J. Steven Cox, Judge. Cause No. 24C01-0308-FD-542. Cause No. 24C01-0308-FD-543.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a husband and a wife, were charged with various drug offenses. They filed a motion to suppress the physical evidence seized from their property on the ground that a search of their trash violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 11. The Franklin Circuit Court (Indiana) denied the motion. Defendants filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: An officer received a telephone call from an anonymous person who said that the husband was manufacturing methamphetamine and growing marijuana at his home. The caller also said that the husband had a suspended driver's license, which the officer later verified. The police decided to ride along with the private trash service that picked up defendants' trash. After the trash was picked up, the police searched the trash, which contained evidence of drug activity. The court first held that the search was improper because the tip was insufficiently reliable to give rise to a reasonable suspicion. Although the tip provided the police with information about the driver's license, it lacked any information that would allow the police to corroborate the claim that illegal activity was afoot. The good faith exception of Ind. Code § 35-37-4-5, however, applied. At the time of the search, case law did not require articulable suspicion for trash searches. Under the reasonableness standard existing at the time, the search was proper. The trash service collected the trash on the day it normally did, and the trooper did not enter the property but merely supervised the collection process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the motion.

Brown v. State


No. 49A05-0506-CR-321


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


848 N.E.2d 699; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1067



June 7, 2006, Decided  
June 7, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 12, 2006.
Rehearing granted by Brown v. State, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2382 (Ind. Ct. App., Nov. 13, 2006)
On rehearing at, Reaffirmed Brown v. State, 856 N.E.2d 739, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2332 (Ind. Ct. App., 2006)
Superseded by Brown v. State, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 477 (Ind., June 22, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion for a mistrial and entered final judgments of conviction on three findings of guilt the jury made regarding criminal confinement charges the State filed against him. Prior to doing so, the trial court merged three findings of guilt on identity deception charges against him into the criminal confinement counts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with three counts of class D felony criminal confinement and three counts of class D felony identity deception after three separate incidents in which he called three different restaurants pretending to be a radio disc jockey from a specific radio station running a contest in which a restaurant employee would go to defendant's house where the employee would undress in return for winning a prize. At defendant's jury trial, one of the victims identified him by stating that defendant was wearing a "jail armband." The trial court denied defendant's mistrial motion. Defendant was convicted on all charges. Before entering the convictions, the trial court merged the identity deception into the criminal confinement counts and convicted defendant only on the criminal confinement counts. The trial court also imposed a $400 jury fee. On appeal, the appellate court found the mistrial motion was properly denied, the criminal confinement statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant, the identity deception statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to him, and the imposition of a $400 jury fee exceeded the trial court's $2 statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed defendant's judgments of conviction and sentence for criminal confinement, affirmed the guilty verdicts for identity deception, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

545 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Smith v. City of Hammond


No. 45A03-0509-CV-468


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


848 N.E.2d 333; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 995



May 30, 2006, Decided  
May 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 5, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Smith v. City of Hammond, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1536 (Ind. Ct. App., Aug. 3, 2006)
Transfer denied by Smith v. City of Hammond, 860 N.E.2d 601, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 1144 (Ind., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Gerald Svetanoff, Judge. Cause No. 45D04-0402-PL-7.
Smith v. City of Hammond, 388 F.3d 304, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 22789 (7th Cir. Ind., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a bail agent, a bail agency, and a bail agents' association, sued appellees, a city, the city clerk, a judge, and the chief of police, alleging, inter alia, that appellees denied licensed bail agents equal access to the city's jail for the purpose of providing bonds for detainees, in violation of Ind. Code § 27-10-3-18. The Lake Superior Court (Indiana) granted appellees summary judgment; appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants alleged the judge's cash-only bond policy denied them equal access to the jails in violation of § 27-10-3-18; that the bond statute, Ind. Code § 35-33-8-3.2(a)(2), violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 17; and that the clerk did not transfer forfeited money to the Indiana Common School Fund, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-33-8-7(2)(e). The appellate court held that as the granting of bail was within a judge's discretionary judicial actions, and there was no evidence he acted without jurisdiction, the trial court properly found the judge had judicial immunity from suits for money damages. This absolute judicial immunity extended to the clerk and chief of police who enforced the judge's policy. Appellants lacked standing to challenge the bond statute, as the protected class consisted of persons who were incarcerated and required to make bail, and the only harm to appellants was a possible reduction in demand for their business. Further, the bail agent failed to show how he fell within "extreme circumstances," which were required to grant him taxpayer standing. He also lacked standing as a taxpayer to complain about an alleged violation of § 35-33-8-7(2)(e).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court to determine whether sanctions against appellants and their counsel were warranted for filing repeated, meritless challenges to Indiana's bail scheme.

Cracker Barrel Old Country Store, Inc. v. Town of Plainfield


No. 32A01-0507-CV-296


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


848 N.E.2d 285; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 924



May 24, 2006, Decided  
May 24, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Cracker Barrel Old Country Store, Inc. v. Town of Plainfield, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 802 (Ind., Sept. 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Karen M. Love, Judge. Cause No. 32D03-0311-PL-48.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee town sued appellant restaurant in the Hendricks Superior Court (Indiana), alleging that the restaurant's sign had lost its status as a preexisting nonconforming use. The restaurant counterclaimed that the town's interpretation and enforcement of an ordinance was an unconstitutional taking. The court granted the town's motion for summary judgment, and ordered the restaurant to remove the sign from its property. The restaurant appealed.


OVERVIEW: When it opened for business, the restaurant received permission from a county planning and building department to construct a freestanding highway identification sign on its property. Sometime thereafter, an annexation occurred, whereby the restaurant came under the town's jurisdiction. After the town enacted Plainfield, Ind., Ordinance No. 21-97, it was subsequently determined that the restaurant's sign violated the provisions of the ordinance because it exceeded height and surface area limitations. However, the sign qualified as a preexisting, legally established, nonconforming structure as defined in the ordinance. The trial court ruled that the sign lost its status as a legally established nonconforming structure in accordance with the town's zoning ordinance when the restaurant had a contractor remove the sign from its pole to perform maintenance on the sign before replacing the sign. On appeal, the court found that, under the definitions in the ordinance, that the restaurant moved its sign and sign structure. Hence, under the plain language of the ordinance, that movement caused the restaurant's pole sign to lose its nonconforming use status.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Harmon


No. 09A02-0508-CR-789


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


846 N.E.2d 1056; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 821



May 9, 2006, Decided  
May 9, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 16, 2006.
Rehearing denied by State v. Harmon, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2572 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 6, 2006)
Transfer denied by State v. Harmon, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 112 (Ind., Feb. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CASS SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard Maughmer, Judge. Cause No. 09D02-0408-FA-6.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Cass Superior Court (Indiana) with dealing in methamphetamine and marijuana and possession of a controlled substance and paraphernalia. The trial court granted his motion to suppress evidence seized pursuant to a search warrant, and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant's tip led an officer to collect defendant's trash. The appellate court held it was error to suppress evidence seized from defendant's home pursuant to a warrant obtained on the basis of evidence seized from the trash. Each time an officer collected the trash, he did so in substantially the same manner as a trash collector, without trespassing onto defendant's property or causing a disturbance. When the officer searched the trash, a subsequent appellate decision was not available as precedent. Thus, the officer conducted the trash search in a manner consistent with applicable case law at the time. Thus, in searching defendant's home, the officer relied in good faith, under Ind. Code § 35-37-4-5, on a valid search warrant issued as a result of the discovery of items associated with illegal drug use in a reasonable search of defendant's trash.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

Anglemyer v. State


No. 43A05-0510-CR-590


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


845 N.E.2d 1087; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 662



April 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Transfer granted by, Vacated by Anglemyer v. State, 855 N.E.2d 1012, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 522 (Ind., 2006)
Superseded by Anglemyer v. State, 868 N.E.2d 482, 2007 Ind. LEXIS 490 (Ind., June 26, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a plea bargain, defendant pled guilty to Class B felony robbery and Class C felony battery. The Kosciusko Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced him to 10 years on the robbery conviction and six years on the battery conviction and ordered the sentences to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant beat and robbed a pizza deliveryman. The trial court considered defendant's criminal history and the seriousness of the offense as aggravating circumstances and his age as a mitigating circumstance. The appellate court noted that based on the sentencing ranges for the offenses, under Ind. Code § 35-38-1-7.1(d), the trial court was permitted to impose a 16-year sentence regardless of the aggravators and mitigators; therefore, its allegedly improper consideration of aggravating and mitigation circumstances could not result in a sentencing error. In view of the extensive discretion afforded to trial courts under Indiana's revised sentencing system, the appellate court urged them to continue issuing detailed sentencing statements pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-38-1-3(3) so as to facilitate appellate review of the appropriateness of sentences under Ind. R. App. P. 7(B). Defendant's Rule 7(B) claim that his 16-year sentence was not appropriate was waived because, by agreeing to a plea that allowed for an executed sentence "capped" at 16 years, he implicitly agreed that any total sentence up to 16 years was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Moyer v. Three Unnamed Physicians


No. 49A02-0504-CV-306


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


845 N.E.2d 252; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 640



April 13, 2006, Decided  
April 13, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable K. D. Mattingly, Master Commissioner. Cause No. 49D12-0404-CT-744.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured persons, one a former patient, sought review of the grant of summary judgment by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of appellees, two doctors who prescribed an acne drug which may have resulted in heart disease in the former patient.


OVERVIEW: The patient was prescribed acne medicine by the two doctors. The patient subsequently had to undergo open heart surgery due to heart disease. The patient later met an emergency room doctor who informed the patient that there was a possible link between his heart disease and the use of the acne medicine. The appellate court held that the patient did not have to know with certainty that malpractice caused his injury in order to trigger Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b). Even if there continued to be doubts about the cause of the heart disease or the possibility of malpractice, the information provided by the emergency room doctor was sufficient to require the patient to promptly seek additional medical and legal advice to assist them in deciding whether to seek legal recourse. Thus, the emergency room visit was the discovery date because it was on that date that the emergency room doctor informed the patient of a possible link between his heart disease and the acne medicine. The patient filed the complaint more than 18 months after that conversation. In the appellate court's view, that delay was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

550 of 1119 DOCUMENTS



Smyth v. Carter


No. 49A04-0504-CV-235


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


845 N.E.2d 219; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 636



April 12, 2006, Decided  
April 12, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Smyth v. Carter, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 755 (Ind., Aug. 24, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smyth v. Carter, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 1195 (U.S., Jan. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Theodore M. Sosin, Judge. Cause No. 49C01-0406-CT-001945.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shareholder sued defendant State, claiming that the State's retention of interest pursuant to the Indiana Unclaimed Property Act constituted an unconstitutional taking of private property without just compensation. The Marion Circuit Court, Indiana, dismissed the complaint. The shareholder appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State took custody of the shareholder's corporate stock and certain dividends that had been deemed abandoned. The State later sold the stock. The shareholder made a claim for the stock and any accruements. The State approved the claim and sent the shareholder the amount of the sale proceeds, plus the dividends that had been earned but not paid before it took custody of the stock, but it retained the interest that had accrued after the stock's liquidation. The shareholder claimed that Ind. Code § 32-34-1-31(c) required the State to pay him the value of his stock on the date it was delivered to the Indiana Attorney General. However, the court noted that the statute referred to the payment of a valid claim that was made for any securities in the possession of the Attorney General. The shareholder made his claim two years after the stock was sold. Thus, at the time the claim was made, the securities were not in the possession of the Attorney General. The court concluded that the retention of interest by the State pursuant to Ind. Code § 32-34-1-29 did not constitute an unconstitutional taking. Furthermore, the payment of the net proceeds of the sale of the stock was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Redding v. State


No. 48A05-0508-CR-495


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


844 N.E.2d 1067; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 597



April 4, 2006, Decided  
April 4, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 10, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Redding v. State, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1105 (Ind. Ct. App., June 6, 2006)
Decision reached on appeal by Redding v. State, 873 N.E.2d 206, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2163 (Ind. Ct. App., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MADISON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Fredrick R. Spencer, Judge. Cause No. 48C01-0309-FA-00270.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Madison Circuit Court (Indiana) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of child molesting, a class A felony. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim was five or six years old when she spent the night at the apartment of her mother's friend. Defendant also stayed there that evening. During the night, he allegedly forced the victim to submit to sexual intercourse. The victim did not tell anyone about the alleged incident until two or three years later. Defendant was then charged with child molesting. Defendant claimed at trial that he had not molested the victim, but instead that another person had done so on a prior occasion. A doctor testified about her examination of the victim. The doctor acknowledged that she could not determine what had caused the injury, when it happened, or who had caused the injury. Defendant was not allowed to cross-examine the doctor or the victim about the victim's alleged prior molestation. Defendant then made an offer of proof that the jury, through defendant's cross-examination, should hear evidence of the prior molestation. Defendant was convicted. On appeal, the appellate court found that defendant's Sixth Amendment right to cross-examination had been violated.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Palmer v. Gorecki


No. 46A03-0506-CV-286


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


844 N.E.2d 149; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 471



March 20, 2006, Decided  
March 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 22, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Palmer v. Gorecki, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1354 (Ind. Ct. App., July 12, 2006)
Transfer denied by Palmer v. Gorecki, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 1038 (Ind., Nov. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Walter P. Chapala, Special Judge. Cause No. 46D02-0404-MI-56.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a patient and his wife, challenged a summary judgment from the Laporte Superior Court (Indiana), which was in favor of appellee cardiologist on the patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The patient, and the wife through consortium claims, alleged personal injuries as a result of unnecessary antibiotic treatment following a purported misdiagnosis by the cardiologist. The cardiologist moved for summary judgment on the basis of the statute of limitations (SOL) at Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1. The superior court granted the motion and the patient appealed. The court found the act that commenced running the SOL was the cardiologist's misinterpretation of the echocardiogram, which occurred outside the limitations period. Moreover, under the discovery doctrine, the latest the patient should have discovered the injury was when he experienced symptoms from the unnecessary treatment, which also occurred outside the limitations period. The SOL was not tolled by fraudulent concealment or the continuing wrong doctrine as there was no evidence that the cardiologist concealed any fact and the cardiologist's continued treatment of the patient did not warrant application of the continuing wrong doctrine. He did not have a continuing duty regarding his misdiagnosis from years earlier. Finally, since the patient's main claim failed, the consortium claim also failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for the cardiologist.

Joint Noble-LeGrange County Drainage Bd. v. Acres, Inc.


No. 57A03-0507-CV-308


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


844 N.E.2d 134; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 466



March 16, 2006, Decided  
March 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As corrected March 20, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NOBLE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable James Heuer, Special Judge. Cause No. 57C01-0306-MI-035.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a joint county drainage board, established certain portions of a river and its tributary branches as a regulated drain. Appellees -- cities, towns, a corporation, an association, a conservancy district, and individuals -- sought review; appellee Director of the Indiana Department of Natural Resources (DNR) intervened. The Noble Circuit Court (Indiana) vacated the order and remanded the matter to the board, which appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board granted the request of county commissioners to create regulated drains running through two nature preserves and DNR wetland conservation areas. The trial court vacated the order because, inter alia, the commissioners failed to establish a particularized need to drain a specific public highway and therefore exceeded the scope of the authority granted to them under Ind. Code § 36-9-27-54(b)(2). The appellate court agreed; the commissioners' rote listing of nearly every road in the watershed was insufficient to comply with § 36-9-27-54(b)(2). And under Ind. Code § 14-31-1-7(8) of the Indiana Nature Preserves Act, Ind. Code § 14-31 et seq., as the board's order entailed modification or encroachment of the nature preserves, it was a "taking" of the preserves, and its failure to make a finding of necessity and to obtain the governor's approval rendered the order invalid. The order also imposed an implicit duty on the DNR to accept the placement and maintenance of a drain, in violation of Ind. Code § 36-1-3-8(a)(3). Under Ind. Code § 36-9-27-65, one of the cities and its conservancy district lacked standing to appeal as they waived their right to object to the board's order.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

554 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Gonser v. State


No. 44A05-0504-CR-210


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


843 N.E.2d 947; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 544



March 15, 2006, Decided  
March 15, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 16, 2006. As Corrected March 22, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAGRANGE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable J. Scott Vanderbeck, Judge. Cause No. 44C01-0311-FA-8.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with theft as a class D felony, possession of methamphetamine as a class A felony, and possession of a switchblade knife as a class B misdemeanor. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the methamphetamine, paraphernalia, and the switchblade knife. The Lagrange Circuit Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal pursuant to Ind. R. App. P. 14(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. The State argued that the automobile exception applied. The appellate court concluded that the State failed to meet its burden to show that the automobile exception applied because there was not sufficient evidence presented the location of the items seized. The court, sua sponte, also addressed the search incident to an arrest exception and the inventory exception and found that neither supported the State's position. The search of defendant's vehicle occurred after the vehicle was towed to the towing company's building; thus, the search was incident to an arrest exception was inapplicable because the search did not occur contemporaneously in both time and place with defendant's arrest. As for the inventory exception, the appellate court found that the State failed to meet its burden to show that the decision to impound the vehicle was in keeping with established departmental routine or regulation. As none of the aforementioned exceptions applied, the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying defendant's motion to suppress was denied. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

Turner v. State


No. 79A04-0507-CR-370


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


843 N.E.2d 937; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 407



March 10, 2006, Decided  
March 10, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 13, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Turner v. State, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1265 (Ind. Ct. App., June 22, 2006)
Appeal after remand at Turner v. State, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2764 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas H. Busch, Judge. Cause No. 79D02-0308-FA-25.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to dealing in cocaine. Before the sentencing hearing, defendant filed a motion to suppress and a motion to withdraw his guilty plea. The Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana) denied the motion to withdraw the guilty plea and sentenced defendant to 25 years, with five suspended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court should have granted his motion to withdraw his guilty plea because the trial court had not yet accepted the plea. The appellate court noted that such was not a dispositive factor in determining whether the trial court should have granted the motion. Defendant also maintained that the granting of his motion to withdraw his guilty plea was necessary to correct a manifest injustice because, after he entered his plea, the Indiana Supreme Court decided Litchfield, which defendant claimed established a credible defense that was not previously available. In Litchfield, it was decided that in order for officers to conduct a "trash pull," the officers must possess an articulable individualized suspicion, essentially the same as required for a Terry stop of an automobile, that the individual was engaged in illegal activity. The appellate court agreed that the trial court should have granted defendant's motion because he should have been given a fair opportunity to vindicate his Ind. Const. art. I, § 11 rights against unreasonable search and seizure as enunciated in Litchfield.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

556 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Mohamed v. State


No. 49A04-0503-CR-144


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


843 N.E.2d 553; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 367



March 8, 2006, Decided  
March 8, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael Jensen, Magistrate. Cause No. 49G20-0407-FB-130203.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance analog, Ind. Code § 35-48-1-9.3(a). Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: A police officer found a plant called khat in defendant's vehicle during a traffic stop. A crime lab chemist testified that the plant was widely cultivated in Arabia and parts of Africa and contained a naturally occurring stimulant compound called cathinone. Cathinone was not a listed drug under Ind. Code §§ 35-48-2-4 or 35-48-2-6. The chemist testified that cathinone was chemically similar to methcathinone, which was a controlled substance. The trial court found that because the effect of the two drugs were similar, cathinone was a controlled substance analog under Ind. Code § 35-48-1-9.3. Defendant argued that the conviction was not supported by sufficient evidence. The appellate court held that the State was required to prove that the analog substance had an effect on the central nervous system substantially similar to or greater than the effect of the controlled substance. The chemist testified that he had no knowledge of the comparative effects of cathinone and methcathinone. Thus, the appellate court held that the evidence was insufficient to establish beyond a reasonable doubt that khat was a controlled substance analog.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Beck v. City of Evansville


No. 82A04-0505-CV-248


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


842 N.E.2d 856; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 260



February 21, 2006, Decided  
February 21, 2006 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 27, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Beck v. City of Evansville, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 1108 (Ind. Ct. App., June 6, 2006)
Transfer denied by Beck v. City of Evansville, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 936 (Ind., Oct. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Wayne S. Trockman, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-0309-PL-4175.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners challenged a decision from the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city in a claim alleging negligence, nuisance, and inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: The litigation arose from extraordinary rainfall, and the flooding that resulted. The trial court granted summary judgment on the claims asserted by the homeowners, and they sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the trial court did not err by finding that the city was immune under Ind. Code § 34-13-3-1(7) from the negligence and nuisance claims. The appellate court determined that the city was performing a discretionary function when it commissioned and adopted a storm water plan. Notwithstanding governmental immunity, the homeowners failed to present any evidence to support their allegation that the city negligently operated and maintained the sewer system. Next, there was no taking of any actual physical part of the homeowners' real estate, nor were any important rights attached to the real estate taken. There was no permanent physical occupation of any definable part of the homeowners' property, and there was no transfer of a definable part of the homeowners' properties. To the contrary, the homeowners or tenants continued to live in their homes.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Castro v. State Office of Family & Children


No. 53A01-0507-JV-00308


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


842 N.E.2d 367; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 221



February 13, 2006, Decided  
February 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 20, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable E. Michael Hoff, Judge. Cause No. 53C01-0409-JT-00607.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed from an order of the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana) terminating his parental rights to his daughter.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the trial court erred when it terminated his parental rights to his daughter. The appellate court disagreed, noting, among other things, that the condition that resulted in the child's removal, the father's incarceration and consequent inability to provide her, was not likely to be remedied within a meaningful time. In addition, several factors weighed in favor of the trial court's conclusion that termination of the father's parental rights was in the child's best interests: the child was in need of stability and permanency, the child was doing well in her current placement, and there was no guarantee that the father would be a suitable parent once he was released or that he would even obtain custody. The father also argued that he was denied due process because certain actions taken did not satisfy statutory requirements. The appellate court found no violation. Among other things, earlier notification about the child's removal from the mother's home would have made no difference as the father could not have done anything to change the situation. Finally, the court concluded that Ind. Code § 31-35-2-4.5(a)(2)(B) does not violate the Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Swami, Inc. v. Lee


No. 02A05-0509-CV-516


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


841 N.E.2d 1173; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 169



February 8, 2006, Decided  
February 8, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Swami, Inc. v. Lee, 860 N.E.2d 583, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 599 (Ind., 2006)
Related proceeding at Retz v. Swami, Inc., 879 N.E.2d 1232, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 112 (Ind. Ct. App., 2008)
Related proceeding at Swammi, Inc. v. Shambaugh, Kast, Beck, Williams, LLP, 2012 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 826 (Ind. Ct. App., July 13, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas L. Ryan, Senior Judge. Cause No. 02C01-0208-PL-109.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Allen Circuit Court, Indiana, granted summary judgment in favor of intervenor, property buyer, on appellee tax auditor's petition requesting authority to issue a tax deed to the buyer for appellant corporation's property, and denied the corporation's cross-motion for summary judgment. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that the trial court erred when it refused to set aside the tax deed that was issued to the buyer. The appellate court found that Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-16 (Section 16) had to be strictly applied, as a person may defeat a tax title only by proving one of the seven defects. The corporation did not show or even assert the existence of any of the defects listed in Section 16. The corporation did not allege that any part of the tax sale process or issuance of the tax deed did not comply with the tax sale statutes. There was nothing for the trial court to correct. Because the corporation failed to inform the auditor's office of its change of address, it could not complain that it was misinformed about the status of taxes due or that it had no reason to know that the corporation's property was scheduled for tax sale. The corporation did not file an Ind. R. Trial P. 60(B) motion at the trial court challenging the tax deed. Because the corporation did not assert the Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 argument at the trial court, it waived it for review. The limitation in Section 16 of the ways to defeat a tax sale did not violate a substantive due process right.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Villas West II v. McGlothin


No. 34A02-0504-CV-370


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


841 N.E.2d 584; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 123



January 30, 2006, Decided  
January 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by, Vacated by Villas W. II of Willowridge Homeowners Ass'n v. McGlothin, 2008 Ind. LEXIS 408 (Ind., May 15, 2008)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a condominium association, challenged the judgment of the Howard Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of appellee, a personal representative of the estate of a deceased condominium unit owner. The unit owner had died during the proceedings and the personal representative became a party. The association had filed a complaint for injunctive relief against the unit owner, alleging a violation of a covenant against leasing her residence.


OVERVIEW: The association's declaration had a restrictive covenant that prohibited leasing of a residence. When the unit owner went into a nursing home, her residence was leased to others. The personal representative admitted that she was renting the residence but asserted that the covenant against leasing was unenforceable as a violation of the Fair Housing Act, 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 3601-3619. A bench trial was held and a judgment was entered in favor of the personal representative that held that the covenant against leasing violated the Fair Housing Act since it had a disparate impact on African Americans as the majority of the units in the association were owned by white persons and only two dwellings were owned by African Americans, with the unit owner's being one of those dwellings. The court upheld the judgment in favor of the personal representative, finding that the association provided a bona fide and legitimate justification for the covenant based on having a positive effect on property values but that the personal representative showed that less discriminatory alternatives existed, namely enforcing the maintenance of the properties and their value by the other declaration covenants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the personal representative.

Scott v. State


No. 71A03-0505-CR-240


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


840 N.E.2d 376; 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 26



January 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Scott v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 213 (Ind., Mar. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William H. Albright, Judge. Cause No. 71D03-0302-FA-10.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his 40-year sentence which was imposed by the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) after he pled guilty to class A felony robbery. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in sentencing him by relying upon an improper aggravating factor, the offense, and by failing to find that his guilty plea and his mental illness constituted mitigating factors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant picked out a random victim, had him give him his money, and then shot him in the chest. The trial court failed to articulate its reasoning, balancing, and evaluation of the aggravating factors. Defendant's criminal history revealed that upon reaching majority, he had a consistent and steady record of criminal activity. The fact that defendant was on probation for two offenses when he committed robbery was properly considered in enhancing his sentence. Defendant's arrest record and criminal history were aggravating factors. The circumstances of the robbery constituted an aggravating factor of high weight. Defendant was entitled to have some mitigating weight extended to his guilty plea, however, not significant weight. While he suffered from bipolar disorder, it appeared that he was capable of controlling his behavior, did not have significant limitations on his functioning, and failed to identify a nexus between his mental illness and the robbery. Thus, the failure to identify the proffered mitigating factors constituted error. However, the error was harmless because the record supported the finding of the two aggravating circumstances identified by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Johnson v. State


No. 49A02-0410-CR-901


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


856 N.E.2d 706; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2560



December 30, 2005, Decided  
December 30, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 20, 2006.
Ordered published by Johnson v. State, 856 N.E.2d 706, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 251 (Ind. Ct. App., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, CRIMINAL DIVISION 14. The Honorable David Shaheed, Judge. Cause No. 49G14-0403-FD-037027.
Johnson v. State, 841 N.E.2d 673, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2549 (Ind. Ct. App., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division 14 (Indiana), with possession of a controlled substance, battery on a law enforcement officer, resisting law enforcement, and possession of marijuana. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress, and defendant pursued an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: An officer saw defendant and others enter a car without a license plate. The appellate court held an investigatory stop began when the officer ordered defendant out of the car and told him to put his hands on the car's trunk, as a reasonable person would not have felt free to leave. Before the car was driven, which would have been a crime, the officer sought identification. He became suspicious when defendant could not produce a social security number. The officer had no reasonable suspicion of criminal activity. A claim that a crime was about to be committed was speculative and failed as defendant was not in the driver's seat. The officer said he thought defendant tried to hide his identity but did not say what criminal activity he thought had or was about to take place, so an inability to provide a social security number gave rise only to a hunch. The unlawful investigative stop preceded a search of defendant's person revealing contraband. But for the stop, the contraband would not have been seized. The intrusion violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 11.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

 

564 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Gary Cmty. Sch. Corp. v. Serv. Emples. Int'l


No. 45A03-0503-CV-114


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


839 N.E.2d 1191; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2436; 178 L.R.R.M. 3194



December 27, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Gary Cmty. Sch. Corp. v. SEIU, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 415 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE COUNTY DOMESTIC RELATIONS COURT. The Honorable James Danikolas, Judge. The Honorable Maria Luz Corona, Magistrate. Cause No. 45D03-0409-PL-00080 MLC.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a school corporation, challenged the order of the Lake County Domestic Relations Court (Indiana), which enjoined appellee employees from striking but also ordered the school to contribute money to a health and insurance trust fund for the employees in connection with the grant of the temporary restraining order and preliminary injunction. The school had brought suit seeking injunctive relief to prevent the employees from striking.


OVERVIEW: The insurance fund had informed the school that it was facing insolvency if additional contributions were not made by the school on behalf of the employees. The school never responded and the fund informed the parties that to preserve solvency, it was forced to cut benefits, including eliminating all benefits for dependents of the employees. In response to that drastic cut in benefits, the employees went on strike. The school brought suit and obtained the injunction it sought against the employees to stop the strike but it was also ordered to make the additional contributions. The school, on appeal, asserted that the trial court abused its discretion by imposing the condition that required them to pay a higher amount to the insurance fund than it had agreed to under contract. The court agreed that the trial court abused its discretion by imposing the condition that the school contribute a higher amount to the insurance fund. The court noted that the injunction enjoining the employees from committing illegal activity, namely striking, was proper but that the order requiring the school to contribute to the insurance fund was not a reasonable condition to maintain the status quo.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the trial court's grant of the injunction enjoining the employees from striking but reversed that part of the order that required the school to make an additional contribution to the insurance fund.

 

565 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Garneau v. Bush


No. 12A02-0502-CV-138


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


838 N.E.2d 1134; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2324



December 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Garneau v. Bush, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 318 (Ind., Apr. 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CLINTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Joseph W. Carey, Special Judge. Cause No. 12C01-0401-CT-29.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the judgment of the Clinton Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant doctor on the patient's claim for medical malpractice on the ground that the suit was filed outside the two-year statute of limitations set forth in Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b) (1999).


OVERVIEW: The doctor performed a hip replacement surgery on the patient and placed a certain type of prosthesis in the patient's hip. After the surgery, the patient continued to experience problems with her hip dislocating. Almost 20 months after the initial surgery, the doctor referred the patient to an orthopedic surgeon who removed the prosthesis and replaced it with a different type of prosthesis. The trial court found that the patient's suit was untimely filed and granted summary judgment to the doctor. On appeal, the court found that the patient should have known that she had a potential malpractice claim, at the absolute latest, when the prosthesis was replaced, which was more than two years before suit was brought; thus, the suit was filed outside the period set forth in § 34-18-7-1(b). However, the affidavit of a doctor submitted by the patient established a genuine issue of material fact as to whether the doctor's installation of an obsolete prosthesis, followed by treatment with prescription pain medication and failure to recommend revision after more than six months had passed since surgery, constituted a continuing wrong so as to have tolled the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

566 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Diversified Invs., LLC v. U.S. Bank, N.A.


No. 02A05-0503-CV-121


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


838 N.E.2d 536; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2272



December 7, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas L. Ryan, Judge. Cause No. 02C01-0208-PL-109.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant limited liability company (LLC) challenged a decision from the Allen Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied its motion for summary judgment to quiet title to property in a tax deed that the LLC held, which simultaneously granted appellee bank's cross-motion for summary judgment relief from the judgment ordering the tax deed, and which voided the tax deed.


OVERVIEW: In recording a mortgage assignment, a company listed a business address. It later changed its name, moved to a new address and, ultimately, merged into the bank. The county mortgage records were never corrected to reflect the name and address changes. The bank began a foreclosure action sometime after the LLC obtained a tax sale certificate for the property. The auditor sent tax deed notices to the address listed in the county records and signed mail receipts came back. After the auditor issued a tax deed, the LLC began a quiet title action, which was consolidated into the bank's foreclosure. The trial court voided the tax deed for inadequate notice. On appeal, the parties disputed whether notice to the address in the county records substantially complied with notice obligations under Ind. Code §§ 6-1.1-25-4.5, -4.6, and with due process. The court found the auditor was not obliged to search for addresses outside of the county records because the notices were not returned as undeliverable and mail receipts confirmed delivery. Also, the bank had an obligation during the two years it held a mortgage interest to ensure the county records of that interest were correct.


OUTCOME: The court reverse the denial of the LLC's summary judgment motion and the grant of relief from the tax deed to the bank. The court remanded for reinstatement of the tax deed and for a grant of summary judgment to quiet title in the LLC's favor.

Snover v. State


No. 20A03-0506-CR-254


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


837 N.E.2d 1042; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2191



November 30, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Snover v. State, 2015 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1228 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 30, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Terry C. Shewmaker, Judge. Cause No. 20C01-0311-FA-199.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence discovered in his home, a jury found defendant guilty of dealing in methamphetamine as a Class A felony and possession of marijuana as a Class D felony. The Elkhart Circuit Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to 35 years for dealing methamphetamine, to be served concurrent with a one-and-a-half year sentence for possession of marijuana. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A search warrant for defendant's house was issued based on information received from an informant who had been arrested for possession of drugs. The informant told police that defendant was his source and that he had additional drugs in his second floor bedroom at his house. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred by admitting evidence discovered during the search of his house. Defendant claimed that the affidavit in support of the search warrant did not contain probable cause to support the issuance of the search warrant because the police failed to corroborate the informant's hearsay or demonstrate its credibility. The appellate court agreed, noting that the informant's statement was not against his own penal interest as it did not implicate him in any additional crimes. The informant's knowledge of defendant's address and defendant's prior convictions could not support a finding of probable cause where police failed to corroborate such information. The court concluded, however, that the warrant was not so facially deficient that the executing officers could not reasonably presume it to be valid and thus, the evidence was admissible under the good faith exception.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Murphy v. State


No. 18A05-0411-CR-617


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


837 N.E.2d 591; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2176



November 22, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable John M. Feick, Judge. Cause No. 18C04-0309-FD-244.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Delaware Circuit Court (Indiana) entered a judgment that denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charge lodged against her of unauthorized receipt from a voter of a ballot prepared by the voter for voting, a Class D felony, after she filed that motion and claimed the relevant statute, Ind. Code § 3-14-2-16, was unconstitutional. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to a person's apartment and had the person sign a form to receive an absentee ballot in the mail. Defendant later returned to collect the ballot. The person gave defendant a sealed envelope containing the ballot and defendant put it in a mailbox to be delivered to the county clerk. Thereafter, defendant was charged under Ind. Code § 3-14-2-16 with unauthorized receipt from a voter of a ballot prepared by the voter for voting after defendant accepted a ballot in a sealed envelope from the absentee voter and placed it in the mailbox. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss that defendant filed in which defendant claimed that the statute under which she was charged was unconstitutional. On defendant's interlocutory appeal, the appellate court found that it did not need to address her constitutional challenge because she lacked standing to challenge the statute. It explained that she lacked standing because she was clearly not a person authorized under the statute to accept the ballot from the absentee voter. It also rejected her claim that she had not violated the statute because she had not touched the ballot, but only the sleeve holding the ballot.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

569 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Mueller v. State


No. 49A02-0503-CR-172


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


837 N.E.2d 198; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2165



November 16, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] INTERLOCUTORY APPEALS FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William Nelson, Judge. Cause Nos. 49F07-0403-CM-51572, 49F07-0410-CM-189904.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants appealed an order of the Marion Superior Court, Indiana, which refused to require the prosecutor to permit them to participate in a pretrial diversion program, notwithstanding their inability to pay the $ 230 in fees.


OVERVIEW: The dispositive issue on appeal was whether requiring payment of a fee as an absolute condition of participating in a pretrial diversion program violated the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The pretrial diversion statute, Ind. Code § 33-39-1-8, did not require the payment of fees as an absolute condition of participation in a pretrial diversion program. The instant court concluded that precluding defendants from participating in the pretrial diversion program based solely on their asserted inability to pay the $ 230 in fees violated their rights under the Fourteenth Amendment. The argument that the fees helped offset the costs of running the pretrial diversion program was not sufficient to establish a rational basis for distinguishing between the indigent and those able to pay the fees. The concept that the criminal justice system should be operated as far as reasonably possible without regard to a defendant's financial resources was axiomatic and beyond dispute. Allowing some defendants and not others to completely avoid prosecution and a potential criminal conviction, based solely on their abilities to pay certain fees, violated this fundamental principle.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Pinkston v. State


No. 49A02-0412-CR-1003


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


836 N.E.2d 453; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2036



October 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Pinkston v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 43 (Ind., Jan. 11, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Sheila Carlisle, Judge. Cause No. 49G03-0307-FA-118002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence after being found guilty of theft and auto theft, both Class D felonies, by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana). Defendant was sentenced to a four-year term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: In sentencing defendant, the trial court found three aggravating factors that it used to enhance his sentence, namely, his criminal history, consisting of only juvenile adjudications, that he was in need of correctional or rehabilitative treatment, and that imposition of a reduced or suspended sentence would have depreciated the seriousness of the offense. The court held that the trial court's reliance on each of those aggravating factors was improper and, therefore, defendant was entitled to the presumptive sentence. The court held that juvenile convictions were not proper considerations under Blakely/Apprendi and using defendant's prior juvenile adjudications, without having the matters submitted to a jury and proven beyond a reasonable doubt, violated defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, defendant's sentence for both his theft conviction and his auto theft conviction and held that he was entitled to the presumptive sentence of one and one-half years for both. The court also held that those sentences were to run concurrently for a total of one and one half years.

 

571 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Logan v. State


No. 46A03-0502-CR-50


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


836 N.E.2d 467; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 2032



October 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Logan v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 10 (Ind., Jan. 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Robert W. Gilmore, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 46C01-0307-FC-91.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with child exploitation and possession of child pornography. Defendant objected to the trial date and then filed a motion for discharge. The LaPorte Circuit Court (Indiana) ultimately denied defendant's motion to dismiss and motion for discharge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ind. Code § 35-42-4-4 was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. The appellate court found that it was overbroad but not substantially so. Ind. Code § 35-42-4-4(b) applied to not only visual child pornography but also written descriptions of child pornography. Similarly, Ind. Code § 35-42-4-4(c) applied to written descriptions of child pornography, virtual child pornography, and pornography showing youthful-looking adults. However, these arguably impermissible applications of the statute did not amount to more than a tiny fraction of the materials within the statute's reach. Defendant did not argue that the alleged child pornography found on his work computer was outside the permissible reach of § 35-42-4-4. Defendant did not show that regulation of child pornography was an abuse of his right to expression. Child pornography was not political expression and was not a "core" value. A rationality review was used to determine if the State could reasonably have concluded that, to the extent defendant's activity was expressive, it was an "abuse" of his right to expression. The State's interest in protecting child welfare easily passed this standard.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

572 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


No. 30A01-0502-CR-94


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


835 N.E.2d 1102; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1996



October 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Davis v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 4 (Ind., Jan. 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HANCOCK CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Richard D. Culver, Special Judge. Cause No. 30C01-0404-FB-29.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction and sentence of the Hancock Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant for class B felony robbery and class D felony resisting law enforcement. Defendant was sentenced to a 20-year term for the robbery conviction and a three-year term for the resisting law enforcement conviction, to have been served concurrently. .


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction and sentence arose from a bank robbery. Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court committed fundamental error when it failed to instruct the jury on the elements of resisting law enforcement. The court found no error, however, because the jury heard the charging instrument twice, and the prosecution referred to the elements in its closing argument. Sufficient evidence was found to have supported defendant's convictions, because it was not necessary that the State was to prove that defendant personally committed every act constituting the perpetration of the offenses since he aided another and was, therefore, chargeable as a principal. While driving away, defendant told his accomplice not to stop, which demonstrated his participation in the fleeing. The fact that defendant's BB gun was unloaded did not defeat his robbery conviction, because the gun was still considered a deadly weapon as the bank tellers testified that they were in fear, as did the customers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Sharp v. State


No. 18A02-0501-CR-30


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


835 N.E.2d 1079; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1993



October 25, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Sharp v. State, 2015 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1333 (Ind. Ct. App., Nov. 30, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Marianne Vorhees, Judge. Cause No. 18C01-0310-FA-15.
Sharp v. State, 807 N.E.2d 765, 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 795 (Ind. Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Delaware Circuit Court (Indiana) of two counts of burglary, two counts of criminal confinement, criminal deviate conduct, and child molesting. He appealed, alleging that his Fourth Amendment rights were violated when he was required to give a DNA sample, and that his counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: A masked man entered a 14-year-old girl's home at night and raped her. Several months later, a masked man entered another home at night and molested a seven-year-old girl. Later, defendant was charged with violating probation and was ordered to provide a DNA sample, which was sent to the State' DNA database. DNA retrieved from the two victims matched defendant's, and he was charged with those crimes. He then appealed his probation revocation, arguing that the statute requiring probationers to give DNA samples was unconstitutional; this claim failed because he had not raised it below. The trial court in the instant case, in ruling on defendant's motion to suppress the DNA tests, held that he was collaterally estopped from relitigating the constitutionality of the taking of his DNA. The appellate court agreed. Further, once the DNA sample was collected, defendant had no legitimate expectation of privacy in it. That defendant's probation revocation proceeding was untimely filed had no effect upon the validity of the order requiring him to provide a DNA sample; thus, his counsel was not ineffective for not objecting to the taking of defendant's DNA pursuant to that order.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Harris v. State


No. 43A05-0502-PC-80


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


836 N.E.2d 267; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1942



October 18, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Harris v. State, 841 N.E.2d 192, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 1145 (Ind., 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by Harris v. Ind. Parole Bd., 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41006 (N.D. Ind., June 4, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE KOSCIUSKO SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Rex L. Reed, Special Judge. Cause No. 43D01-9805-CF-44.
Harris v. State, 762 N.E.2d 163, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 131 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a denial, by the Kosciusko Superior Court (Indiana), of his request for post-conviction relief from revocation of his parole by respondent Indiana Parole Board. He challenged the constitutionality and validity of special conditions imposed under Ind. Code § 11-13-3-4, and also challenged the evidentiary basis for the revocation itself under Ind. Code § 11-13-3-10, as well as the constitutionality of the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, convicted of molesting a young boy, agreed to several special conditions when he was paroled, most prominently, that he would not use the Internet except in the course of employment by his entertainment company and that he would not solicit work that would bring him in contact with children. Parole revocation proceedings commenced after he contacted others in the entertainment business, sometimes using e-mail, about his ideas for projects that included several that required large casts of young boys, as well as one planned video that sounded like a justification for the events that had led to his original conviction. The court held, first, that the two challenged conditions were not violations of due process or freedom of association (which was quite limited for a parolee), although another condition was unconstitutionally vague. It did not matter that some of the evidence considered by the board was hearsay since the board could consider any relevant evidence. The revocation proceedings had met basic due process standards, and the inmate had not been deprived of his good time credits since they helped him to gain early parole, which he then lost through his own acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying relief.

State v. Sagalovsky


No. 45A05-0411-CR-637


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


836 N.E.2d 260; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1929



October 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by State v. Sagalovsky, 841 N.E.2d 192, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 1149 (Ind., Dec. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jesse M. Villalpando, Judge. Cause No. 45D12-0301-CM-102.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) with operating a vehicle while intoxicated and operating a vehicle while intoxicated endangering a person. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss, the State appealed, and, after dismissing the appeal, the appellate court reinstated it.


OVERVIEW: There was a 15-month delay between defendant's arrest and the filing of charges. The appellate court held the State's failure to serve its notice of appeal on defendant or counsel did not require the appeal's dismissal, as serving a notice of appeal was not jurisdictional, and the appellate court's procedural rules were only a means to achieve orderly and speedy justice. The delay in filing charges was within the 24-month statute of limitations period for a misdemeanor, in Ind. Code § 35-41-4-2(a)(2) (2004). As the interval between accusation and trial did not cross the threshold between ordinary and presumptively prejudicial delay, factors used to analyze prejudicial delay were not invoked. Defendant did not show the delay was unduly prejudicial, as he made no specific or concrete prejudice claims supported by evidence, so it was error to find his Sixth Amendment right to a speedy trial was violated. Neither the arresting officer nor any other government official intentionally delayed processing arrest paperwork upon which defendant's charges were based to gain a tactical advantage, so the State did not violate defendant's right to a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

Highler v. State


No. 02A03-0505-CR-203


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


834 N.E.2d 182; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1741

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Allen Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of rape as a Class B felony in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of raping a guest who had become intoxicated, vomited, and was taken to a room to sleep. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the jury selection system in the county did not deprive defendant of his right to a trial by a jury of his peers as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI and XIV because the county's computerized selection of potential jurors from voter registration lists and bureau of motor vehicle records satisfied Ind. The court found that the prosecutor's statement, which bore on the pastor's religious affiliation, was improper; however, the court found that the record showed that the primary motivation for the strike was not the pastor's religious affiliation; rather, it was his stated lack of respect and confidence in the criminal justice system.

Westray v. Wright


No. 45A04-0405-CV-275


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


834 N.E.2d 173; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1682



September 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer dismissed by Westray v. Wright, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 1075 (Ind., Nov. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert Pete, Judge. Cause No. 45D05-9712-CT-2394.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver and moving company appealed the judgment from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which, in plaintiffs' suit alleging that defendants acted with gross negligence and with willful, wanton, and conscious disregard for plaintiffs' safety, awarded plaintiffs compensatory damages and punitive damages. Plaintiffs cross-appealed, contending that the trial court improperly reduced the jury's punitive damage award.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, a mother, her husband, and her two year old son, filed suit against defendants after the mother, her son, aunt and mother-in-law were in a car accident. The evidence showed that the moving company driver took his attention off the road for several seconds and crashed into plaintiffs' car. The mother and son were injured, and the aunt and mother-in-law were killed. One of the deceased passengers was decapitated. A jury awarded compensatory damages of $ 1,145,000 and $ 15 million in punitive damages. In accordance with Ind. Code § 34-51-3-4, which provided that a punitive damage award could only be three times the amount of the compensatory damage award, the trial court reduced the punitive damages award to $ 3,435,000. On appeal, the court found that punitive damages were not appropriate, noting that the driver was not speeding and there was no evidence that he was drowsy or intoxicated. The court found also that there was simply no evidence to support an award of punitive damages against the moving company directly because plaintiffs failed to offer proof that the company consciously disregarded knowledge that the driver was a substantial danger to motorists.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award of punitive damages and remanded the cause.

Edwards v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT
