DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) for possession of marijuana in an amount greater than 30 grams.


OVERVIEW: Police received information indicating that defendant was dealing drugs. An officer saw four trash bags left near the street for collection. Officers picked up the bags, and upon examining them, found items believed to be evidence of drug crimes, including balled up plastic wrap which contained marijuana particles. The police obtained a search warrant based on this evidence, and found marijuana and other evidence in defendant's home. Defendant argued that the search warrant was not supported by probable cause. The appellate court initially found that the search of defendant's trash was constitutional. The trash was placed in a public area. The court held that the police made the search in good faith pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-37-4-5. The court further held that probable cause supported the search warrant pursuant to Ind. Const. art. 1, § XI and the Fourth Amendment. The fact that the officers did not have the material discovered in the trash tested to be sure it was marijuana was not fatal because the officer were able to identify the material based on their training and experience.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

579 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Villegas v. Silverman


No. 49A02-0410-CV-823


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


832 N.E.2d 598; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1451



August 12, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Villegas v. Silverman, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1990 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 21, 2005)
Transfer dismissed by Villegas v. Silverman, 855 N.E.2d 1000, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 209 (Ind., 2006)
Subsequent appeal at Silverman v. Villegas, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 2122 (Ind. Ct. App., Sept. 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Patrick L. McCarty, Judge. Cause No. 49D03-0208-PL-1448.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff undocumented aliens appealed from a summary judgment entered by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of defendant Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles (BMV) in the aliens' constitutional challenge to the BMV's enactment, without promulgation under the Indiana Administrative Rules and Procedures Act (ARPA), Ind. Code § 4-22-2 et seq., of a directive requiring driver license applicants to produce several types of identification.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had held that the aliens lacked standing to pursue their class action challenge. The court on review held that regardless of the type of identification document being sought, the aliens had standing because the social security documents they lacked should not have been used as a pretext for denying the documents where Indiana law actually provided an alternative procedure for applicants without social security numbers. Although the aliens challenged the new directive on constitutional grounds, the court did not reach that issue. As a rule of general application to the public at large, rather than an internal agency directive, the rule had to have been adopted after following the procedures set forth in ARPA, but the BMV had not followed those procedures. Therefore, even though Ind. Code § 9-24-9-2 empowered the agency to set driver license issuance requirements, its directive was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of the BMV and remanded the matter with directions to enter summary judgment in favor of the aliens.

State ex rel. Steinke v. Coriden


No. 49A04-0408-CV-435


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


831 N.E.2d 751; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1271



July 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by State ex rel. Steinke v. Coriden, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 972 (Ind., Oct. 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Patrick L. McCarty, Judge. Cause No. 49D03-0403-PL-507.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed the attorney's writ of mandate action against appellees, the members of the Workers' Compensation Board, for lack of standing as a member of the public, as an attorney, and under the public standing doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The attorney's practice included representing employees before the Board. The attorney filed a verified complaint for writs of mandate which alleged that members of the Board violated the Worker's Compensation Act, Ind. Code Ann. § 22-3-1-1 et seq. The attorney cited no specific incident or episode in which he was harmed by the alleged violations but instead filed his action on behalf of the residents of Indiana. The attorney claimed he was injured because attorneys such as himself lacked access to a full-time Board. The appellate court held that although the attorney presented a hypothetical scenario in which the Board's unavailability could or would delay payments due him, he alleged no incidents when the harm actually occurred. In the absence of a showing that he had suffered or would immediately suffer a direct injury, there was no standing under the general rule. The Board's alleged failure to fulfill its statutory obligations under the Act harmed an injured worker's attorney only incidentally, if at all. The nexus of harm had to be more direct to confer standing under the public interest exception. Therefore, he was not the proper party to seek an action of mandate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

581 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Gregory v. Manning (In re G.R.G.)


No. 32A05-0412-JV-649


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


829 N.E.2d 114; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1047



June 10, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jeffrey V. Boles, Judge. Cause No. 32C01-9907-JP-55.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the order of the Hendricks Circuit Court (Indiana), which computed the father's child support obligation, determined his child support arrearage and ordered payment of the same, as well as addressed various parenting issues with regard to the paternity action brought by appellee mother. The mother had filed a motion to modify the paternity order as to the father's parenting time and child support.


OVERVIEW: The parties were the parents of a child born out-of-wedlock. The mother had both legal and physical custody of the child, with parenting time to the father. The father contended on appeal that the trial court erred by including overtime hours in his income for purposes of calculating his child support obligation. The court upheld the trial court's calculation of the father's weekly gross income, which was based on the father's average income for a three-year period. The court found no error with regard to that portion of the trial court order requiring the father to satisfy the child support arrearage, because the trial court had the authority to order the support retroactive to any date after the filing of the petition to modify support. The court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's order requiring the parties to communicate only in writing, because the father had been making unannounced visits to the mother's home. Due to the father's fluctuating work schedule, the parenting time order was upheld, with the court advising the father that he was permitted to seek a modification if he was able to arrange a different work schedule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Doe v. Donahue

583 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Dommer v. Dommer


No. 64A03-0409-CV-410


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


829 N.E.2d 125; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1046



June 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Dommer v. Dommer, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 180 (Ind., Mar. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William E. Alexa, Judge. Cause No. 64D02-0401-CT-532.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a wife and her friends, appealed from a grant of summary judgment by the Porter Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of defendant husband in their action seeking to recover damages under 18 U.S.C.S. § 2520 and Ind. Code § 35-33.5-5-4 for secretly taping their conversations, the content of which the husband allegedly used during subsequent dissolution proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Both federal and Indiana wiretap statutes criminalizing unauthorized taping of private conversations provided civil remedies for victims. Although the husband and wife had originally acquired the taping equipment to investigate their suspicions regarding a son's possible involvement with drugs, the wife had no idea that the husband had later used the same equipment to record her conversations with family and friends. After noting that the trial court had inappropriately granted summary judgment without a request, it rejected, on the merits, the husband's argument that case law applying the federal statute had created an exception for interspousal recording when a spouse performed the actual interception, and that Indiana law had imported that exception. The only case that recognized such an exception had been overruled in one of the successor circuits to the one in which it had originally been decided, and had not been followed by other federal courts. Furthermore, Indiana's highest court had held that the Indiana statute was not to be interpreted as incorporating exemptions developed in federal case law. Thus, nothing precluded the wife and friends from seeking damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Moore v. State


No. 49A02-0405-CR-436


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


827 N.E.2d 631; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 887



May 23, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Moore v. State, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1503 (Ind. Ct. App., Aug. 12, 2005)
Transfer denied by Moore v. State, 841 N.E.2d 186, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 950 (Ind., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Moore v. State, 2015 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 535 (Ind. Ct. App., May 13, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G02-0308-MR-128884. The Honorable Robert Altice, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) convicting him of murder, criminal confinement, and arson, arguing that ballistics evidence admitted at trial was fruit of the poisonous tree, that the evidence was insufficient, and that imposition of consecutive sentences amounting to 120 years was a violation of his right to jury trial as well as unjust based on his lack of a past criminal record.


OVERVIEW: A couple of years before the murders of which defendant was convicted, the murder weapon had been temporarily seized by a policeman who had been trying to defuse a tense neighborhood situation. At that time, ballistics information had been recorded, and the information was retrieved and used in prosecuting defendant for brutally abducting and then murdering a male cross-dresser and a woman after what he perceived as their humiliation of him and for burning up the car that contained their bodies. The appeals court held that since there was no probable cause for retaining and recording information about the gun, for which there was a permit, the evidence admitted at trial was fruit of the poisonous tree. Since it was merely cumulative of other evidence, particularly the damaging testimony of an accomplice that was sufficient in itself, even this constitutional error was harmless. Although defendant had a clean criminal record, there was no impropriety in the imposition of long consecutive sentences, since they were well within the ranges of statutory maximums and the trial court had explicitly stated that the brutality of the crimes outweighed any possible factors in mitigation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Gaddis v. McCullough


No. 67A05-0409-CV-482


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


827 N.E.2d 66; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 791



May 10, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Gaddis v. McCullough, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 795 (Ind., Aug. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PUTNAM CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 67C01-0311-MI-341. The Honorable R. Paulette Stagg, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an election contest pursuant to Ind. Code § 3-12-8-2, plaintiff losing town council candidates (losers) sought review of a judgment of the Putnam Circuit Court (Indiana) denying their request for a new election based on alleged irregularities. Defendant winning candidates (winners) appealed the trial court's denial of their request for attorney's fees under Ind. Code § 34-52-1-1.


OVERVIEW: The small town's election officials decided it would be most efficient to have three precincts vote at the same site. The losers challenged that practice and also based their challenge on the fact that officials had combined the electronic voting results of all three precincts before reporting them. The appellate court held, first, that the plain language of Ind. Code § 3-10-7-22 actually authorized the combining of precinct voting sites in small communities and that there was no way either alleged irregularity could be said to have altered the outcome of the election or deprived voters of their right to vote. Furthermore, since the losers had never challenged the outcome of the election as invalid, their election contest could be called frivolous and in bad faith, justifying an award of trial attorney's fees. Furthermore, since the trial judge had warned the losers that they were running a risk of incurring sanctions if they appealed, appellate attorney's fees were also awarded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of election contest relief but held that the winners were entitled to awards of both trial and appellate attorney's fees. It remanded for determination of appropriate awards.

Young v. State


No. 49A04-0403-CR-143


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


826 N.E.2d 665; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 726



May 2, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Young v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 604 (Ind., July 13, 2005)
Superseded by, Remanded by Young v. State, 834 N.E.2d 1015, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 877 (Ind., Oct. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G06-0309-FB-151740. The Honorable Jane Magnus-Stinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) to six counts of Class B felony robbery and one count of Class C felony robbery. The trial court imposed an aggravated sentence of multiple sentences with a total aggregate sentence of 36 years with 12 suspended for an executed sentence of 24 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed at least seven businesses within the span of three weeks. Defendant or an accomplice was armed with a handgun in each of the robberies. Defendant was arrested and found to be in possession of an unlicensed handgun. Defendant argued that he was entitled to have a jury determine beyond a reasonable doubt whether aggravating circumstances existed before the trial court enhanced the sentences above the presumptive for each of the convictions and ordered some of the sentences to be served consecutively. On appeal, the court noted that it was the admission by defendant that defendant committed multiple violent crimes within a short period of time that the trial court relied upon in deciding that a slight aggravation of some of his sentences was warranted under Ind. Code § 35-38-1-7.1(b). Therefore, defendant's Sixth Amendment rights were not violated because the trial court enhanced defendant's sentence based only upon facts to which defendant admitted when he pleaded guilty. Finally, the court could not say that defendant's slightly aggravated sentence was inappropriate, under Ind. R. App. P. 7(B), in light of the nature of the offenses and the character of defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ankney v. State


No. 15A05-0404-CR-216


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


825 N.E.2d 965; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 670



April 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Ankney v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 610 (Ind., July 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DEARBORN CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 15C01-0202-FB-1. The Honorable James Humphrey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Dearborn Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him for attempted escape as a Class B felony, two counts of battery as Class C felonies, battery as a Class D felony, and resisting law enforcement (RLE) as a Class D felony, and which sentenced him to a total executed term of 15 years.


OVERVIEW: While being booked for public intoxication, defendant struck police officers in an attempt to escape. Despite psychological testing, he was deemed competent to stand trial. Evidence of an insanity defense was precluded because defendant did not timely submit a written notice of his intent to use the defense. On appeal, defendant argued evidence of his mental illness was improperly excluded, his convictions violated double jeopardy, and he was improperly sentenced. The court found that defendant never made a showing of good cause, as required by Ind. Code § 35-36-2-1, to justify his belated, oral motion to assert the insanity defense, so such evidence was properly excluded. However, since the jury likely used the same evidence to convict defendant of RLE on each of the batteries, and since the same injuries were used to enhance the attempted escape and battery convictions to felonies, double jeopardy under Ind. Const. art. I, § 14, was implicated. Finally, defendant's well-documented and long-standing significant mental illness was a factor that warranted mitigating weight. A reduction of his sentence was appropriate under Ind. R. App. P. 7(B).


OUTCOME: The court remanded with instructions to vacate the resisting law enforcement conviction and to reduce the battery convictions to Class A misdemeanors. The court further instructed that defendant be resentenced to the presumptive sentences on each conviction, to run concurrently, for a total term of 10 years.

Schrenger v. Caesars Ind.


No. 10A01-0408-CV-349


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


825 N.E.2d 879; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 611



April 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Schrenger v. Caesars Ind., 2005 Ind. LEXIS 687 (Ind., July 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CLARK CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Daniel F. Donahue, Judge. Cause No. 10C01-0309-CC-593.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff casino sued defendant debtor, seeking to recover money for credit extended to the debtor. The complaint sought actual damages in addition to treble damages pursuant to Ind. Code § 34-24-3-1. The Clark Circuit Court (Indiana) entered summary judgment in favor of the casino. The debtor appealed and the casino cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The casino sought to collect $ 25,000 in credit it had extended to the debtor. The debtor wrote 10 checks, each in the amount of $ 2,500, to repay the casino, but the checks were returned when presented for payment, noting that there were not sufficient funds to cover the checks. The trial court's judgment awarded actual damages, attorneys fees, and costs to the casino, but not treble damages. The debtor argued that Ind. Code § 34-16-1-1 (1998) prohibited the casino's action to collect the money it loaned to him. The appellate court disagreed. While Ind. Code § 4-33-9-15 (Supp. 2004) did not explicitly refer to Ind. Code § 34-16-1-1 (1998), it effectively created an exception for riverboat casino debts incurred legally pursuant to Ind. Code § 4-33-9-15 (Supp. 2004). Summary judgment in favor of the casino was proper. The decision to award damages in excess of actual damages pursuant to Ind. Code § 34-24-3-1 rested within the discretion of the trial court and there was no absolute entitlement to an award of treble damages. The casino was incorrect in arguing that it was entitled to treble damages.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kendall v. State


No. 49A02-0312-CR-1032


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


825 N.E.2d 439; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 607



April 18, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Kendall v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 563 (Ind., June 27, 2006)
Affirmed in part and superseded in part by Kendall v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 551 (Ind., June 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G20-0012-CF-221196. The Honorable William E. Young, Judge.
Hardister v. State, 821 N.E.2d 912, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 162 (Ind. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) of dealing in cocaine as a class A felony and resisting law enforcement. He was sentenced to 40 years in prison. He appealed his convictions and sentence. The State cross-appealed the trial court's failure to enter a judgment of conviction on the jury's guilty verdict for one count of possession of cocaine and a firearm, a class C felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to sever his trial from his brother's. The appellate court held his brother's testimony implicating him did not require two trials nor was defendant prejudiced as the brother could testify in a separate trial. No prima facie Batson violation was shown as the State left two African-Americans in the jury pool. A tip on drug manufacturing at defendant's home and the fact the home's occupants ran, instead of answering the door, when officers knocked, let an officer follow an unobstructed walk to the house's rear, and, when there, his observation, through an uncovered window, of a co-defendant discarding apparent cocaine was admissible. This provided exigent circumstances as to imminent evidence destruction, allowing immediate warrantless entry. A suppression ruling was permissibly modified before final judgment. The amount of cocaine and defendant's history allowed an enhanced 40-year sentence. Under statutory construction rules and common law, and not double jeopardy, defendant's possession of cocaine and a firearm conviction was properly vacated due to a conviction for dealing the same cocaine as the firearm crime was necessarily included in the dealing crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Montgomery v. Bd. of Trs.


No. 79A05-0411-CV-591


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


824 N.E.2d 1278; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 560; 95 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1271



April 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Montgomery v. Bd. of Tr., 841 N.E.2d 181, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 741 (Ind., 2005)
Superseded by Montgomery v. Bd. of Trs., 849 N.E.2d 1120, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 554 (Ind., June 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Randy Williams, Judge Pro Tempore. Cause No. 79D01-0305-CT-36.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee sought review of the dismissal of his case by the Tippeconoe Superior Court (Indiana) and the judgment on the pleadings for his age discrimination claim against appellee board of trustees of a university. The issue was whether the university was an "employer" for purposes of the Indiana Age Discrimination Act (IADA), Ind. Code §§ 22-9-2-1 to 22-9-2-11.


OVERVIEW: The former employee was employed by the university for 19 years when he was dismissed after declining involuntary retirement. The 58-year-old former employee filed a complaint for wrongful discharge under the IADA. Ind. Code § 22-9-2-1 provided that an "employer" for purposes of the IADA did not include a person or governmental entity which was subject to the federal Age Discrimination in Employment Act (ADEA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 621 et seq. Both parties agreed that the university was a governmental entity, but they disagreed whether the university was "subject to" the ADEA. Both parties seemed to agree that the university was an instrumentality of the state and therefore an "employer" under the ADEA. Both parties agreed that the Eleventh Amendment shielded the university, an instrumentality of the state, from private actions for monetary damages under the ADEA. The appellate court held that the university remained "subject to" the ADEA's enforcement provisions and was therefore not an "employer" for purposes of the IADA.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

592 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Jurich v. John Crane, Inc.


No. 45A05-0407-CV-385


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


824 N.E.2d 777; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 520; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,367



March 31, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Jurich v. John Crane, Inc., 2005 Ind. LEXIS 752 (Ind., Aug. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 45D01-9704-CT-345. The Honorable Jeffrey J. Dywan, Judge.
Jurich v. Garlock, Inc., 785 N.E.2d 1093, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 269 (Ind., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrators challenged a decision from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee corporations in an action brought under the Indiana Product Liability Act (PLA).


OVERVIEW: Two former employees died of mesothelioma as a result of exposure to asbestos. Thereafter, the administrators filed an action against the corporations under the PLA. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the corporations based on the ten-year statute of repose in Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1. The administrators then sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the statute of repose generally barred any suit brought more than ten years after the delivery of a product to the initial user or consumer. A claim under the PLA only accrued at the point where a physician who was reasonably experienced in making such a determination could have diagnosed an asbestos-related illness or disease. The evidence showed that the decedents were asymtomatic during the ten year period. As such, no reasonable physician would have performed invasive tests to see if the decedents were afflicted with the disease. The requirement of a manifested absestos-related disease or illness referred to a disease that could have been detected during a routine examination. Finally, the court determined that Ind. Const. art. 1, § 12 was not violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

593 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Horn v. Hendrickson


No. 82A05-0402-CV-83


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


824 N.E.2d 690; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 512



March 29, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Scott Bowers, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-0307-CT-3055.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the judgment of the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed her wrongful death claim under Ind. R. Trial P. 12(B)(6). The mother had brought suit against appellee driver.


OVERVIEW: The mother was six months pregnant and a passenger in a car when the vehicle was struck by the driver's car. The mother's unborn fetus died as a result of the collision. The trial court dismissed the mother's cause of action, because case law precedent had established that Indiana did not recognize a wrongful death claim for the death of an unborn child. The court agreed that Ind. Code § 34-23-2-1 did not provide relief for the death of an unborn fetus. The court strongly disagreed with the case law precedent and asserted that such precedent did not accurately interpret the term "child" under § 34-23-2-1. The court urged the Indiana Supreme Court to reconsider its prior case law decision to support a conclusion that the Indiana legislature intended to permit recovery not only for the death of children born alive but also for the death of viable unborn children. Within its holding addressing the inappropriateness of the case law precedent, the court held that § 34-23-2-1 violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 in that it discriminated against parents of children born alive and parents whose children were born dead. The court found no inherent difference between the two categories.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Burgess v. E.L.C. Elec., Inc.


No. 49A02-0406-CV-504


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


825 N.E.2d 1; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 429; 10 Wage & Hour Cas. 2d (BNA) 750



March 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at E.L.C. Elec., Inc. v. Ind. Dep't of Labor, 825 N.E.2d 16, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 479 (Ind. Ct. App., 2005)
Rehearing denied by Burgess v. E.L.C. Elec., Inc., 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 654 (Ind. Ct. App., Apr. 19, 2005)
Transfer denied by Burgess v. E.L.C. Elec., Inc., 2005 Ind. LEXIS 751 (Ind., Aug. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT ROOM NO. 3. The Honorable Patrick L. McCarty, Judge. Cause No. 49D03-0111-CP-001783.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment to appellee employer after concluding that appellant employees' claim for unpaid wages for work on three specific public works projects performed for the employer, filed pursuant to Indiana Common Construction Wage Act, Ind. Code § 5-16-7-1 et seq., was preempted by the federal Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974, 29 U.S.C.S. § 1001 et seq. The employees appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following an investigation, the state labor department sent written notice to the employees informing them that, pursuant to the Indiana Common Construction Wage Act, Ind. Code § 5-16-7-1 et seq. (CCWA), they had been underpaid for the work that they had performed while employed by the employer on three specific public works projects. In response, the employees filed suit against the employer seeking unpaid wages and related relief pursuant to the CCWA. The trial granted the employer's summary judgment motion after concluding that the employees' CCWA claims were preempted by the federal Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974, 29 U.S.C.S. § 1001 et seq. (ERISA). On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court erred in finding that ERISA preempted the CCWA. It so concluded because it found that ERISA was concerned with the administration of employee benefit plans and their beneficiaries, while the CCWA involved wage payments to employees working on public works projects. As a result, the appellate court found that ERISA did not preempt the CCWA in the present case because the employees' wage claims were not "connected with" nor did they "refer to" ERISA.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

595 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Moon v. State


No. 27A02-0408-CR-687


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


823 N.E.2d 710; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 388



March 9, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Moon v. State, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 824 (Ind. Ct. App., May 9, 2005)
Transfer denied by Moon v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 897 (Ind., Sept. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE GRANT SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 27D02-0401-FA-9. The Honorable Randall L. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Grant Superior Court (Indiana) for sexual misconduct with a minor. He also contested his sentence of 20 years. Defendant argued that he should not have had the burden to prove the defense that he reasonably believed that his victim was older than 15; that his sentencing enhancement violated the Sixth Amendment; and that the trial court should not have rejected a proffered mitigator.


OVERVIEW: The victim, age 13, was picked up by defendant, age 27, while hitchhiking to a middle school. Defendant convinced her to go to his house, watched a pornographic videotape with the victim, and eventually convinced her to have sexual intercourse with him. Defendant had sexual intercourse on a subsequent occasion after the victim turned 14. The appellate court held the trial court's instruction was a correct statement of law because the mistaken belief defense in Ind. Code § 35-42-4-9 did not negate an element of the crime. If believed, the defense only reduced defendant's culpability for acts he admitted that he committed. Defendant's knowledge of the victim's age was not an element of the crime. The trial court noted that defendant had five prior criminal convictions. Those convictions had already been proven beyond a reasonable doubt and were exempt from the Apprendi rule. That aggravator was sufficient to justify a sentence enhancement. The invalidity of any other aggravator had no effect on defendant's ultimate sentence. Thus, there was no Sixth Amendment violation. Defendant's proffered mitigator of facilitation was inapplicable as she could not consent to sexual contact.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

596 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Edwards v. State


No. 49A05-0401-CR-61


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


822 N.E.2d 1106; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 278



February 28, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G03-0102-CF-036584. CRIMINAL DIVISION 3. The Honorable Cale Bradford, Judge.
Edwards v. State, 773 N.E.2d 360, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1332 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) of attempted murder, a Class A felony pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-41-5-1 ( 2004) and Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1 (2004). The trial court imposed a 40-year sentence upon his conviction. Defendant appealed the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Ind. Code § 35-50-2-4 (2004) provided that a person who committed a Class A felony would be imprisoned for a fixed term of 30 years, with not more than 20 years added for aggravating circumstances or not more than 10 years subtracted for mitigating circumstances. In its sentencing statement, the trial court stated that probably the most significant aggravating factor was defendant's planning and preparation of the attack. Defendant asserted that in convicting him of attempted murder, the jury was required to find only that he attacked his victim with the specific intent to kill. Defendant thus argued that the degree of planning and preparation was a fact not found by the jury and, therefore, could not have been considered by the court as justification for imposing an enhanced sentence. On appeal, the court found that the facts of planning and preparation need not have been found by the jury for the jury to have found defendant guilty of attempted murder. Thus, under the Sixth Amendment, the trial court could not itself make the finding of planning and preparation and then rely upon such in sentencing defendant to an enhanced term of imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded to the trial court with instructions to either convene a jury for sentencing purposes or impose the presumptive sentence of 30 years for defendant's attempted murder conviction.

 

597 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


$ 100 v. State


No. 82A01-0310-CV-421


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


822 N.E.2d 1001; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 224



February 18, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by $ 100 v. State, 831 N.E.2d 748, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 505 (Ind., May 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 82C01-0305-MI-295. The Honorable David D. Kiely, Magistrate.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car owner challenged a judgment from the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which ordered the forfeiture of her car pursuant to Ind. Code § 34-24-1-1.


OVERVIEW: The owner was stopped for a traffic infraction after she left a suspected drug house. Marijuana and money were found in her car and an apparent drug ledger was found in her house. She pled guilty to one count of dealing drugs. The State's forfeiture complaints for the money and the car resulted in forfeiture of only the car. On appeal, the owner argued that insufficient evidence supported the forfeiture and that Ind. Code § 34-24-1-1 was unconstitutional for various reasons, including double jeopardy under U.S. Const. amend. V and as an excessive fine under U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The guilty plea was reliable evidence to show that the owner transported drugs for dealing, so forfeiture of the car was authorized by Ind. Code § 34-24-1-1(a)(1). Double jeopardy was not violated because the statute was civil. The value of the car was not grossly disproportionate to the gravity of the offense, so the forfeiture was not excessive. The remaining challenges under the takings clause, the bill of attainder clause, the common schools fund clause of Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 3, and 7, and the free administration of justice clause under Ind. Const. art. I, § 12, were waived and lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order requiring forfeiture of the owner's car.

 

598 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Abney v. State


No. 25A05-0407-CR-394


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


822 N.E.2d 260; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 214



February 15, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Abney v. State, 831 N.E.2d 743, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 345 (Ind., Apr. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FULTON SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 25D01-0307-FC-103. The Honorable Wayne E. Steele, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Indiana) convicting defendant of possessing material capable of causing bodily injury by an inmate, a Class C felony, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-44-3-9.5.


OVERVIEW: During a search of defendant's cell, a prison guard found an altered binder clip. In addition, the guard found a shank partially inserted into a vent in the wall of the cell. The guard described the shank as a hardened steel object with one end wrapped in a face cloth secured by a string. The other end was sharpened to a point. The steel portion of the item originated from the altered binder clip. The State presented sufficient evidence that defendant constructively possessed the shank. Defendant was the sole occupant of the cell and was capable of exercising dominion and control over all items discovered therein. Defendant intended to maintain dominion and control over the shank, as defendant admitted to the guard that he knew the shank was present, and the binder clip from which the shank was made was found amongst defendant's possessions. The State presented sufficient evidence that the device was intended to be used in a manner readily capable of causing bodily injury pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-44-3-9.5. The guard testified that the shank was hardened steel, sharpened to a point, that was capable of causing bodily injury to guards or other inmates.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

599 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Levy v. Newell


No. 45A03-0401-CV-37


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


822 N.E.2d 234; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 173



February 10, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Levy v. Newell, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 564 (Ind. Ct. App., Apr. 5, 2005)
Transfer denied by Levy v. Newell, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 655 (Ind., July 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 45C01-0305-CT-00099. The Honorable George S. Ivancevich, Civil Magistrate Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake Circuit Court (Indiana) entered a judgment that denied appellant doctor's motion for summary judgment after appellees, a patient and her spouse, filed a medical malpractice complaint alleging that the doctor negligently performed gall bladder surgery on the patient. The doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The doctor performed gall bladder surgery on the patient. She experienced problems and returned to the hospital three days later. Three days thereafter, a test revealed that she had a bile duct injury. She sought follow-up care at another hospital. Six months after the surgery, the patient and her spouse hired an attorney to pursue a medical malpractice claim. The attorney sent a letter to the doctor indicating that it was believed that the doctor had deviated from the standard of care. However, the patient and spouse did not filed a complaint with the trial court until more than one-month beyond the two-year anniversary of the surgery date. They filed a proposed complaint with the Indiana Department of Insurance the next day. The trial court denied the doctor's motion for summary judgment, alleging the complaint and proposed complaint were barred by the two-year statute of limitations. On appeal, the appellate court found that the patient and spouse's complaints were time-barred because they had a reasonable amount of time of at least 14 months, if not longer, in which to file their complaints from the time they should have discovered they had a medical malpractice claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court with instructions for it to grant the doctor's motion for summary judgment.

 

600 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Gray v. Daimler Chrysler Corp.


No. 93A02-0408-EX-673


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


821 N.E.2d 431; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 115



January 27, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Gray v. Daimler Chrysler Corp., 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 565 (Ind. Ct. App., Apr. 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA WORKERS COMPSENATION BOARD. The Honorable G. Terence Coriden, Chairman. Cause No. C-165594.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant, the wife of deceased worker, appealed the dismissal of her application for adjustment of claim by the Indiana Worker's Compensation Board.


OVERVIEW: Approximately 20 years after his last work at a foundry, the worker was diagnosed with silicosis, allegedly caused by the worker's exposure to silica dust at the foundry. A single board member found that the application for adjustment of claim to reflect the silicosis was barred by Ind. Code § 22-3-7-9(f)(1), which placed a three-year limit on silicosis claims, as the worker's disablement did not occur within three years after the last day of the last exposure to the silica dust. The wife argued that Ind. Code § 22-3-7-9(f)(1) violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, because it granted unequal privileges and immunities to the broad class of individuals who suffered from occupational diseases. The appellate court held that the inherent distinctions between individuals who suffered from the various types of occupational diseases justified the disparate treatment accorded to them in Ind. Code § 22-3-7-9(f). The appellate court further held that Ind. Code § 22-3-7-9 was not unconstitutional as applied, because the preferential treatment afforded under Ind. Code § 22-3-7-9(f)(1) was uniformly applicable and equally available to all persons similarly situated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
